Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Dog's Lick Purification: Ta'abbud vs. Ta'lil
Inter-madhhab dispute over dog's lick hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of ta'abbud vs. ta'lil to interpret the hadith on dog's lick and distinguish the resulting fiqh rulings across madhahib.

Core Idea
The same hadith yields different rulings because of a usul dispute: is the command a fixed ritual or a reasoned purification?

The dispute over washing a vessel after a dog's lick is not merely a fiqh detail; it reveals a fundamental usul division. The majority view the command as ta'abbudi (an act of worship with an imperceptible cause), requiring seven washes and soil. The Hanafis see it as mu'alla (reasoned), based on impurity removal, allowing flexibility in number. This lesson dissects the textual evidence and the usul principles that generate these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the textual evidence
Locate the hadith of Abu Hurayra and its variants cited in the passage. Note the core phrase: 'wash it seven times' and the addition of soil.
The hadith is transmitted through multiple chains with slight variations.
2
Classify the command (amr) in usul terms
Determine whether the imperative 'falyaghsilhu' indicates obligation (wujub) or recommendation, and whether the specification of number and soil is essential or incidental.
Hanafi usul: the default for amr is wujub, but the number may be interpreted as indicating repetition, not a fixed ritual.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle of ta'lil
Recognize that inanimate objects (like vessels) are not subject to pure acts of worship. The command must be for purification, and the number indicates severity, not a fixed ritual.
This uses istihsan to override the apparent meaning (zahir) of the hadith.
4
Compare the majority approach (ta'abbud)
Understand that the Shafi'i and other schools take the command literally as ta'abbudi, accepting the number and soil as essential parts of the ritual purification.
They argue that the wisdom (hikma) is imperceptible; thus the ruling is not open to rational analogy.
5
Derive the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
Note the concrete fiqh outcome: Hanafis wash two or three times without soil; Shafi'is require exactly seven with soil; Malikis view it as ta'abbudi but do not deem the water impure.
This illustrates how a single text produces varied rulings based on usul methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني/ الاختلاف في الْمَثْنِ
قولين
النموذج الثاني:
طهارة الإناء من ولوغ الكلب
۱۷۱
اختلف الفقهاء في عدد الغسلات التي يحصل بها التطهير من ولوغ الكلب عَلَى
الأول: ذهب جمهور الفقهاء إلى أنَّ الإناء يغسل سبع مرات من ولوغ الكلب، واختلفوا في نجاسة سؤره واشتراط التتريب، وهل الأمر بالغسل للنجاسة أم هُوَ للتعبد ؟ على النحو الآتي: ١ ذهب الشافعية إلى أن سؤر الكلب نجس، ويغسل الإناء سبعاً أولاهـن بالتراب والأمر بالغسل سبعاً للتعبد )
۲. ذهب مالك إلى أن الأمر بإراقة سؤر الكلب وغسل الإناء مِنْهُ، عبادة غَيْر مدركة العلة، والماء الذي ولغ فِيْهِ لَيْسَ بنجس، وَلَمْ يرَ إراقة ما سوى الماء في أشهر الروايات عَنْهُ .
قَالَ المازري: اختلف في غسل الإناء من ولوغ الكلب، هَلْ هُوَ تعبد أو سبع مرات : أَنَّهُ لَوْ كَانَتْ العلة لنجاسته ؟ فعندنا أنَّهُ تعبد، واحتج أصحابنا بتحديد غسله
النجاسة لكان المطلوب الإنقاء، وَقَدْ يحصل في مرة واحدة».
. ذهب الحنابلة إلى أن سؤر الكلب نجس، ويجب غسل الإناء مِنْهُ سبعاً،
إحداهن بالتراب من غَيْر تحديد لمكانها من السبع ٤ قَالَ الظاهرية سؤر الكلب طاهر، وغسل الإناء مِنْهُ سبعاً إذا ولغ فيه فرض، وما في الإناء من طعام وشراب وماء فَهُوَ طاهر . قَالَ الزيدية: التسبيع في غسل الإناء وتتريبه واجب، من غير تعيين لغسل
التراب، وهذا الحكم يخالف غسل سائر النجاسات؛ لحكمة مختصة غير معقولة). الثاني: ذهب الحنفية إلى نجاسة الكلب، وأن الإناء الَّذِي يلغ فِيْهِ يجب مرتين أو ثلاثاً كسائر النجاسات من غَيْر حدّ، وأن الأمر بالغسل للتنجيس لا للتعبد؛ لأن الجمادات لا يلحقها حكم العبادات، والزيادة في العدد والتعفير بالتراب دليل على غلظ النجاسة .
وبنحو هَذَا القول: قَالَ الليث بن سعد وسفيان الثوري؛ إلا أنهما قيدا الغسل بطمأنينة القلب إلى زوال النجاسة، سواء كَانَتْ الغسلات سبعاً أو أقل أو أكثر. وإليه ذهب الإمامية، فقالوا: يغسل الإناء من ولوغ الكلب ثلاثاً، تَكُون الثانية مِنْهَا بالتراب، وإن الكلب نجس لا يجوز التطهر بما أفضل، ويجب إراقته). واستدل القائلون بالمذهب الأول بما صح عن أبي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُوْلَ الله إذا شرب الكلب في إناء أحدكم فليغسله سبع مرات». وفي رِوَايَة: «إذا ولغ الكلب في إناء أحدكم فليرقه ثُمَّ يغسله سبع مرات. وفي رِوَايَة: «طهور إناء أحدكم إذا ولغ فيه الكلب أن يغسله سبع مرات أولاهن بالتراب». والحديث رَوَاهُ عَبد الرزاق والحميدي وأحمد والبخاري
Chapter Two: Differences in the Text (Matn)
Two Statements
Second Model:
Purification of a Vessel from the Licking of a Dog
171
The jurists differed regarding the number of washes by which purification from a dog's licking is achieved. First: The majority of jurists held that the vessel is washed seven times due to a dog's licking, and they differed regarding the impurity of its leftover water and the condition of using soil, and whether the command to wash is due to impurity or is an act of worship, as follows: 1. The Shafi'is held that the leftover water of a dog is impure, and the vessel is washed seven times, the first with soil, and the command to wash seven times is an act of worship. 2. Malik held that the command to pour away the dog's leftover water and wash the vessel from it is an act of worship whose cause is not perceived, and the water in which it licked is not impure, and he did not require pouring away other than water in the most famous narrations from him. Al-Maziri said: There is disagreement about washing the vessel from a dog's licking: is it an act of worship or [due to] impurity? In our view it is an act of worship, and our companions argued by specifying its washing: if it were due to impurity, the required thing would be removal, and that might be achieved in one wash. 3. The Hanbalis held that the leftover water of a dog is impure, and it is obligatory to wash the vessel from it seven times, one of them with soil, without specifying its place among the seven. 4. The Zahiris said: The leftover water of a dog is pure, and washing the vessel from it seven times when it has licked is obligatory, and whatever food, drink, and water are in the vessel are pure. 5. The Zaydis said: The sevenfold washing of the vessel and its soil application are obligatory, without specifying which wash is with soil, and this ruling differs from washing other impurities due to a specific wisdom not rationally understood. Second: The Hanafis held the impurity of the dog, and that the vessel in which it licks must be washed two or three times like other impurities without a fixed number, and that the command to wash is due to impurity, not as an act of worship, because inanimate objects are not subject to rulings of worship, and the increase in number and the use of soil indicate the severity of the impurity. Similar to this view was held by Layth ibn Sa'd and Sufyan al-Thawri, except that they conditioned the washing on the heart's reassurance of the removal of impurity, whether the washes are seven, fewer, or more. The Imamis also held this view, saying: The vessel is washed three times from a dog's licking, the second of which is with soil, and the dog is impure, and it is not permissible to purify with its leftover water, and it must be poured away. Those who held the first madhhab adduced as evidence what is authentic from Abu Hurayra: The Messenger of Allah said: 'If a dog drinks from the vessel of any one of you, let him wash it seven times.' And in a narration: 'If a dog licks the vessel of any one of you, let him pour it out, then wash it seven times.' And in a narration: 'The purification of the vessel of any one of you when a dog licks it is to wash it seven times, the first of them with soil.' The hadith was narrated by Abd al-Razzaq, al-Humaydi, Ahmad, and al-Bukhari.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed inter-madhhab dispute over the ruling on purifying a vessel after a dog has licked or drunk from it. The core textual evidence is the hadith narrated by Abu Hurayra with variations on the number of washes and the use of soil. The author first lists the positions of the majority schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali, Zahiri, Zaydi) that generally require seven washes—though they differ on the impurity status, the obligation of soil, and whether the command is ritual (ta'abbudi) or rational. The Hanafi position is then stated: the dog is impure, the vessel is washed two or three times without a fixed number, and the command is for purification (tanjis), not worship. This is because inanimate objects cannot be subject to pure acts of worship, and the extra washes and soil indicate the severity of impurity rather than a fixed ritual. The Hanafis also cite the opinions of Layth ibn Sa'd, Sufyan al-Thawri, and the Imamis. The passage shows how the same hadith can be interpreted differently based on usul principles: whether the command is considered ta'abbudi or mu'alla (reasoned), and whether the number is taken literally or as indicating multiplicity. The Hanafi view aligns with the concept of 'illah (effective cause) being the removal of impurity, which can be achieved without a fixed number.

Key Terms
ولوغ (walūgh): The act of a dog drinking by lapping with its tongue, leaving saliva in the vessel.
سؤر (su'r): The leftover water or food in a container after an animal (here, a dog) has drunk from it.
تتريب (tatrīb): Using soil or dust in the washing process, specifically as part of purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the command to wash the vessel after a dog's lick considered mu'alla (reasoned) rather than ta'abbudi (ritual)?
A) Because the dog is not impure in the Hanafi school
B) Because inanimate objects cannot be subject to acts of worship
C) Because the hadith is weak
D) Because the number seven is impossible to achieve

Key Takeaway
The dog's lick dispute illustrates how a single hadith yields different fiqh rulings based on the usul principle of ta'abbud vs. ta'lil.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
The Dispute Over Washing a Vessel After a Dog's Lick: A Usul al-Fiqh Analysis
Analyzing a usul dispute over purity rulings using hadith criticism and abrogation principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi and Jumhur positions on washing a vessel after a dog's lick, evaluate the strength of their respective hadith evidence using hadith criticism principles, and apply the concept of naskh to explain the Hanafi argument.

Core Idea
A narrator's own fatwa can be evidence of abrogation, but hadith critics may overrule it when the marfu' narration is authentic.

In this lesson, we examine a classic usul dispute arising from differing transmissions of the same Companion (Abu Hurairah). The Hanafis argue that the command to wash seven times may have been abrogated because the narrator himself gave a fatwa of three times. The Jumhur reject this, citing the weakness of the 'three times' narration and the strength of the 'seven times' one. This case illustrates how differences in matn and isnad lead to divergent rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its evidence
Identify what the Hanafis rule and which narrations they rely on, including the fatwa of Abu Hurairah.
2
State the Jumhur position and its evidence
Identify the majority view and the well-known hadith of seven times, first with dust.
3
Analyze the Hanafi argument for naskh
Examine how the Hanafis use the narrator's own fatwa to suggest that the ruling might have been abrogated.
4
Evaluate the Jumhur's response
Consider the critique of the weak narrator (al-Arzami) and the principle that the stronger chain prevails.
5
Determine the tarjih
Assess which side has preponderance according to hadith critics like al-Bayhaqi and Ibn Hajar.

غسله الترب، وهذا الحكم يخالف غسل سائر النجاسات؛ لحكمة مختصة غير معقولة). الثاني: ذهب الحنفية إلى نجاسة الكلب، وأن الإناء الذي يلغ فيه يجب مرتين أو ثلاثاً كسائر النجاسات من غير حد، وأن الأمر بالغسل للتنجيس لا للتعبد؛ لأن الجمادات لا يلحقها حكم العبادات، والزيادة في العدد والتعفير بالتراب دليل على غلظ النجاسة (٢). وبنحو هذا القول: قال الليث بن سعد وسفيان الثوري؛ إلا أنهما قيدا الغسل بطمأنينة القلب إلى زوال النجاسة، سواء كانت الغسلات سبعاً أو أقل أو أكثر (۳). وإليه ذهب الإمامية، فقالوا: يغسل الإناء من ولوغ الكلب ثلاثاً، تكون الثانية منها بالتراب، وإن الكلب نجس لا يجوز التطهر بما أفضل، ويجب إراقته). واستدل القائلون بالمذهب الأول بما صح عن أبي هريرة، قال: قال رسول الله - صلى الله عليه وسلم -: «إذا شرب الكلب في إناء أحدكم فليغسله سبع مرات». وفي رواية: «إذا ولغ الكلب في إناء أحدكم فليرقه ثم يغسله سبع مرات». وفي رواية: «طهور إناء أحدكم إذا ولغ فيه الكلب أن يغسله سبع مرات أولاهن بالتراب». والحديث رواه عبد الرزاق والحميدي وأحمد والبخاري ومسلم وأبو داود وابن ماجه والترمذي والنسائي وابن خزيمة. واعترض القائلون بالمذهب الثاني على استدلال الجمهور، بأن أبا هريرة - راوي الحديث - أفتى بخلاف ما روى، وهو الغسل ثلاثاً، فكان دليلاً على وجود النسخ. فروى الطحاوي والدارقطني من طريق عبد الملك بن أبي سليمان العرزمي، عن عطاء، عن أبي هريرة - في الإناء يلغ فيه الكلب أو الهر - قال: «يغسل ثلاث مرات». وأجاب الجمهور عن اعتراضهم بأن هذه الرواية تفرد بها العرزمي، ونص الحفاظ على خطئه فيها، ومخالفته للثقات. وروى الدارقطني من طريق حماد بن زيد عن أيوب عن محمد بن سيرين، عن أبي هريرة - في الكلب يلغ في الإناء - قال: «يراق ويغسل سبع مرات». قال الدارقطني: «صحيح موقوف». ومما يشد عضد هذه الرواية أنها موافقة للمرفوع، فظهر بها أن عبد الملك بن أبي سليمان العرزمي أخطأ فيها، وقد قال عنه الإمام أحمد: «ثقة يخطئ». وقال الحافظ ابن حجر: «صدوق له أوهام». وقد رجح الرواية الموافقة للحديث المرفوع البيهقي، فقال: «تفرد به عبد الملك من أصحاب عطاء، ثم من أصحاب أبي هريرة، والحفاظ الثقات أصحاب عطاء وأصحاب أبي هريرة يروون سبع مرات، وفي ذلك دلالة على خطأ رواية عبد الملك بن أبي سليمان، عن عطاء عن أبي هريرة في الثلاث، وعبد الملك لا يقبل منه ما يخالف الثقات لمخالفته أهل الحفظ والثقة في بعض روايته تركه شعبة بن الحجاج، ولم يحتج به البخاري في صحيحه. وقال ابن حجر: ورواية من روى عنه موافقة فتياه لروايته أرجح من رواية من
Chapter Two: Disagreement in the Text (Matn). ... its washing with dust, and this ruling differs from washing other impurities due to a specific wisdom that is not rationally understood. Second: The Hanafis held the impurity of the dog, and that a vessel from which it laps must be washed two or three times like other impurities without a fixed number, and that the command to wash is for purification not for worship, because inanimate objects are not subject to worship rulings, and the increase in number and dusting indicates the severity of impurity. Similar to this view was said by Layth ibn Sa'd and Sufyan al-Thawri, except that they conditioned washing on tranquility of heart that impurity is removed, whether the washings are seven, fewer, or more. The Imamiyyah (Shia) also held this, saying: wash the vessel from a dog's lick three times, the second of which with dust, and the dog is impure, and one may not purify with water left over, and it must be thrown away. The proponents of the first view (Jumhur) adduced what is authentically reported from Abu Hurairah, who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'If a dog drinks from a vessel of one of you, let him wash it seven times.' In another narration: 'If a dog laps in a vessel of one of you, let him pour it out, then wash it seven times.' In another narration: 'The purification of a vessel of one of you when a dog laps in it is to wash it seven times, the first of them with dust.' This hadith was narrated by Abd al-Razzaq, al-Humaydi, Ahmad, al-Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Khuzaymah. The proponents of the second view objected to the Jumhur's evidence, saying that Abu Hurairah - the narrator of the hadith - gave a fatwa contrary to what he narrated, namely washing three times, which indicates abrogation (naskh). Al-Tahawi and al-Daraqutni narrated via Abd al-Malik ibn Abi Sulayman al-Arzami, from Ata', from Abu Hurairah, concerning a vessel in which a dog or cat laps, he said: 'Wash it three times.' The Jumhur responded to their objection that this narration is unique to al-Arzami, and the hadith scholars have stated his error in it and his contradiction of trustworthy narrators. Al-Daraqutni narrated via Hammad ibn Zayd from Ayyub from Muhammad ibn Sirin from Abu Hurairah concerning a dog lapping in a vessel, he said: 'Pour it out and wash it seven times.' Al-Daraqutni said: 'Authentic, but mawquf (stopped at the Companion).' This narration is strengthened by its agreement with the marfu' (raised to the Prophet) version, showing that Abd al-Malik ibn Abi Sulayman al-Arzami was mistaken in it. Imam Ahmad said about him: 'Trustworthy but makes mistakes.' Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: 'Truthful but has errors.' Al-Bayhaqi gave preponderance to the narration that agrees with the marfu' hadith, saying: 'Abd al-Malik alone among Ata''s students reported it, and among Abu Hurairah's students, and the trustworthy, precise scholars from Ata' and Abu Hurairah's students report seven times. This indicates the error of Abd al-Malik ibn Abi Sulayman's narration from Ata' from Abu Hurairah of three times. Abd al-Malik is not accepted when he contradicts trustworthy transmitters; due to his inconsistency, Shu'bah ibn al-Hajjaj abandoned him and al-Bukhari did not use him as evidence in his Sahih.' Ibn Hajar said: 'The narration of one whose fatwa agrees with his narration is more preponderant than the narration of one...'
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage presents a classic usul al-fiqh dispute arising from differences in hadith transmission (matn and isnad). The issue is how many times to wash a vessel after a dog laps from it. The Jumhur (majority, including Shafi'is and Hanbalis) hold seven times, first with dust, based on the well-known hadith from Abu Hurairah. The Hanafis hold two or three times without a fixed number, arguing that the command is for purification, not worship, and that the increase in number merely indicates severity of impurity. They also point to a fatwa from Abu Hurairah himself ordering three washes, suggesting the hadith might be abrogated. The Jumhur respond by criticizing the chain of the 'three times' narration, deeming it weak due to a problematic transmitter (Abd al-Malik al-Arzami), and they produce a mawquf narration from Abu Hurairah ordering seven times. Al-Bayhaqi and Ibn Hajar side with the Jumhur, emphasizing that the majority of trustworthy narrators transmitted seven times. The passage illustrates how hadith criticism (jarh wa ta'dil) and the principle of tarjih (preponderance) are used to resolve ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
نجاسة (najāsa): Legal impurity requiring specific purification
غسل (ghusl): Washing with water to remove impurity
ولوغ (wulūgh): Lapping or drinking by an animal
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a previous ruling by a later one
متن (matn): The text of a hadith, as opposed to its chain

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A hadith narrated by Abd al-Razzaq ordering three times
B) Abu Hurairah's own fatwa of three times, suggesting abrogation
C) Qiyas with cat's saliva
D) The opinion of al-Shafi'i

Key Takeaway
Differences in hadith transmission can lead to divergent rulings, and resolving them requires careful hadith criticism and weighing of evidence.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Evaluating Conflicting Narrations: The Dog Lapping Dispute
Examining a hadith matn dispute and narrator criticism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi principles of jarh wa ta'dil and tarjih to evaluate conflicting hadith narrations and derive the stronger ruling.

Core Idea
A solitary narration contradicting stronger chains is weak; the ruling follows reliable evidence, not a narrator's personal fatwa.

This passage presents a classic case where a narrator's reported fatwa appears to contradict the hadith he narrated. The majority of scholars, including the Hanafis, uphold the hadith of seven washes because the narration supporting the three-wash fatwa is critically weak. You will learn how meticulous hadith criticism resolves such apparent contradictions and ensures that the ruling is based on the strongest proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting positions
First, determine the two views: one requiring seven washes (majority) and another requiring three (based on Abu Hurayra's fatwa). Note the key narrations cited for each.
The majority rely on a marfu' hadith; opponents cite a mawquf report.
2
Examine the chain of the opposing narration
Focus on the narration from 'Abd al-Malik ibn Abi Sulayman. Note that he is the sole transmitter (tafarrada) of this report. Review the critical assessments of him by Ahmad, Ibn Hajar, and al-Bayhaqi.
Tafarruḍ alone does not invalidate a report, but when combined with other weaknesses, it can.
3
Analyze the stronger chain
The narration via Hammad ibn Zayd is supported by multiple trustworthy narrators and agrees with the marfu' hadith. Recognize that this chain is among the most authentic.
Al-Daraqutni declared this chain sahih mawquf.
4
Apply the principle of tarjih
Prefer the narration that has stronger chains and is supported by other evidence. The principle of tarjih leads to adopting the seven-wash ruling.
The disagreement is a legitimate ikhtilaf, but the preponderant view is with the majority.
5
State the mufta bihi ruling
Conclude that the Hanafi position (seven washes) is the operative ruling for fatwa, based on the strength of the dalil.
This case illustrates how hadith criticism directly impacts fiqh.

ومسلم وأبو داود وابن ماجه والترمذي والنسائي وابن خزيمة). واعترض القائلون بالمذهب الثاني عَلَى استدلال الجُمْهُور، بأن أبا هُرَيْرَةَ - راوي الْحَدِيث - أفتى بخلاف ما رَوَى، وَهُوَ الغسل ثلاثاً، فكان دليلاً على وجـود النسخ . فروى الطحاوي والدارقطني من طريق عبد الملك بن أبي سليمان العرزمي، عن عطاء، عن أبي هُرَيْرَةَ - في الإناء يلغ فِيْهِ الكلب أو الهر - قَالَ: «يغسل ثلاث مرات». وأجاب الجُمْهُور عن اعتراضهم بأن هَذِهِ الرِّوَايَة تفرد بها العرزمي، ونص الحفاظ عَلَى خطئه فِيهَا، ومخالفته للثقات. إذا رَوَى الدارقطني من طريق حماد بن زيد عن أيوب عن مُحَمَّد بن سيرين، عن أبي هُرَيْرَةَ - في الكلب يلغ في الإناء - قَالَ: «يراق ويغسل سبع مرات». قال الدارقطني: «صحيح موقوف». ومما يشد عضد هَذِهِ الرِّوَايَة أنها موافقة للمرفوع، فظهر بها أن عبد الملك أبي سليمان العرزمي أخطأ فيها ، وَقَدْ قَالَ عَنْهُ الإمام أحمد: «ثقة يخطئ». وَقَالَ الحافظ ابن حجر: «صدوق له أوهام». وَقَدْ رجّح الرِّوَايَة الموافقة للحديث المرفوع البيهقي، فَقَالَ: «تفرد بِهِ عَبْد الملك من أصحاب عطاء، ثُمَّ من أصحاب أبي هُرَيْرَةَ، والحفاظ الثقات أصحاب عطاء من وأصحاب أبي هُرَيْرَةَ يروون سبع مرات، وفي ذَلِكَ دلالة عَلَى خطأ رِوَايَة عَبْد الملك بن أبي سليمان، عن عطاء عن أبي هُرَيْرَةَ في الثلاث، وعبد الملك لا يقبل مِنْهُ ما يخالف الثقات لمخالفته أهل الحفظ والثقة في بَعْض روايته تركه شعبة بن الحجاج، وَلَمْ يحتج بِهِ البُخَارِيّ في صحيحه. وَقَالَ ابن حجر: ورواية من رَوَى عَنْهُ موافقة فتياه لروايته أرجح من رِوَايَة من رَوَى عَنْهُ مخالفتها من حَيْثُ الإسناد ومن حَيْثُ النظر، أما النظر فظاهر، وأما الإسناد فالموافقة وردت من رِوَايَة حماد بن زيد عن أيوب، عن ابن سيرين، عَنْه، وهذا من أصح الأسانيد، وأما المخالفة فمن رِوَايَة عَبْد الملك بن أبي سليمان، عن عطاء، وَهُوَ دُونَ الأول فى القوة بكثير).
Chapter Two / Discrepancy in the Matn. And Muslim, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Khuzaymah (reported). And the proponents of the second opinion objected to the majority's inference, because Abu Hurayra - the narrator of the hadith - gave a fatwa contrary to what he narrated, which is washing three times, so that was evidence of abrogation. Al-Tahawi and al-Daraqutni narrated via 'Abd al-Malik ibn Abi Sulayman al-'Arzami, from 'Ata, from Abu Hurayra - concerning a vessel in which a dog or cat has drunk - he said: 'Wash three times.' And the majority answered their objection that this narration is singularly transmitted by al-'Arzami, and the hadith critics explicitly state his error in it and his contradiction of trustworthy narrators. For al-Daraqutni narrated via Hammad ibn Zayd from Ayyub from Muhammad ibn Sirin from Abu Hurayra - concerning a dog drinking from a vessel - he said: 'Pour it out and wash seven times.' Al-Daraqutni said: 'Sahih mawquf.' What strengthens this narration is that it agrees with the marfu' version, so it becomes clear that 'Abd al-Malik ibn Abi Sulayman al-'Arzami erred in it. Imam Ahmad said about him: 'Trustworthy but makes mistakes.' Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: 'Truthful, has errors.' And al-Bayhaqi preferred the narration that agrees with the marfu' hadith, saying: 'Abd al-Malik is alone among the students of 'Ata, then among the students of Abu Hurayra, while the trustworthy preservers among the students of 'Ata and Abu Hurayra narrate seven times. In that is evidence of the error of 'Abd al-Malik ibn Abi Sulayman's narration from 'Ata from Abu Hurayra of three. 'Abd al-Malik is not accepted when he contradicts the trustworthy, due to his opposition to the people of memory and trustworthiness in some of his narrations; Shu'ba ibn al-Hajjaj abandoned him, and al-Bukhari did not use him as evidence in his Sahih.' And Ibn Hajar said: 'The narration of one who narrated from him and whose fatwa agrees with his report is more likely correct than the narration of one who narrated from him and whose fatwa contradicts it, both in terms of isnad and reasoning. As for reasoning, it is clear; as for isnad, the agreeing narration came via Hammad ibn Zayd from Ayyub from Ibn Sirin from him, and that is among the most authentic chains. As for the contradicting narration, it came via 'Abd al-Malik ibn Abi Sulayman from 'Ata, and he is far weaker than the first.'
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a detailed textual analysis of a hadith matn dispute. The issue is the number of washes required for a vessel after a dog or cat has drunk from it (ولوغ الكلب). The majority (جمهور) hold that it is seven times based on a marfu' hadith. Opponents note that Abu Hurayra, the narrator of the hadith, reportedly gave a fatwa of only three washes, suggesting the hadith was abrogated or not practiced. The majority respond by critically examining the chain. The narration attributing three washes to Abu Hurayra is solitary (تفرد بها) from 'Abd al-Malik ibn Abi Sulayman al-'Arzami, who is deemed unreliable in this particular report by hadith critics. They contrast this with a stronger chain from Hammad ibn Zayd that confirms seven washes. The author presents opinions of Ahmad, Ibn Hajar, and al-Bayhaqi to demonstrate that the solitary report is erroneous and that the correct position is seven washes. This illustrates how matn criticism (نقد المتن) and careful examination of narrators' reliability can resolve apparent contradictions between narrated hadith and reported fatwas.

Key Terms
تفرد (tafarrada): That a narrator is the sole transmitter of a report, here indicating weakness when contradicting more reliable narrators.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the majority reject the narration that Abu Hurayra said to wash three times?
A) Because Abu Hurayra himself later retracted it.
B) Because the narrator 'Abd al-Malik ibn Abi Sulayman was considered unreliable in that report and stronger chains support seven washes.
C) Because the hadith is mawquf and not marfu'.
D) Because the majority prefer analogy over this hadith.

Key Takeaway
The majority (including Hanafis) adopt the seven-wash ruling because the solitary narration for three washes is critically weak, and the stronger chain supports the marfu' hadith.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Conflict Between Solitary Hadith and Analogy in Hanafi Usul
Usul al-fiqh dispute on precedence between solitary hadith and analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main Hanafi positions on the conflict between khabar al-wahid and qiyas, explain the rationale behind each, and apply the narrator categorization to evaluate a given solitary hadith.

Core Idea
Not all Hanafis reject khabar al-wahid when it contradicts qiyas; acceptance depends on the narrator's fiqh competency.

A common misconception is that Hanafis always require khabar al-wahid not to contradict qiyas. In reality, there is a rich internal debate. This lesson unpacks the two dominant Hanafi positions, the role of narrator expertise, and how this plays out in concrete examples like the wudu hadith from Abu Hurayrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two Hanafi positions
Read the passage to distinguish the early majority view (khabar always takes precedence) from the later view (narrator categorization: non-fiqh experts' reports accepted only if they agree with qiyas).
The later view is associated with 'Isa ibn Aban and Abu Zayd al-Dabusi.
2
Understand the narrator categorization
Focus on how later Hanafis divide narrators: those known for fiqh (e.g., caliphs, 'Abdallahs) vs. those known only for narration (e.g., Abu Hurayrah, Anas). Note the conditions for acceptance.
If a non-fiqh expert's hadith contradicts all qiyas, it is rejected.
3
Compare with the Maliki and Mu'tazili views
The passage mentions Malikis share the later Hanafi view, while the Mu'tazili Abu al-Husayn al-Basri gives qiyas precedence if its 'illa is qat'i.
What is the basis for the Mu'tazili view? (Text on 'illa is like text on ruling)
4
Analyze the Ibn Abbas – Abu Hurayrah example
Examine how Ibn Abbas challenged Abu Hurayrah's wudu hadith using qiyas, and how Abu Hurayrah defended it. Note what this reveals about the early Hanafi defense of the narrator's fiqh.
Abu Hurayrah's response indicates he considered his own hadith authoritative over analogical reasoning.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Determine the practical difference: a solitary hadith like 'توضؤوا مما مست النار' would be accepted by early Hanafis, but might be rejected by later Hanafis if the narrator is deemed a non-faqih and the hadith contradicts all qiyas.
The later view requires careful assessment of the narrator's fiqh background.

الفصل الثاني / الاختلاف في الْمَتْن
رَوَى عَنْهُ مخالفتها من حَيْثُ الإسناد ومن حَيْثُ النظر، أما النظر فظاهر، وأما الإسناد فالموافقة وردت من رِوَايَة حماد بن زيد عن أيوب، عن ابن سيرين، عَنْه، وهذا من أصح الأسانيد، وأما المخالفة فمن رِوَايَة عَبْد الملك بن أبي سليمان، عن عطاء، وَهُوَ دُونَ الأول فى القوة بكثير).
المبحث الخامس
مخالفة الحديث للقياس
ذهب جمهور عُلَماء الأمة إلى القول بحجية القياس، وأنه أحد أدلة الأحكام الشرعية ومصادرها في الفقه الإسلامي والقياس هُوَ: حمل معلوم على معلوم في إثبات حكم لهما، أو نفيه عنهما، بأمرٍ جامع بَيْنَهُما من إثبات حكم أو صفة أو نفيهما عنهما.
لذا كَانَ مبتنى القياس النظر والإستنباط من تصرفات الشارع وربط الأحكام بعللها، فإذا عارض خبر الواحد القياس، فأي مِنْهُمَا يقدم موجبه عَلَى الآخر؟ اشتهر عن الحنفية اشتراط عدم مخالفة خبر الواحد للقياس حَتَّى يصح العمل بِهِ كدليل مستقل، والحق أن هَذَا الموطن لَيْسَ محل اتفاق بَيْنَهُمْ، بَلْ هناك تفصيل في مذهبهم على النحو الآتي:
إذا تعارض خبر الآحاد مع القياس فأكثر المتقدمين من الحنفية على تقديم الخبر وافق القياس أو خالفه؛ لأن القياس اجتهاد ولا اجتهاد في مورد النص.
وأما الَّذِيْنَ قالوا بتقديم القياس عَلَى خبر الواحد فهم بَعْض المتقدمين مِنْهُمْ، وتابعهم عَلَيْهِ كَثِير من المتأخرين ولكنهم لَمْ يقولوا بالرد بإطلاق، بل قسموا الرُّوَاة على قسمين: الأول: الرُّوَاة المعروفون بالضبط والفقه والاجتهاد، كالخلفاء الأربعة والعبادلة ومعاذ بن جبل وزيد بن ثابت - رضي الله عَنْهُمْ - فهؤلاء تقبل أخبارهم باتفاق. الثاني: الرُّوَاة الَّذِيْنَ اشتهروا بالرواية، وَلَمْ يعرفوا بالفقه والاجتهاد والفتيا، فإذا جاءوا بخبر الآحاد، فإن وافق القياس قبل، وإن خالف القياس ووافق قياساً آخر قبل أيضاً، وإن خالف جميع الأقيسة، فَقَالَ عيسى بن أبان (۱) والقاضي أبو زيد الدبوسي وتابعهما أكثر المتأخرين من الحنفية أنَّه لا يقبل (۳). وَهُوَ قول للمالكية).
وفصل أبو الْحُسَيْن البصري () من المعتزلة تفصيلاً آخر، فرأى أن القياس يقدّم على خبر الواحد في حالة ثبوت علة القياس بدليل قاطع، وعلل ذلك بأن النص عَلَى العلة كالنص على حكمها، فحينئذ القياس قطعي، وخبر الآحاد ظني والقطعي مقدم على الظني.
واستدلوا بأن عرض خبر الواحد عَلَى القياس كَانَ من ضمن المناهج التي اتبعها الصَّحَابَة في نقد المرويات وتمحيص الأخبار، فهذا ابن عَبَّاسٍ يرد عَلَى أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عندما حدث بحديث: توضؤوا ممَّا مست النار، قائلاً: أنتوضأ من الدهن، أنتوضأ من الحميم؟ فَقَالَ أَبو هُرَيْرَةَ: يا ابن أخي إذا سَمِعْت حديثاً عن رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فَلا تضرب الأمثال.
فابن عَبَّاسٍ قَدْ توقف في قبول خبر أبي هُرَيْرَةَ وعارضه بالقياس. وأجاب الجُمْهُور بأن دعوى أن مِثْل هَؤُلاَءِ من الصَّحَابَة – كأبي هُرَيْرَةَ وأنس – ليسوا من أهل الفقه، أمر فيه نظر طويل، ولوا أمعنا النظر في مروياته وآرائه لعلمنا رجاحة عقليته الفقهية، وإجابته لابن عَبَّاسٍ تدل عَلَى هَذَا دلالة لا يشوبها لبس أو
Chapter two: Difference in the text. He narrated from him its contradiction in terms of chain and reasoning. As for reasoning, it is apparent; as for chain, the agreement came from the narration of Hammad ibn Zayd from Ayyub, from Ibn Sirin, from him, and this is one of the most authentic chains. The disagreement came from the narration of 'Abd al-Malik ibn Abi Sulayman from 'Ata', and he is much weaker than the first. The fifth section: Contradiction of hadith to qiyas. The majority of scholars of the nation have held that qiyas is authoritative and that it is one of the proofs of legal rulings and sources in Islamic jurisprudence. Qiyas is: applying a known thing to another known thing in affirming a ruling for them, or negating it from them, due to a common link between them in affirming a ruling or attribute or negating them from them. Therefore the basis of qiyas is consideration and deduction from the acts of the Lawgiver and linking rulings to their causes. So if a khabar al-wahid contradicts qiyas, which of them takes precedence? It is well-known from the Hanafis the condition that a khabar al-wahid does not contradict qiyas in order for it to be valid as an independent proof. The truth is that this point is not agreed upon among them; rather there is detail in their madhhab as follows: When a solitary report conflicts with qiyas, most early Hanafis give precedence to the report whether it agrees with qiyas or contradicts it, because qiyas is ijtihad and there is no ijtihad in the presence of a text. As for those who said to give precedence to qiyas over khabar al-wahid, they are some of the early ones among them, followed by many later ones, but they did not reject it absolutely. Rather they divided narrators into two categories: First: narrators known for precision, fiqh, and ijtihad, like the four caliphs, the 'Abadilah, Mu'adh ibn Jabal, and Zayd ibn Thabit (may Allah be pleased with them). Their reports are accepted by agreement. Second: narrators famous for narration but not known for fiqh, ijtihad, and fatwa. If they bring a solitary report, if it agrees with qiyas it is accepted; if it contradicts qiyas but agrees with another qiyas it is also accepted; if it contradicts all qiyas, then 'Isa ibn Aban and Qadi Abu Zayd al-Dabusi and most later Hanafis followed them said it is not accepted. This is also the opinion of the Malikis. Abu al-Husayn al-Basri from the Mu'tazilites detailed another view: he held that qiyas is given precedence over khabar al-wahid when the 'illa of the qiyas is established by a decisive proof, reasoning that the text on the 'illa is like a text on its ruling, so then qiyas is definitive (qat'i) and khabar al-wahid is speculative (zanni), and the definitive takes precedence over the speculative. They argued that presenting khabar al-wahid to qiyas was among the methodologies the Companions followed in criticizing narrations and sifting reports. For example, Ibn 'Abbas objected to Abu Hurayrah when he narrated the hadith: 'Perform wudu from what is touched by fire,' saying: 'Should we perform wudu from oil? Should we perform wudu from hot water?' Abu Hurayrah said: 'O son of my brother, when you hear a hadith from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), do not strike parables.' So Ibn 'Abbas hesitated in accepting Abu Hurayrah's report and contradicted it with qiyas. The majority responded that the claim that such Companions as Abu Hurayrah and Anas were not people of fiqh is a matter requiring lengthy consideration; if we had carefully examined his narrations and opinions, we would know the soundness of his legal reasoning, and his answer to Ibn 'Abbas indicates this clearly without any confusion or...
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the conflict between khabar al-wahid (solitary hadith) and qiyas (analogy) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author first defines qiyas in the standard way: applying a known case to another due to a common cause, to affirm or negate a ruling. He then poses the central question: if a solitary report contradicts qiyas, which takes precedence? The famous Hanafi condition that khabar al-wahid must not contradict qiyas is shown not to be unanimous. The author distinguishes two positions within the Hanafi school: (1) Most early Hanafis give absolute precedence to khabar al-wahid over qiyas, because qiyas is ijtihad and ijtihad is not permitted where a text exists. (2) Some early and many later Hanafis (followed by Isa ibn Aban and Abu Zayd al-Dabusi) give precedence to qiyas over khabar al-wahid, but not absolutely. They categorize narrators: those known for fiqh and ijtihad (like the four caliphs) are accepted unconditionally; those known only for narration but not fiqh are accepted only if their report agrees with qiyas or at least with another qiyas. If it contradicts all qiyas, it is rejected. This is also the Maliki position. The author then mentions the Mu'tazili Abu al-Husayn al-Basri, who gives qiyas precedence if its 'illa (effective cause) is proven by a decisive (qat'i) text, arguing that the text establishing the 'illa is like a text on the ruling itself. The passage concludes with an example: Ibn 'Abbas's objection to Abu Hurayrah's hadith 'Perform wudu from what is touched by fire' by analogy with oil and hot water. Abu Hurayrah's response shows he defends the text. The majority response (probably Hanafi position) is that Abu Hurayrah was indeed a jurist, and his answer demonstrates his legal acumen. The passage ends abruptly, but the argument defends the reliability of narrators like Abu Hurayrah.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A solitary hadith or report that does not reach the level of tawatur
القياس (al-qiyas): Applying a known ruling to a new case due to a common cause ('illa)
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause or ratio legis that grounds a legal ruling in qiyas
لا اجتهاد في مورد النص (la ijtihada fi mawarid al-nass): A usul maxim meaning: no independent reasoning is permitted where a textual ruling exists

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi view (as stated by 'Isa ibn Aban and Abu Zayd al-Dabusi), what happens when a narrator who is not known for fiqh reports a solitary hadith that contradicts all qiyas?
A) The hadith is accepted unconditionally.
B) The hadith is rejected.
C) The hadith is preferred over qiyas.
D) The narrator is considered a faqih.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains two positions on khabar al-wahid conflicting with qiyas: early Hanafis give precedence to the khabar unconditionally, while later Hanafis distinguish based on the narrator's fiqh expertise.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
8 min
The Hanafi Position on Qiyas vs Khabar al-Wahid: The Ibn Abbas Incident Analyzed
Dispute on qiyas vs khabar al-wahid with Companion incident

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the later Hanafi position on khabar al-wahid conflicting with qiyas and evaluate the jumhur's rebuttal using the Ibn Abbas incident.

Core Idea
When a khabar al-wahid contradicts all analogies, later Hanafis reject it, but the majority rebut using abrogation.

This lesson examines a foundational usul dispute: does qiyas (analogy) take precedence over a khabar al-wahid (solitary hadith) when they conflict? We focus on the Ibn Abbas–Abu Huraira incident, often cited by later Hanafis to support rejecting ahad hadith opposed by qiyas, and the jumhur's counter-argument that Ibn Abbas actually considered the hadith abrogated. By analyzing this incident, you will understand how the Hanafi school navigates conflicting sources of law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and positions
From the passage, extract the later Hanafi view (Isa ibn Aban, al-Dabusi) that a khabar al-wahid opposing all analogies is not accepted, and note the Maliki agreement. Also note Abu al-Husayn al-Basri's distinction based on qat'i 'illah.
The key contrast is between later Hanafis and the jumhur (majority).
2
Analyze the Ibn Abbas incident
Read how Ibn Abbas rejected Abu Huraira's hadith 'Perform wudu from what fire has touched' using qiyas (analogy to oil and hot water). This is the central evidence for the later Hanafi view.
Ibn Abbas's question 'Should we perform wudu from oil? Should we perform wudu from hot water?' shows qiyas in action.
3
Understand the jumhur's rebuttal
The jumhur argue that Ibn Abbas's rejection was based on abrogation (naskh) by another hadith (Prophet ate sheep shoulder and did not perform wudu), not qiyas. They also point out that many Companions narrated the same hadith, strengthening its transmission.
This rebuttal challenges the evidentiary value of the incident for the qiyas-over-hadith position.
4
Derive the usul principle
From the later Hanafi perspective, when a qiyas has a qat'i 'illah, it becomes qat'i and takes precedence over zanni khabar al-wahid. The Ibn Abbas incident, though contested, illustrates this principle.
The principle: القطعي مقدم على الظني (the definitive takes precedence over the speculative).

Source Text

الفصل الثاني / الاختلاف في المـ الْمَتْن

أيضاً، وإن خالف جميع الأقيسة، فَقَالَ عيسى بن أبان (١) والقاضي أبو زيد الدبوسي (٢) وتابعهما أكثر المتأخرين من الحنفية أنَّه لا يقبل (٣). وَهُوَ قول للمالكية (٤).

وفصل أبو الْحُسَيْن البصري (٥) من المعتزلة تفصيلاً آخر، فرأى أن القياس يقدّم على خبر الواحد في حالة ثبوت علة القياس بدليل قاطع، وعلل ذلك بأن النص عَلَى العلة كالنص على حكمها، فحينئذ القياس قطعي، وخبر الآحاد ظني والقطعي مقدم على الظني (٦).

واستدلوا بأن عرض خبر الواحد عَلَى القياس كَانَ من ضمن المناهج التي اتبعها الصَّحَابَة في نقد المرويات وتمحيص الأخبار، فهذا ابن عَبَّاسٍ يرد عَلَى أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عندما حدث بحديث: توضؤوا ممَّا مست النار، قائلاً: أنتوضأ من الدهن، أنتوضأ من الحميم؟ فَقَالَ أَبو هُرَيْرَةَ: يا ابن أخي إذا سَمِعْت حديثاً عن رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فَلا تضرب الأمثال (٧) لَهُ.

فابن عَبَّاسٍ قَدْ توقف في قبول خبر أبي هُرَيْرَةَ وعارضه بالقياس. وأجاب الجُمْهُور بأن دعوى أن مِثْل هَؤُلاَءِ من الصَّحَابَة – كأبي هُرَيْرَةَ وأنس – ليسوا من أهل الفقه، أمر فيه نظر طويل، ولوا أمعنا النظر في مروياته وآرائه لعلمنا رجاحة عقليته الفقهية، وإجابته لابن عَبَّاسٍ تدل عَلَى هَذَا دلالة لا يشوبها لبس أو غموض.

وأما حديث الوضوء مِمَّا مست النار فَلَمْ يَكُن رد ابن عَبَّاسٍ لَهُ مستنداً إِلَى مخالفة القياس، وإنما كَانَ الْحَدِيث عِنْدَ ابن عَبَّاس منسوخاً بحديث: أن النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أكل كتف شاة وصلى وَلَمْ يتوضأ» (١).

عَلَى أن أبا هُرَيْرَةَ لَمْ يَكُنْ منفرداً برواية حَدِيث الوضوء ممـا مـسـت النار، إذ شاركه في روايته أبو أيوب (٢)، وأبو طلحة (٣)، وزيد بن ثابت (٤)، وأم حبيبة (٥)، وعائشة (٦)، وأبو موسى الأشعري (٧)، وسهل بن الحنظلية (٨)، وأم سلمة (١٠)، وأنس بن مالك (١١)، وعبد الله بن عمر (١٢)، ومعاذ بن جبل (١٣)، وعبد الله بن زيد (١٤)، وغيرهم؛ حَتَّى (١) رَوَاهُ أحمد (٢٥٦/١ ، والبخاري (٦٣/١ (٢١٧)، وأبو داود (١٨٧) ، وابن خزيمة (٤١) من حَدِيث ابن عباس. (٢) خالد بن زيد بن كليب الأنصاري أبو أيوب من كبار الصَّحَابَة، مات سنة (٥٠ هـ)، وَقِيلَ: (٥٢هـ). طبقات لابن سعد ٤٨٤/٣ و ٤٨٥ ، وسير أعلام النبلاء ٤۰۲/۲ و ٤١٤-٤١٣، والتقريب (١٦٣٣) وحديثه عند النسائي ١٠٦/٢. (٣) زيد بن سهل بن الأسود، أبو طلحة الأنصاري صاحب رَسُول الله ، وأحد أعيان البدريين توفي سنة (٣٤) هـ). تاريخ الصَّحَابَة : ١٠٦، وسير أعلام النبلاء ۲۷/۲ و ۲۸ ، والتقريب (۲۱۳۹) وحديثه عِنْدَ النسائي ١٠٦/٢. (٤) عِنْدَ النسائي ٢/ ١٠٧. (٥) أم المؤمنين، رملة بنت أبي سُفْيَان بن حرب، ويقال: صخر بن حرب بن أمية، أم حبيبة، توفيت سنة (٤٤ هـ). انظر: الطبقات لابن سعد ٩٦/٨ و ۱٠٠ ،والطبقات لابن خليفة: ۳۳۲، وسير أعلام النبلاء ۲۱۸/۲ ، وحديثها عند أبي داود (١٩٥). (٦) عِنْدَ مُسْلِم ١/ ١٨٨ (٣٥٣). (۷) عِنْدَ أحمد ٣٩٧/٤ و ٤١٣. (۸) سهل بن الحنظلية ،الأنصاري صحابي والحنظلية أمه أو من أمهاته واختلف في اسم أبيه، والأشهر عَمْرو بن عدي توفي في صدر خلافة معاوية. تاريخ الصَّحَابَة : ۱۲۲، والإصابة ٨٦/٢ و ٨٧، والتقريب (٢٦٥٥). (۹) عِنْدَ أحمد ٤/ ١٨٠ و ٥ / ٢٨٩. (۱۰) عِنْدَ الطبراني في الكبير ٢٣ / ٢٣٦. (۱۱) عِنْدَ البزار، كَمَا في المجمع ١/ ٢٤٨ - ٢٤٩. (۱۲) عِنْدَ البزار والطبراني في الكبير والأوسط، كما في المجمع ١ / ٢٤٩. (١٣) عِنْدَ البزار، كما في المجمع ١ / ٢٤٩. (١٤) هُوَ الصَّحَابِي أبو مُحَمَّد عَبْد الله بن زيد بن عاصم بن كعب الأنصاري المازني المدني، توفي سنة (٦٣ هـ). تاريخ الصَّحَابَة، لابن حبان: ١٥٥، وتهذيب الكمال ١٣٨/٤ (٣٢٦٩)، وسير أعلام النبلاء ٢/
Chapter Two: Disagreement in the Text (Matn). Also, even if it contradicts all analogies, Isa ibn Aban and Qadi Abu Zayd al-Dabusi and most later Hanafis followed them in that it is not accepted. And it is a view of the Malikis. Abu al-Husayn al-Basri from the Mu'tazila made another distinction: he held that analogy is given precedence over khabar al-wahid in the case where the cause of the analogy is established by definitive evidence, and he reasoned that the text on the cause is like the text on its ruling; then the analogy is definitive, and khabar al-wahid is speculative, and the definitive takes precedence over the speculative. They argued that presenting khabar al-wahid to analogy was among the methods the Companions followed in criticizing reports and scrutinizing narrations. Here is Ibn Abbas rejecting Abu Huraira when he narrated the hadith: 'Perform wudu from what fire has touched,' saying: 'Should we perform wudu from oil? Should we perform wudu from hot water?' So Abu Huraira said: 'O son of my brother! When you hear a hadith from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, do not strike examples for it.' Thus Ibn Abbas hesitated in accepting Abu Huraira's report and opposed it with analogy. The majority responded that the claim that such Companions – like Abu Huraira and Anas – were not people of jurisprudence is a matter of lengthy consideration. If we had carefully examined his narrations and opinions, we would have known the strength of his legal intellect, and his answer to Ibn Abbas indicates this with clarity and no ambiguity. As for the hadith of wudu from what fire touched, Ibn Abbas's rejection of it was not based on opposition to analogy. Rather, the hadith was considered by Ibn Abbas to be abrogated by the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ate a sheep's shoulder and prayed without performing wudu. Moreover, Abu Huraira was not alone in narrating the hadith of wudu from what fire touched, as he was joined in narrating it by Abu Ayyub, Abu Talha, Zayd ibn Thabit, Umm Habiba, Aisha, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, Sahl ibn al-Hanzaliyya, Umm Salama, Anas ibn Malik, Abdullah ibn Umar, Muadh ibn Jabal, Abdullah ibn Zayd, and others, such that...
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage discusses the important usul al-fiqh dispute regarding the relative authority of khabar al-wahid (solitary hadith) and qiyas (analogy) when they conflict. It opens by presenting the view of Isa ibn Aban, al-Qadi Abu Zayd al-Dabusi, and most later Hanafis that a khabar al-wahid is not accepted if it contradicts all analogies. This is also a Maliki position. Then it mentions the distinction of Abu al-Husayn al-Basri (a Mu'tazili): if the 'illah (effective cause) of the qiyas is proven by qat'i (definitive) evidence, then the qiyas is qat'i and takes precedence over the zanni (speculative) khabar al-wahid. The text then provides the istidlal (argument) of those who support rejecting khabar al-wahid due to qiyas: they cite the practice of the Companions, particularly the incident where Ibn Abbas rejected Abu Huraira's hadith about wudu from cooked food, apparently using qiyas. The jumhur (majority) response is that Companions like Abu Huraira were indeed jurists, and Ibn Abbas's rejection was not based on qiyas but on his belief that the hadith was abrogated by another hadith (the Prophet eating a sheep's shoulder and not performing wudu). The passage then lists many Companions who narrated the same hadith about wudu from fire, showing its widespread transmission and weakening the argument that it was weak or contradicted by qiyas. The discussion highlights the nuanced approach of the Hanafi school: while later scholars like al-Dabusi favored qiyas over ahad hadith in certain cases, the incident commonly cited to support this is actually explained differently by the majority.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith narrated by one or a few narrators that does not reach the level of tawatur.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning; applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to a shared effective cause ('illah).
قطعي وظني (qat'i and zanni): Qat'i: definitive and certain; zanni: speculative and probable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to later Hanafis like al-Dabusi, what is the ruling regarding a khabar al-wahid that contradicts all analogies (qiyas)?
A) It is accepted and the qiyas is set aside.
B) It is not accepted because qiyas takes precedence.
C) It is accepted only if the qiyas is speculative.
D) It is considered abrogated.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when a khabar al-wahid contradicts a qiyas with a qat'i 'illah, the qiyas is preferred, a principle illustrated by the contested Ibn Abbas incident.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Hanafi Ruling on Benefiting from Mortgaged Property
Illustrates how differences in usul lead to fiqh differences on benefiting from a pledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on benefiting from a mortgaged property and explain the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf, while comparing it with the Hanbali/Zahiri position.

Core Idea
Hanafis prohibit the mortgagee from using the property without permission; some deem it riba even with permission.

This passage exposes a deep usul divergence: whether a specific permissive hadith overrides a general prohibition. We will unpack the Hanafi stance—rooted in a fear of riba—and see how internal debates further nuance the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
The question is whether the mortgagee may derive any benefit (like riding, milking, dwelling) from the mortgaged property. The passage presents two clashing views.
The debate reflects a clash between a general prohibition hadith and a specific permissive hadith.
2
Locate the Hanafi position
The Hanafis generally prohibit the mortgagee from benefitting without the mortgagor's permission. Note the internal variation: some say even with permission it is riba; others distinguish based on stipulation in the contract.
This internal ikhtilaf shows the school's careful approach to preventing riba.
3
Understand the usul reasoning
The Hanafis rely on a hadith stating that the pledge does not leave its owner's possession, implying that all benefits belong to the mortgagor. They consider the permissive hadith weak or abrogated.
This preference for one hadith over another is a classic usul al-fiqh operation.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis require permission for any use; Hanbalis allow use of riding and milch animals without permission.
This difference has real-world impact on pledges of animals, vehicles, or properties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النموذج الأول: الانتفاع بالعين المرهونة اختلف العلماء في العين المرهونة، هل يجوز الانتفاع بها؟ على قولين: الأول: يجوز للمرتهن الانتفاع بالعين المرهونة إذا كَانت مركوباً أو محلوباً، أذن الراهن أم لَمْ يأذن. وبه قَالَ إسحاق (۳) ، والحنابلة)، والظاهرية ) . الثاني: لا يجوز الانتفاع بالعين المرهونة وبه قَالَ جمهور الفقهاء، على تفصيل مختلف بَيْنَهُمْ عَلَى النحو الآتي: ۱ - قَالَ الحنفية: لَيْسَ للراهن ولا المرتهن الانتفاع بالمرهون مطلقاً، لا بالسكنى ولا بالركوب ولا بغيرهما، إلا بإذن كُلّ مِنْهُمَا للآخر. وفي قَوْل لَهُمْ لا يجوز الانتفاع للمرتهن ولو أذن الراهن؛ لأنه ربا. وَلَهُمْ قَوْل آخر: إنْ شَرَطَهُ في العقد كَانَ رباً، وإلا جاز للمرتهن الانتفاع بإذن الراهن. ٢ - قَالَ :المالكية ما ينتج عن المرهون ملك للراهن، والمرتهن نائـب عـنـه فـي ۳۷۷، والتقريب (۳۳۳۱)، وحديثه عِنْدَ الطبراني في الأوسط ٢٣٦/١(٣٦٤) بتحقيق الطحان. (۱) انظر: نظم المتناثر : ۷۹ (٣٥) (۲) المنهل الروي: ۳۲ ، وانظر: أسباب اختلاف الفقهاء: ۲۹۲ (۳) الجامع الكبير للترمذي عقب (١٢٥٤). (٤) المغني ٤ / ٤٣٢ ، والمقنع ،۱۱۸ ، والمحرر ١/ ٣٣٦ ، وكشاف القناع ٣/ ٣٤٢. (٥) المحلى ۸۹/۸ (٦) بدائع الصنائع ٦ / ١٤٦ ، وشرح فتح القدير ۸ / ۲۰۱ ، وتبيين الحقائق /٦ / ٦٧، وحاشية الطحطاوي على مراقي الفلاح ٤ / ٢٣٦ ، وحاشية ابن عابدين ٣١٠/٥.
First Model: Benefiting from the Mortgaged Property. Scholars differed regarding the mortgaged property: is it permissible to benefit from it? Two opinions: First: It is permissible for the mortgagee to benefit from the mortgaged property if it is a riding animal or a milch animal, whether the mortgagor permits or not. This was held by Ishaq, the Hanbalis, and the Zahiris. Second: It is not permissible to benefit from the mortgaged property, and this was held by the majority of jurists, with different details among them as follows: 1 - The Hanafis said: Neither the mortgagor nor the mortgagee may benefit from the mortgaged property at all, not by dwelling, riding, or anything else, except with mutual permission. And there is a view among them that it is not permissible for the mortgagee even with the mortgagor's permission because it is usury. And they have another view: if it is stipulated in the contract it is usury, otherwise it is permissible for the mortgagee to benefit with the mortgagor's permission. 2 - The Malikis said: The produce of the mortgaged property belongs to the mortgagor, and the mortgagee is his agent in... [footnotes follow]
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage illustrates how differences in usul principles (specifically regarding khabar al-wahid vs qiyas) translate into actual fiqh rulings. The example is the permissibility of benefiting from a mortgaged property. The author presents two main positions: one group (Ishaq, Hanbalis, Zahiris) allows the mortgagee to use a riding or milch animal regardless of permission, while the majority (including Hanafis, Malikis, Shafi'is) prohibit it, with nuances. The Hanafi position is detailed: generally, neither party may use the property without the other's permission. However, there are variant Hanafi opinions: some say even with permission it is prohibited because it resembles riba; others distinguish based on whether the benefit was stipulated in the contract. This nuance reflects the Hanafi concern with preventing usury. The passage ends with citations of Hanafi sources. This example demonstrates how the usul principle (preferring a hadith that forbids benefiting from a pledge over qiyas that might allow it) leads to the ruling of prohibition.

Key Terms
الرهن (al-rahn): Mortgage or pledge; a property given as security for a debt.
المرتهن (al-murtahin): The mortgagee; the person who receives the pledge as security.
الربا (al-riba): Usury or interest; any excess in exchange of same commodities or deferred payment.
الانتفاع (al-intifa'): Benefiting; using the property to derive utility (e.g., riding, dwelling, milking).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented, what is the default ruling on the mortgagee using the mortgaged property?
A) The mortgagee may always use it if it is a riding or milch animal.
B) The mortgagee may not use it unless the mortgagor permits.
C) The mortgagee may use it only after the debt is due.
D) The mortgagee may never use it, even with permission.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits the mortgagee from using the pledged property without permission, grounded in a general prohibition hadith and a strong aversion to riba, though internal opinions vary on the effect of permission.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
Khabar al-Wahid vs Qiyas: Benefiting from Pledged Property
Analyzing the impact of usul positions on a fiqh ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Hanafi preference for qiyas over khabar al-wahid leads to the ruling prohibiting the pledgee's use of pledged property without permission, and contrast it with the Shafi'i-Hanbali position that permits it based on a hadith.

Core Idea
The Hanafi refusal to prioritize khabar al-wahid over qiyas restricts the pledgee's use of pledged property, despite a prophetic hadith permitting it.

This lesson explores how a foundational usul disagreement—whether a solitary hadith (khabar al-wahid) overrides analogical reasoning (qiyas)—directly shapes a fiqh ruling. The case study is the permissibility of a pledgee using a pledged animal's back or milk. The Hanafi school, applying its stricter conditions for accepting khabar al-wahid, upholds the qiyas-based prohibition, while the Shafi'i and Hanbali schools give precedence to the hadith. Understanding this dispute clarifies both the usul methodology and its practical impact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the usul dispute
Recognize that the disagreement over benefiting from pledged property stems from a deeper usul question: when a khabar al-wahid contradicts qiyas, which takes precedence? The Hanafi school often prefers qiyas unless the hadith meets certain criteria; the Shafi'i school generally prefers a sound khabar al-wahid.
This is not merely a fiqh difference but a methodological one.
2
State the general position of hadith scholars
According to Ibn Jama'ah and the majority of hadith scholars, a sound khabar al-wahid is acceptable and preponderant over qiyas. This view is attributed to al-Shafi'i and Ahmad ibn Hanbal.
This sets the backdrop for the Hanafi counter-position.
3
Analyze the fiqh example: the hadith on pledged property
Examine the hadith of Abu Hurayrah: the back of a pledged animal is ridden and its milk drunk in return for expenses. This hadith is a khabar al-wahid that directly permits the pledgee's use, creating an exception to the general rule that benefit from another's property requires permission.
The hadith is accepted by Shafi'is and Hanbalis as overruling qiyas.
4
Compare the Hanafi ruling with the Shafi'i/Hanbali ruling
The Hanafi school rules that the pledgee may not use the pledged property without the pledgor's permission (with nuances about riba). The Shafi'i/Hanbali school permits use of riding/milking animals based on the hadith, even without permission. This difference is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).
Both positions are internally consistent given their usul premises.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In a Hanafi context, a pledgee cannot ride or milk the animal without permission; in a Shafi'i/Hanbali context, he can, provided he covers expenses. This directly impacts daily transactions involving pledged livestock.
The usul choice determines the fiqh outcome.

Source Text

الفصل الثاني / الاختلاف في الْمَتْن
عدوه من المتواتر (۱).
۱۷۷
فالراجح من ناحية النظر والدليل: ماذهب إِلَيْهِ جمهور الْعُلَمَاء، لذا قَالَ ابن جَمَاعَة : والصحيح الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ أَئِمَّة الحَدِيث أو جمهورهم، أن خبر الواحد العدل المتصل في جَمِيع ذَلِكَ مقبول وراجح على القياس المعارض لَهُ، وبه قَالَ الشَّافِعِي وأحمد بن حنبل وغيرهما من أَئِمَّة الحَدِيث والفقه والأصول (۳).

غَيْر أَن هَذَا الاختلاف في المواقف بشأن مخالفة خبر الواحد للقياس تَرَكَ أثراً
في الإستنباطات الفقهية نلمسها جلية في الأمثلة الآتية:
النموذج الأول: الانتفاع بالعين المرهونة
اختلف العلماء في العين المرهونة، هل يجوز الانتفاع بها؟ على قولين: الأول: يجوز للمرتهن الانتفاع بالعين المرهونة إذا كَانت مركوباً أو محلوباً، أذن الراهن أم لَمْ يأذن. وبه قَالَ إسحاق (۳) ، والحنابلة)، والظاهرية ) . الثاني: لا يجوز الانتفاع بالعين المرهونة وبه قَالَ جمهور الفقهاء، على تفصيل مختلف بَيْنَهُمْ عَلَى النحو الآتي:

Chapter Two: Difference in the Matn. They count it from the mutawatir (1). 177 Therefore, the preponderant from the perspective of theory and evidence is what the majority of scholars held; hence Ibn Jama'ah said: The correct view that the imams of hadith or their majority hold is that the solitary report of a just, continuous chain is in all that acceptable and preponderant over the qiyas that contradicts it, and this is the view of al-Shafi'i, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, and others from the imams of hadith, fiqh, and usul (3). However, this difference in stances regarding the contradiction of khabar al-wahid with qiyas left an impact on legal deductions that we clearly perceive in the following examples: The first example: Benefiting from the pledged property. The scholars differed regarding pledged property: is it permissible to benefit from it? On two views: First: It is permissible for the pledgee to benefit from the pledged property if it is a riding animal or a milking animal, regardless of whether the pledgor permitted or not. This is held by Ishaq (3), the Hanabilah, and the Zahiris. Second: It is not permissible to benefit from the pledged property; this is held by the majority of jurists, with different details among them as follows: 1. The Hanafis said: Neither the pledgor nor the pledgee may benefit from the pledged property absolutely, whether by dwelling, riding, or anything else, except with each other's permission. And there is a view among them that it is not permissible for the pledgee even if the pledgor permits, because it is riba. And they have another view: if it is stipulated in the contract, it is riba; otherwise, it is permissible for the pledgee to benefit with the permission of the pledgor. 2. The Malikis said: What is produced from the pledged property belongs to the pledgor, and the pledgee is his deputy in obtaining it. The pledgee may benefit from it under conditions: a) that it be stipulated in the core of the contract; b) the period be determined; c) the debt for which it is pledged not be a loan. If the condition is missed in the contract, then if the pledgor later permits the pledgee to benefit, it is not permissible. 3. The Shafi'is said: The pledgee has only his right to secure his debt, and he is prevented from any disposal or benefit from the pledged property. The pledgor may have any benefit that does not reduce the value, such as riding, milking, dwelling, etc. As for what reduces the value, like building on the land or planting in it, it is not permissible except with the pledgee's permission. 4. The Zaydis said: The pledgee only has the right of retention; if he uses it, he owes the pledgor rent. 5. The Imamis said: It is not permissible for either the pledgor or pledgee to dispose of the pledged property except with the other's permission. 6. Ahmad said in one narration: Even if the pledged property is a milking or riding animal, he is donating its expenses, and it is not permissible for him to benefit from it in any way. Those who permitted it adduced what Abu Hurayrah narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The back (of a riding animal) is ridden in return for its expenses when it is pledged, and the milk of a milking animal is drunk in return for its expenses when it is pledged, and the one who rides and drinks bears the expenses.' It was reported by Ibn Abi Shaybah, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, Ahmad, al-Bukhari, and Abu [Dawud]. (Footnotes omitted in translation)
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute illustrating how the methodological prioritization of khabar al-wahid over qiyas directly affects fiqh rulings. The author begins by stating the preferred view of the hadith scholars and many jurists (including al-Shafi'i and Ahmad) that a sound khabar al-wahid is accepted and takes precedence over qiyas. Then he presents the first applied example: benefiting from pledged property (al-ʿayn al-marhūnah).

The dispute is divided into two broad camps: (1) those who permit the pledgee to benefit from a riding or milking animal regardless of the pledgor's permission (Ishaq, Hanbalis, Zahiris), and (2) the majority who restrict or prohibit it. The Hanafi position is detailed: generally, neither party may benefit without the other's consent. Within the Hanafi school, there are three nuanced views: absolute prohibition even with permission (citing riba), prohibition only if stipulated in the contract, and permissibility with permission if not stipulated. The other schools (Maliki, Shafi'i, Zaydi, Imami, and one narration from Ahmad) each have their own conditions and restrictions.

The evidence for the permissibility view is the hadith of Abu Hurayrah: the riding animal is ridden in return for its expenses when pledged, and the milk is drunk likewise. This hadith is a khabar al-wahid that directly permits the pledgee's use, contradicting the general qiyas that property used by someone else without compensation is either a loan or rental requiring payment. The Hanafi position, which does not accept this hadith as overriding qiyas (due to their stricter conditions for accepting khabar al-wahid or because they consider it abrogated or specific), adheres to the qiyas prohibiting benefit without explicit permission. This exemplifies how usul choices lead to divergent furūʿ rulings.

The passage also includes extensive footnoted (1-9) references to primary sources for each school's position and the hadith's narrations.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wāḥid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators that does not reach the level of tawātur.
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning used to derive a ruling for a new case based on an existing ruling from the primary sources.
العين المرهونة (al-ʿayn al-marhūnah): The specific property that is pledged as collateral for a debt.
المرتهن (al-murtaḥin): The creditor or pledgee who holds the pledged property as security.
الراهن (al-rāhin): The debtor or pledgor who gives the property as collateral.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, may a pledgee ride a pledged animal without the pledgor's permission?
A) Yes, because of the hadith 'The back is ridden in return for its expenses'
B) No, not even with permission, because it is riba
C) No, unless the pledgor permits, and if stipulated in the contract it is riba
D) Yes, if the animal is a riding animal

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi preference for qiyas over khabar al-wahid in this case illustrates how usul methodology—not mere scriptural evidence—determines fiqh rulings on pledged property use.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Evaluating the Hadith on Mortgage Benefits: The Majority's Response and Usul Critique
Majority scholars' refutation of a hadith permitting mortgagee's benefit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the majority scholars' response to the hadith on mortgage benefits by identifying the ambiguity in the hadith, applying the supporting hadith and qiyas arguments, and explaining the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
A hadith's ambiguity and conflict with stronger evidence can lead the majority to reinterpret or set it aside.

This passage shows how the majority of jurists (جمهور الفقهاء) critically engage with a hadith that appears to allow the mortgagee to benefit from the pledged property. They do not simply accept it but subject it to usul analysis: they identify its ambiguity, cite a clearer hadith, and point out its contradiction to qiyas and agreed-upon principles. This lesson walks you through their reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested hadith and its ambiguity
The hadith under scrutiny (referenced but not fully quoted) does not specify who is spending and benefiting. The majority argue that this ambiguity makes it weak evidence. They note two possibilities: the spender could be the mortgagor (using his own property) or the mortgagee (benefiting in exchange for expenses).
Ambiguity (ihtimal) in a text reduces its clarity and strength as dalil.
2
Examine the supporting hadith from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib
The majority cite the hadith 'لا يغلق الرهن – لصاحبه غنمه وعليه غرمه' (The pledge is not foreclosed; its profit belongs to its owner and its loss is upon him). This explicitly assigns both profit and loss to the mortgagor, supporting the view that the mortgagee has no right to benefit.
This hadith is clearer in its dalalah and serves as a murajjih (preponderator) for the majority position.
3
Analyze the two qiyas objections
The majority argue the contested hadith contradicts analogy in two ways: (1) it permits a non-owner (the mortgagee) to use the property (riding, drinking) without the owner's permission, violating the principle that use follows ownership; (2) it makes the mortgagee liable only for expenses rather than the actual value of the benefit, which is inconsistent with compensation rules.
Qiyas objections show that the hadith conflicts with established legal principles and can be set aside.
4
Understand the final rejection via consensus and stronger traditions
Ibn 'Abd al-Barr summarizes the majority view: the hadith is rejected because it opposes principles upon which there is consensus and authentic traditions (e.g., the prohibition on milking another's livestock without permission). Thus, the hadith cannot stand against stronger evidence.
The authority of ijma and mutawatir/conclusive traditions overrides an ambiguous ahad hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْفَصْلُ الثَّانِي / الِاخْتِلَافُ فِي الْمَتْنِ

دَاوُدَ وَابْنِ مَاجَهْ (٣)، وَالتِّرْمِذِيِّ (٣)، وَأَبِي يَعْلَى (٤)، وَابْنِ الْجَارُودِ (٥)، وَالطَّحَاوِيِّ (٦)، وَابْنِ حِبَّانَ (٧)، وَالدَّارَقُطْنِيِّ (٨)، وَالْبَيْهَقِيِّ (٩)، وَالْبَغَوِيِّ (١٠). وَأَجَابَ الْجُمْهُورُ عَنْ هَذَا الْحَدِيثِ: بِأَنَّ الْحَدِيثَ لَمْ يَنْصَّ عَلَى تَعْيِينِ الْمُنْتَفِعِ هَلْ هُوَ الرَّاهِنُ أَمِ الْمُرْتَهِنُ فَإِنَّ الْحَدِيثَ مُحْتَمَلٌ لِكَوْنِ الْمُنْفِقِ هُوَ الرَّاهِنُ، وَيَسْتَخْدِمُ الْمَرْهُونَ بِحَقِّ مِلْكِهِ لَهُ. وَيُحْتَمَلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْمُرْتَهِنُ وَيَكُونَ انْتِفَاعُهُ عِوَضًا عَنْ نَفَقَتِهِ وَاسْتَدَلُّوا أَيْضًا بِمَا رَوَاهُ سَعِيدُ بْنُ الْمُسَيِّبِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «لَا يُغْلَقُ الرَّهْنُ - (ثَلَاثًا) - لِصَاحِبِهِ غُنْمُهُ وَعَلَيْهِ غُرْمُهُ» (١٢)، وَوَجْهُ الدَّلَالَةِ مِنَ الْحَدِيثِ: أَنَّ الْمَغْنَمَ وَالْمَغْرَمَ عَلَى الرَّاهِنِ، فَدَلَّ هَذَا عَلَى أَنَّ النَّفَقَةَ عَلَى الرَّهْنِ وَكَذَا النَّتَاجُ يَكُونُ لَهُ، وَوَجَبَ عَلَيْنَا أَنْ نُؤَوِّلَ الْحَدِيثَ الْمَاضِيَ. وَقَالُوا أَيْضًا إِنَّ هَذَا الْحَدِيثَ مُخَالِفٌ لِلْقِيَاسِ مِنْ وَجْهَيْنِ: الْأَوَّلُ: أَنَّ فِيهِ جَوَازَ الرُّكُوبِ وَالشُّرْبِ لِغَيْرِ مَالِكِ رَقَبَةِ الْعَيْنِ الْمَرْهُونَةِ مِنْ غَيْرِ إِذْنِ الْمَالِكِ. الثَّانِي: تَضْمِينُ الْمُرْتَهِنِ الْمُنْتَفِعِ بِالْعَيْنِ الْمَرْهُونَةِ عِوَضَ انْتِفَاعِهِ نَفَقَةً لَا قِيمَةً (١). وَقَالَ ابْنُ عَبْدِ الْبَرِّ: «هَذَا الْحَدِيثُ عِنْدَ جُمْهُورِ الْفُقَهَاءِ تَرُدُّهُ أُصُولٌ يُجْتَمَعُ عَلَيْهَا وَآثَارٌ ثَابِتَةٌ لَا يُخْتَلَفُ فِي صِحَّتِهَا، وَقَدْ أَجْمَعُوا أَنَّ لَيْسَ الرَّهْنُ وَظَهْرُهُ لِلرَّاهِنِ، وَلَا يَخْلُو أَنْ يَكُونَ احْتِلَابُ الْمُرْتَهِنِ لَهُ بِإِذْنِ الرَّاهِنِ، أَوْ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِهِ، فَإِنْ كَانَ بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِهِ فَفِي حَدِيثِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ : لَا يَحْتَلِبَنَّ أَحَدٌ مَاشِيَةَ أَحَدٍ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ (٢) مَا يَرُدُّهُ وَيَقْضِي بِهِ مُرْسَلًا.
Second Chapter / Differences in the Text

Dawood, Ibn Majah (3), al-Tirmidhi (3), Abu Ya'la (4), Ibn al-Jarud (5), al-Tahawi (6), Ibn Hibban (7), al-Daraqutni (8), al-Bayhaqi (9), and al-Baghawi (10). And the majority responded to this hadith: that the hadith did not specify who the beneficiary is, whether he is the mortgagor or the mortgagee, for the hadith is open to the possibility that the spender is the mortgagor, and he uses the mortgaged property by right of his ownership. And it is possible that it is the mortgagee and his benefit is in exchange for his expenses. And they also adduced as evidence what Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib narrated from Abu Hurayra, that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The pledge is not foreclosed (three times); to its owner belongs its profit and upon him is its loss' (12). And the indication from the hadith: that the profit and the loss are upon the mortgagor, so this indicates that the expense upon the pledge, and likewise the offspring, belongs to him, and we must interpret the previous hadith. And they also said that this hadith contradicts analogy in two ways: first: that it contains permission to ride and drink for other than the owner of the corpus of the mortgaged property without the owner's permission. Second: making the mortgagee who benefits from the mortgaged property liable for his benefit in exchange for expenses, not value (1). And Ibn 'Abd al-Barr said: 'This hadith, according to the majority of jurists, is rejected by principles upon which there is consensus and by established traditions whose authenticity is not disputed. And they have agreed that the pledge and its back are for the mortgagor, and it is inevitable that the mortgagee's milking of it is either with the permission of the mortgagor or without his permission. If it is without his permission, then in the hadith of Ibn 'Umar from the Prophet: 'Let no one milk the livestock of anyone except with his permission' (2) that which refutes it and he rules by it as a mursal narration.'
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage presents the response of the majority of scholars (جمهور الفقهاء) to a hadith that appears to permit the mortgagee (المرتهن) to benefit from the mortgaged property (الرهن) without the mortgagor's permission, with the benefit offsetting expenses. The majority argue that the hadith is ambiguous: it does not specify whether the spender is the mortgagor or the mortgagee. If the mortgagor is the spender, he uses the property by right of ownership; if the mortgagee, his benefit is merely compensation for expenses. To support their position, they cite another hadith, 'لا يغلق الرهن' (the pledge is not foreclosed), indicating that profit and loss belong to the mortgagor. They then claim that the originally cited hadith contradicts qiyas (analogy) in two ways: (1) it allows a non-owner (the mortgagee) to use the property (riding, drinking) without the owner's permission, and (2) it makes the mortgagee liable only for expenses rather than the actual value of the benefit. Finally, they quote Ibn 'Abd al-Barr, who rejects the hadith on the basis that it is opposed by agreed-upon principles and authentic traditions, including the prohibition on milking another's livestock without permission. This is a classic example of a dispute over a hadith's interpretation and its conflict with stronger evidence (qiyas, consensus). The Hanafi school, aligned with the majority, maintains that the mortgagee cannot use the mortgaged property without the mortgagor's consent.

Key Terms
الرَّهْن (al-rahin): The collateral or pledge given as security for a debt.
الغُنْمُ (al-ghunm): The profit or benefit derived from the mortgaged property (e.g., offspring, milk, rent).
الغُرْمُ (al-ghurm): The loss or liability (e.g., expenses, depreciation) associated with the mortgaged property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority in this passage, why is the contested hadith on mortgage benefits considered ambiguous?
A) It is narrated by weak transmitters.
B) It does not specify who the spender/beneficiary is.
C) It contradicts the Quran explicitly.
D) It has no supporting hadith.

Key Takeaway
When a hadith is ambiguous and contradicts stronger dalil (clearer hadith, qiyas, consensus), the majority sets it aside or reinterprets it to align with established principles.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Milk-Gorged Animal Dispute: Hanafi vs. Majority
Presenting two opinions on returning a defectively milk-gorged animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on returning a musarrah animal and identify the practical difference between the Hanafi and majority positions.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school does not permit returning a milk-gorged animal, unlike the majority.

This lesson examines a classic dispute where the Hanafi school diverges from the majority of jurists on whether a buyer can return an animal that was milk-stuffed to deceive. Understanding this ikhtilaf illustrates how different usul principles can lead to divergent rulings even when the same basic facts are present.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
The issue is whether a buyer can return a milk-gorged animal (musarrah) upon discovering the defect of tasriyah (intentional withholding of milk to deceive).
This is a dispute about khiyar al-ayb (option of defect) and whether tasriyah qualifies as a defect that gives the right of return.
2
State the Two Opinions
The text presents two opinions: (1) It is not permissible to return – the Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and a narration of Abu Yusuf). (2) It is permissible to return – the view of the majority including the Shafi'is.
Memorize the scholars associated with each opinion.
3
Analyze the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: Under the Hanafi view, the buyer must keep the animal and may only claim compensation for the milk. Under the majority view, the buyer may return the animal within three days.
This difference affects the buyer's rights and the seller's liability.
4
Consider the Absence of Proof
The passage does not present the proofs (adillah) for either view. It only records the ikhtilaf. This highlights that in usul al-fiqh, we often study disputes as examples of how different usul lead to different furu'.
Later lessons may delve into the specific hadith and qiyas arguments.

Second Model: Returning the milk-gorged ewe. The jurists differed regarding the permissibility of returning the milk-gorged ewe when the buyer discovers this defect after purchase, into two opinions: The first: It is not permissible to return the milk-gorged ewe, and this is the view of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf in one narration from him.
