Resolving Narrator Name Disagreements in Hadith Chains
Classifying four subdivisions of narrator-name disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four types of narrator-name disagreements and apply Ibn Hajar's method to evaluate whether a naming variation harms reliability.

Core Idea
Not every variation in a narrator's name harms a hadith; only when the difference affects reliability or meaning does it weaken the chain.

In the study of hadith chains, variations in narrator names are common. Ibn Hajar identifies four subdivisions to help scholars determine when such variations are harmless and when they indicate a deeper issue. Understanding these distinctions is essential for usul al-fiqh, as they affect the authenticity of traditions used in legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subdivision
Read the description of the four divisions: ambiguous vs. named, verbal variation only, explicit but differing context, and explicit but one reliable/weak. Determine which division a specific case falls into.
The first two divisions are generally harmless; the latter two require closer scrutiny.
2
Assess Genuine Contradiction
Ask whether the variation creates a real conflict in meaning or identity. If the ambiguous narrator is likely the same as the named one, or if the wording differs but meaning is identical, no contradiction exists.
Ibn Hajar emphasizes that superficial differences do not constitute idhtirab.
3
Apply Reliability Principle
If the narrator in the explicit version is thiqah (reliable), the narration is not harmed by an ambiguous version. The key is the trustworthiness of the clearly identified narrator.
This follows the Hanafi principle that clear, reliable information overrides ambiguity.
4
Recognize Harmful Variations
In the third and fourth divisions, if the explicit differences affect identity or if one narrator is weak, the hadith may be weakened. Also consider if the difference implies irsal (interruption).
Such cases require further investigation into the narrators' status and chain continuity.
5
Evaluate the Idhtirab Example
Consider Ibn Hajar's critique of Ibn al-Salah's example: the hadith of Abu Amr ibn Hurayth. Since the variations are only in name/lineage and not in the chain itself, it is not genuine idhtirab.
This illustrates how careful classification prevents misjudgment of hadith strength.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النوع السادس: وهو الاختلاف في اسم الرَّاوِي ونسبه فَهُوَ عَلَى أقسام أربعة:
القسم الأول: أن يبهم في طريق وَيُسَمَّى في أخرى، فالظاهر أن هَذَا لا تعارض فيهِ؛ لأَنَّهُ يَكُون المُبْهَم في إحدى الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ هُوَ المعين في الأخرى، وعلى تقدير أن يَكُون غيره، فَلا تضر رِوَايَة من سماه وعرفه إذا كَانَ ثِقَة - رواية من أبهمه.
القِسْم الثَّانِي: أن يَكُون الاختلاف في العبارة فَقَط ، والمَعْنَى بِهَا في الكل واحد، فإِنَّ مِثْل هَذَا لا يعد اختلافاً - أيضاً - ولا يضر إذا كَانَ الرَّاوِي ثِقَة.
قُلْتُ القائل ابن حجر وبهذا يتبين أن تمثيل المصنف (۱) للمضطرب بحديث أبي عمرو بن حريث لَيْسَ بمستقيم انتهى.
القسم الثالث: أن يقع التصريح باسم الرَّاوِي ونسبه لكن مع الاختلاف في سياق ذلِكَ» (٢). ثُمَّ ساق مثالاً لِذلِكَ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «القِسْم الرابع: أن يقع التصريح به من غير اختلاف لَكِنْ يَكُون ذَلِكَ من متفقين: أحدهما ثِقَة، والآخر ضَعِيف. أو أحدهما مستلزم الاتصال، والآخر الإرسال كما قدمناه (۳).
As for the sixth type: it is the disagreement in the name and lineage of the narrator, and it is of four divisions: The first division: that he is left ambiguous in one chain and named in another; the apparent is that there is no contradiction in this, because the one left ambiguous in one of the two narrations is the one specified in the other. And if it were another, then the narration of the one who named him and identified him, if he is reliable, does not harm the narration of the one who left him ambiguous. The second division: that the disagreement is only in the wording, and the meaning by it in all is one; then such a thing is not considered a disagreement, also, and it does not harm if the narrator is reliable. I say (the speaker is Ibn Hajar): and by this it becomes clear that the example given by the author (Ibn al-Salah) for the confused hadith, the hadith of Abu Amr ibn Hurayth, is not correct. End. The third division: that the narrator's name and lineage are explicitly stated, but with disagreement in the context of that. Then he gave an example for that, then he said: The fourth division: that the explicit statement occurs without disagreement, but that is from two agreed-upon narrators: one reliable, the other weak; or one requiring connection, the other requiring interruption as we presented.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage is a classification by Ibn Hajar (as quoted) of the sixth type of disagreement in hadith chains: differences in the name and lineage of the narrator. It is part of a broader discussion on how variations in chains affect juristic differences. The author presents four subdivisions, each addressing a different scenario. The first deals with ambiguity versus specification: if a narrator is unnamed in one chain but named in another, it does not create a contradiction because the ambiguous one is likely the same named person; even if not, the clear narration from a reliable narrator is not harmed by the ambiguous one. The second covers mere verbal differences where the meaning is identical — such differences are not considered harmful. Ibn Hajar then critiques Ibn al-Salah's example of a confused hadith (idhtirab) concerning Abu Amr ibn Hurayth, arguing it does not fit the criteria. The third and fourth subdivisions address explicit but contextually differing statements and cases where the difference stems from one reliable and one weak narrator, or from whether the chain is connected or interrupted. Each subdivision preserves the principle that substantive disagreement only harms when the narrator is unreliable or the difference affects meaning.

Key Terms
المضطرب (al-mudtarib): A hadith that is confused due to irreconcilable differences in chain or text, often weak
الإرسال (al-irsal): A chain where a narrator is omitted, typically a Successor quoting the Prophet directly
المبهم (al-mubham): An unnamed narrator, left ambiguous in the chain

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first subdivision of type six, if a narrator is ambiguous in one chain and named in another, what is the ruling?
A) The hadith is rejected due to contradiction.
B) The ambiguous and named narrators are considered different, causing weakness.
C) The hadith is sound because the ambiguous one is presumed to be the named one.
D) The hadith is accepted only if the ambiguous chain is also from a reliable narrator.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, naming variations are not automatically harmful; the key is whether the narrator's identity is known and reliable.

Understanding Idhtirab in Sanad: Conflict of Wasl and Irsal
Introducing idhtirab in chain and defining conflict between wasl and irsal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify idhtirab in a hadith chain and distinguish the conflict between wasl and irsal, and explain why the Hanafi school prioritizes chain analysis.

Core Idea
The authenticity of a hadith often hinges on whether its chain is connected (wasl) or broken (irsal); resolving this conflict is key to deriving fiqh rulings.

Hadith chains are the backbone of Islamic legal derivation. When a hadith is narrated with both a connected and a broken chain, scholars must determine which version is stronger. This lesson introduces the concept of idhtirab (confusion/irregularity) in the chain, focusing on the first type: the conflict between wasl (connection) and irsal (omission of the companion). Understanding this conflict is crucial for appreciating how the Hanafi school, with its acceptance of mursal from reliable narrators, derives rulings that may differ from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Define Idhtirab and Its Two Domains
Understand that idhtirab is an irreconcilable variation in either the chain (sanad) or the text (matn). The author prioritizes chain because it is more fundamental and has more branches.
Idhtirab makes a hadith weak if the variants cannot be reconciled, but Hanafi scholars tolerate it if one version can be preferred via tarjih.
2
Recognize the Importance of the Chain
Reflect on why early scholars preserved hundreds of thousands of chains. The chain determines authenticity, and the strongest chain is preferred for deriving rulings.
The author quotes al-`Iraqi's poetic classification of hadith into authentic, good, and weak.
3
Identify the Conflict Between Wasl and Irsal
Wasl means a fully connected chain (companion to Prophet). Irsal means a chain where a successor skips the companion. When a hadith is narrated both ways, a conflict arises. Scholars must decide which version is stronger.
Connection (ittisal) is the first condition for authenticity. Hanafi school accepts mursal if the mursil is reliable and the hadith is corroborated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما كَانَ الاضطراب يقع في السَّنَد والمثن رأيت أن أفضل الاضطراب الواقع السَّنَد؛ لأَنَّهُ الأهم والأكثر تشعباً مَعَ بيان أمثلته، ثُمَّ أسوق أثر ذَلِكَ في الفُقَهَاء ثُمَّ الكلام عن اضطراب المثن. وَقَدْ جعلت كلاً مِنْهُمَا فِي نَوع مستقل:
القسم الأول
الاضطراب في السند
بالنظر لما تمتع به الإسناد من أهمية في حياة الأمة الإسلامية كونه من أهم خصائصها، فَقَدْ حضي بالاهتمام من حَيْثُ الحفاظ عَلَيْهِ والتنقير والتفتيش عن صحيحه وضَعِيفه، وَقَدِ اهتم السلف الصالح بحفظ مئات الألوف من الأسانيد، وبينوا قويها من سقيمها حَتَّى خرجوا لَنَا ببحوث ونتائج قل نظيرها. والسند كَمَا يَكُون مِنْهُ الصَّحِيح والأصح ، ففيه الضَّعِيف والمعلول، والذي تدخله العلة من الأسانيد كَثِير لَيْسَ بقليل، وَقَدْ رأيت أن أحسن من صنفها الحافظ العلائي). وسأفصل الكلام عن كُلّ نَوْع بكلام مستقِل
النوع الأول : تعارض الوصل والإرسال
الوصل هنا بمعنى الاتصال، والاتصال هُوَ أحد الشروط الأساسية في صحة الحَدِيث بَلْ هُوَ ،أولها، قال العراقي في نظمه:
إلى صَحِيْحٍ وَضَعِيْفَ وَحَسَنْ وَأَهْلُ هَذَا الشَّأْنِ قَسَّمُوا السُّنَنْ
And since idhtirab occurs in the chain and the text, I saw fit to give precedence to idhtirab occurring in the chain, because it is more important and more ramified, along with showing its examples. Then I will bring the effect of that upon the jurists, then discussion about idhtirab in the text. I have made each of them in an independent type: First Section: Idhtirab in the Chain. Considering the importance that the chain has enjoyed in the life of the Islamic nation, being one of its most important characteristics, it received attention in terms of preserving it, scrutinizing it, and investigating its authentic and weak. The pious predecessors cared for preserving hundreds of thousands of chains, and they distinguished their strong from their weak, until they produced for us research and results rarely matched. And the chain, just as it includes the authentic and the more authentic, so too it includes the weak and the defective, and the chains that have a defect are many not few. I have seen that the best of those who classified them is al-Hafiz al-`Ala'i. And I will detail the discussion of each type in independent speech. The first type: Conflict between wasl and irsal. Wasl here means connection, and connection is one of the basic conditions for the authenticity of hadith, indeed it is the first of them. Al-`Iraqi said in his versification: 'They divided the sunan into authentic, weak, and good, and the people of this craft...'
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on idhtirab (confusion/irregularity) in hadith chains, which is a crucial topic for both hadith criticism and fiqh differences. The author prioritizes chain over text because the chain is more fundamental and branches into many subtypes. He emphasizes the unparalleled care of early scholars in preserving and evaluating chains. The first type of idhtirab in the chain is the conflict between wasl (connected chain) and irsal (broken chain). Connection (ittisal) is the primary condition for a hadith's authenticity. The passage quotes al-`Iraqi's famous poetic summary of hadith classification (into sahih, hasan, da`if). This sets the stage for detailed analysis of how such conflicts affect juristic rulings, though the passage cuts off before reaching the resolution. The implication is that when a chain is narrated both connected and broken, scholars must weigh which version is stronger, and this directly impacts the derivation of legal rules.

Key Terms
الاضطراب (al-idhtirab): Irreconcilable variation in the chain or text that prevents preferring one version over another, often leading to weakness
الوصل (al-wasl): A chain that is fully connected (marfu` or muttasil) from narrator to the Prophet
الإرسال (al-irsal): A chain where a successor omits the companion, saying 'the Prophet said' directly

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author choose to discuss idhtirab in the chain before idhtirab in the text?
A) Because chain is easier to analyze.
B) Because chain is more important and has more branches.
C) Because jurists only care about the chain.
D) Because text variations are irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
Conflict between wasl and irsal is the first type of idhtirab in the chain; resolving it requires weighing reliability and has direct impact on fiqh rulings.

Definition of Mursal and the Five Opinions on Mursal vs. Muttasil
Defines mursal/munqati' and lists five opinions on mursal vs muttasil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the precise definition of mursal and its relationship to discontinuity, and list the five scholarly opinions on preferring mursal or muttasil narrations.

Core Idea
A mursal hadith is not automatically weak; when both mursal and muttasil exist, scholars differ on preference based on deeper criticism.

In Hanafi usul, understanding hadith classifications is essential for deriving rulings. This passage introduces the term mursal (a hadith where a Successor omits the companion) and explains that continuity is a condition for authenticity. However, when a hadith appears in both mursal and muttasil forms, scholars hold varying opinions on which to prefer. The author also reflects on the practice of early scholars, noting that there is no universal rule—preference depends on contextual preponderances.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish mursal from munqati‘
Identify the difference: early usage used mursal for any break, but later scholars restricted it to a break at the end (Successor omitting companion). Understand that munqati‘ is a broader term for any discontinuity.
The passage marks this terminological shift.
2
Identify the five opinions on preferring mursal or muttasil
List each opinion: (1) prefer muttasil because it is an addition by a reliable narrator; (2) prefer mursal; (3) prefer the more memorizing narrator; (4) consideration of the greater number of narrators; (5) suspend judgment (equal).
These opinions reflect different methodological stances in hadith criticism.
3
Analyze the author's conclusion
Understand that the author criticizes later scholars for attempting a universal rule. Early scholars (mutqaddimun) judged case-by-case based on contextual preponderances. This highlights the complexity of usul al-fiqh in dealing with mixed chains.
The author emphasises that deep expertise in hadith is required to make such preferences.

الفصل الثالث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن والاتصال في السَّنَد لا يشترط أن يَكُون في طبقة وَاحِدَة فَقَطْ بَلْ يشترط أن يَكُون من أول السَّنَد إلى آخره؛ فإذا اختل الاتصال في مَوْضِع من المواضع سمي منقطعاً، وَكَانَ يطلق عَلَيْهِ في القرون المتقدمة مرسلا (3) ، ثُمَّ استقر الاصطلاح بعد عَلَى أن المُرْسَل هُوَ: ما أضافه التابعي إلى النبي . ولما كَانَ الاتصال شرطاً للصحة فالانقطاع ينافي الصحة، إذن الانقطاع أمارة من أمارات الضعف؛ لأن الضَّعِيف مَا فَقَدْ شرطاً من شروط الصحة (4). والانقطاع قَدْ يَكُون في أول السَّنَد، وَقَدْ يَكُون في آخره، وَقَدْ يَكُون في وسطه، وَقَدْ يَكُون الانقطاع براو واحد أو أكثر. وكل ذَلِكَ من نَوْع الانقطاع، والذي يعنينا الكلام عَلَيْهِ هنا هُوَ الكلام عن الانقطاع في آخر الإسناد، وَهُوَ مَا يُسَمَّى بالمرسل عِنْدَ المتأخرين، وَهُوَ مَا أضافه التابعي إلى النبي ). ومما ينبغي التنبيه عليه أن للعُلَماء في تعريف المُرْسَل وبيان صوره مناقشات.
لِذلِكَ فإن الحَدِيث إذا روي مرسلاً ،مرة، وروي مرة أخرى موصولاً، فهذا يعد الأمور الَّتِي تعلُّ بِهَا بَعْض الأحاديث، ومن العلماء من لا يعدُّ ذَلِكَ علة، وتفصيل من الأقوال في ذَلِكَ عَلَى النحو الآتي: الثّقة ). القَوْل الأول: ترجيح الرّوَايَة الموصولة عَلَى الرِّوَايَة المرسلة؛ لأنه من قبيل زيادة القَوْل الثَّانِي: ترجيح الرّوَايَة المرسلة (٢). (†) القَوْل الثالث: الترجيح للأحفظ (۳). القَوْل الرابع: الاعتبار لأكثر الرواة عدداً). القَوْل الخامس: التساوي بَيْنَ الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ والتوقف(). هَذَا ما وجدته من أقوال لأهل العِلم في هذه المسألة، وَهِيَ أقوال متباينة مختلفة، وقَدْ أمعنت النظر في صنيع المتقدمين أصحاب القرون الأولى، وأجلت النظر كثيراً في أحكامهم على الأحاديث التي اختلف في وصلها وإرسالها، فوجدت بوناً شاسعاً بَيْنَ قَوْل المتأخرين وصنيع المتقدمين، إذ إن المتقدمين لا يحكمون على الحَدِيث أول وهلة، وَلَمْ يجعلوا ذَلِكَ تَحْتَ قاعدة كلية تطرد عَلَيْهَا جَمِيع الاختلافات، وَقَدْ ظهر لي من خلال دراسة مجموعة من الأحاديث التي اختلف في وصلها وإرسالها : أن الترجيح لا يندرج تَحْتَ قاعدة كلية، لكن يختلف الحال حسب المرجحات والقرائن، فتارة ترجح الرّوَايَة المرسلة وتارة ترجح الرّوَايَة الموصولة. وهذه المرجحات كثيرة يعرفها من اشتغل بالحديث دراية ورواية وأكثر التصحيح والتعليل، وحفظ جملة كبيرة من الأحاديث، وتمكن في علم الرِّجَال وعرف دقائق هَذَا الفن وخفاياه حَتَّى صار الحَدِيث أمراً ملازماً لَه مختلطاً بدمه ولحمه.
Chapter Three / Disagreement in chain and text. Continuity in the chain is not required only in one generation, but it is required from the beginning of the chain to its end. If continuity is broken in any place, it is called munqati‘. In earlier centuries it was also called mursal. Then the terminology settled that mursal is what a Successor attributes to the Prophet. Since continuity is a condition for authenticity, discontinuity contradicts authenticity. Thus discontinuity is an indicator of weakness, because the weak is what lacks a condition of authenticity. Discontinuity may be at the beginning of the chain, at its end, in its middle, and it may be by one or more narrators. All of that is a type of discontinuity. What concerns us here is discontinuity at the end of the chain, which is called mursal by later scholars, and it is what a Successor attributes to the Prophet. It should be noted that there are discussions among scholars about the definition of mursal and its forms. Therefore, if a hadith is narrated once as mursal and another time as muttasil, this is among the issues that affect some hadiths, and some scholars do not consider that a defect. The detailed opinions are as follows: First opinion: preferring the muttasil narration over the mursal because it is an addition by a reliable narrator. Second opinion: preferring the mursal narration. Third opinion: preference for the more memorizing. Fourth opinion: consideration of the greater number of narrators. Fifth opinion: equal between the two narrations and suspension. This is what I found of the scholars' opinions on this issue, and they are diverse differing opinions. I deeply examined the practice of early scholars and carefully considered their judgments on hadiths where there was disagreement on connection and sending, and I found a vast gap between the statement of later scholars and the practice of early scholars. The early scholars did not judge the hadith at first glance, nor did they put that under a universal rule applying to all differences. It became clear to me through studying a group of hadiths that differed in their connection and sending that preference does not fall under a universal rule, but the case varies according to preponderances and indications. Sometimes the mursal narration is preferred, sometimes the muttasil narration is preferred. These preponderances are many, known by one who is engaged in hadith in knowledge and transmission, extensively corrected and criticized, memorized a large number of hadiths, mastered the science of narrators, and knows the subtleties and secrets of this art until hadith became a matter inherent to him mixed with his blood and flesh.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage from a work on the impact of hadith chains and texts on juristic disagreement begins by defining two key terms: mursal and munqati‘. The author explains that a chain must be continuous from beginning to end; if broken anywhere it is munqati‘. In earlier usage, such breaks were also called mursal, but later the term mursal was restricted to a chain where a Successor (tabi‘i) attributes a saying directly to the Prophet, omitting the companion. This discontinuity undermines the hadith's authenticity because continuity is a condition for authenticity. However, when a hadith exists in both a mursal form and a connected (muttasil) form, scholars differed on which to prefer. The author lists five opinions: (1) prefer the muttasil because it is an addition by a reliable narrator; (2) prefer the mursal; (3) prefer the more reliable narrator (the one with stronger memory); (4) consider the majority of narrators; (5) suspend judgment considering both equal. The author then reflects on the practice of early scholars (mutqaddimun) and concludes that there is no universal rule; preference depends on various contextual factors known only to those deeply immersed in hadith criticism. This highlights that fiqh rulings derived from such hadiths may vary based on the strength of the chain, which is a usul issue.

Key Terms
المرسل (al-mursal): A hadith where a Successor directly attributes a saying to the Prophet without mentioning the companion.
المنقطع (al-munqati‘): A hadith whose chain has a break at any point, not necessarily at the end.
الموصول (al-muttasil): A hadith with a continuous chain from narrator to Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the precise definition of 'mursal' according to later scholars?
A) Any hadith with a break in the chain at any point.
B) A hadith that a Successor attributes directly to the Prophet without mentioning the companion.
C) A hadith narrated by a weak narrator.
D) A hadith that is rejected immediately.

Key Takeaway
The classification of a hadith as mursal does not automatically determine its strength; when both mursal and muttasil versions exist, preference depends on contextual indicators and the practice of early scholars.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Preference Between Mursal and Muttasil Narrations
Listing opinions on preferring mursal vs muttasil hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five opinions on preferring mursal vs muttasil narrations and evaluate the Hanafi methodological stance that there is no universal rule.

Core Idea
Mursal vs Muttasil: no universal rule; each hadith is judged on its own preponderating factors.

In usul al-fiqh, the conflict between a mursal and a muttasil narration of the same hadith presents a methodological challenge. Hanafi scholars, drawing from early practice, reject a blanket preference and instead weigh each case individually. This lesson explores the five scholarly opinions and the principle of case-by-case evaluation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize when a hadith is narrated both mursal (with missing link) and muttasil (fully connected). This creates a need to determine which narration should be preferred in fiqh derivation.
This is a common scenario in hadith criticism.
2
List the five opinions
Memorize the five opinions: (1) prefer muttasil because of ziyada al-thiqah, (2) prefer mursal, (3) prefer the more retentive narrator, (4) consider the greater number of narrators, (5) suspend judgment.
Each opinion has its own supporting scholars.
3
Understand the Hanafi position
The author argues that early scholars did not apply a universal rule; instead, they evaluated preponderating factors (murajjihaat) like memory, number, and length of association with the teacher.
This rejects a one-size-fits-all approach.
4
Apply to the example hadith
Examine the hadith of doubt in prayer narrated by Malik. Note how different scholars may prefer mursal or muttasil versions, leading to different fiqh rulings.
The thamarah al-khilaf is in the number of prostrations and rak'ahs.
5
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if muttasil is preferred, the ruling includes an extra rak'ah; if mursal is preferred, the ruling may differ (e.g., only prostrations).
This illustrates how usul differences affect fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث الاختلاف في السند والمتن
لِذلِكَ فإن الحَدِيث إذا روي مرسلاً، مرة، وروي مرة أخرى موصولاً، فهذا يعد الأمور الَّتِي تعلُّ بِهَا بَعْض الأحاديث، ومن العلماء من لا يعدُّ ذَلِكَ علة، وتفصيل من الأقوال في ذَلِكَ عَلَى النحو الآتي:
القَوْل الأول: ترجيح الرّوَايَة الموصولة عَلَى الرِّوَايَة المرسلة؛ لأنه من قبيل زيادة الثّقة ).
القَوْل الثَّانِي: ترجيح الرّوَايَة المرسلة (٢).
القَوْل الثالث: الترجيح للأحفظ (۳).
القَوْل الرابع: الاعتبار لأكثر الرواة عدداً).
القَوْل الخامس: التساوي بَيْنَ الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ والتوقف().
هَذَا ما وجدته من أقوال لأهل العِلم في هذه المسألة، وَهِيَ أقوال متباينة مختلفة، وقَدْ أمعنت النظر في صنيع المتقدمين أصحاب القرون الأولى، وأجلت النظر كثيراً في أحكامهم على الأحاديث التي اختلف في وصلها وإرسالها، فوجدت بوناً شاسعاً بَيْنَ قَوْل المتأخرين وصنيع المتقدمين، إذ إن المتقدمين لا يحكمون على الحَدِيث أول وهلة، وَلَمْ يجعلوا ذَلِكَ تَحْتَ قاعدة كلية تطرد عَلَيْهَا جَمِيع الاختلافات، وَقَدْ ظهر لي من خلال دراسة مجموعة من الأحاديث التي اختلف في وصلها وإرسالها : أن الترجيح لا يندرج تَحْتَ قاعدة كلية، لكن يختلف الحال حسب المرجحات والقرائن، فتارة ترجح الرّوَايَة المرسلة وتارة ترجح الرّوَايَة الموصولة. وهذه المرجحات كثيرة يعرفها من اشتغل بالحديث دراية ورواية وأكثر التصحيح والتعليل، وحفظ جملة كبيرة من الأحاديث، وتمكن في علم الرِّجَال وعرف دقائق هَذَا الفن وخفاياه حَتَّى صار الحَدِيث أمراً ملازماً لَه مختلطاً بدمه ولحمه.
(۱) وهذا هُوَ الَّذِي صححه الخطيب في الكفاية (٥۸۱ ت ، ٤١١ه) وَقَالَ ابن الصَّلاح في مَعْرِفَة أنواع علم الحديث: ٦٥، ١٥٥ طبعتنا : (فما صححه هُوَ الصَّحِيح في الفقه وأصوله». وانظر: المدخل: ٤٠، وقواطع الأدلة ٣٦٨/١-٣٦٩، والمحصول ،۲۲۹/۲ وجامع الأصول ۱۷۰/۱ وكشف الأسرار للبخاري ،۲/۳ ، وجمع الجوامع ١٢٦/٢ وَقَدْ نسب الإمام النَّوَوِي هَذَا القَوْل للمحققين من أهل الحَدِيث شرح صحيح مسلم ١٤٥/١ ثُمَّ إن هَذَا القَوْلَ هُوَ الَّذِي صححه العراقي في شرح التبصرة ١٧٤/١٨، ٢٢٧/١ طبعتنا.
(۲) هَذَا القَوْل عزاه الخطيب للأكثر من أهل الحَدِيث الكفاية: ٥٨٠ت، ٤١١ هـ). (۳) هُوَ ظاهر كلام الإمام أحمد كَمَا ذكر ذَلِكَ ابن رجب الحنبلي في شرحه لعلل الترمذي ٦٣١/٢. (٤) عزاه الحَاكِم في المدخل: ٤٠ لأئمة الحَدِيث، وانظر: مقدمة جامع الأصول ۱۷۰/۱، والنكت الوفية ١/١٣٦.
(٥) هَذَا القَوْل ذكره الشبكي في جمع الجوامع ١٢٤/٢ وَلَمْ ينسبه لأحد.
ومن المرجحات: مزيد الحفظ، وكثرة العدد، وطول الملازمة للشيخ. وَقَدْ يختلف جهابذة الحديث في الحكم عَلَى حَدِيث من الأحاديث، فمنهم: من يرجح الرِّوَايَة المرسلة ومنهم من يرجح الرِّوَايَة الموصولة، ومنهم من يتوقف. وسأسوق نماذج لِذلِكَ مَعَ بيان أثر ذَلِكَ في اختلاف الفُقَهَاء.
مثال ذَلِكَ رِوَايَة مَالِك بن أنس، عن زيد بن أسلم)، عن عطاء بن يسار (۲)؛ أن رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إذا شك أحدكم في صلاته فَلَمْ يدرِ كم صلى أثلاثاً أم أربعاً؟ فليصل رَكْعَة، وليسجد سجدتين وَهُوَ جالس قَبْلَ التسليم، فإِن كَانَتِ الرَّكْعَةِ الَّتِي صلی خامسة شفعها بهاتين السجدتين، وإن كَانَتْ رابعة فالسجدتين ترغيم للشيطان». هَذَا الحَدِيث رَواهُ هكذا عن مَالِك جَمَاعَة الرواة مِنْهُمْ:
١. سويد بن سعيد (۳).
. عبد الرزاق بن همام.
عبد الله بن مسلمة القعنبي (٥)
عَبْد الله بن وهب
٥. عُثْمَان بن عُمَر (۲).
٦. مُحَمَّد بن الحَسَن الشيباني .
أبو مصعب الزُّهْرِيّ).
يَحْيَى بن يَحْيَى الليثي (۱۰)
Chapter Three: Differences in Chain and Text. Therefore, if a hadith is narrated as mursal one time and narrated as muttasil another time, this is among the matters that affect some hadiths. Some scholars do not consider that a defect. The detailed opinions on that are as follows: First opinion: Preferring the muttasil narration over the mursal narration because it is a type of ziyada of a trustworthy [narrator]. Second opinion: Preferring the mursal narration. Third opinion: Preferring the more retentive [narrator]. Fourth opinion: Considering the greater number of narrators. Fifth opinion: Considering the two narrations equal and suspending judgment. These are the opinions I found from scholars on this issue, and they are divergent and different. I have deeply considered the practice of the early scholars (the first generations) and examined their rulings on hadiths that differed regarding being connected or disconnected. I found a wide gap between the statements of the later scholars and the practice of the early scholars. Indeed, the early scholars did not judge a hadith at first glance, nor did they make that under a universal rule applied to all differences. It has become clear to me from studying a group of hadiths that differed in being connected or disconnected that the preference does not fall under a universal rule, but the situation varies according to the preponderating factors and indications. Sometimes the mursal narration is preferred, and sometimes the muttasil narration is preferred. These preponderating factors are many, known only to those who have engaged in hadith both in theory and narration, who have extensively practiced correction and criticism, memorized a large number of hadiths, become proficient in the science of narrators, and known the subtleties and hidden aspects of this art until hadith becomes something inseparable from them, mixed with their blood and flesh. Among the preponderating factors: greater memory, higher number [of narrators], and longer association with the shaykh. And the experts of hadith may differ in their judgment on a particular hadith: some prefer the mursal narration, some prefer the muttasil narration, and some suspend judgment. I will present examples of that with an explanation of its effect on the differences among jurists. An example of that is the narration of Malik ibn Anas from Zaid ibn Aslam from Ata' ibn Yasar that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'If any of you doubts his prayer and does not know whether he prayed three or four rak'ahs, let him pray one rak'ah and then prostrate two prostrations while sitting before the taslim. If the rak'ah he prayed was a fifth, he makes it even with these two prostrations; if it was a fourth, then the two prostrations are to humiliate the devil.' This hadith was narrated from Malik by a group of narrators, including: (1) Suwayd ibn Sa'id, (2) Abd al-Razzaq ibn Hammam, (3) Abdullah ibn Maslama al-Qa'nabi, (4) Abdullah ibn Wahb, (5) Uthman ibn Umar, (6) Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, (7) Abu Musab al-Zuhri, (8) Yahya ibn Yahya al-Laythi.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is from a chapter on differences in chain (sanad) and text (matn) of hadith. The author addresses the issue of a hadith being transmitted sometimes as mursal (with a missing link) and sometimes as muttasil (fully connected). He lists five scholarly opinions on how to prefer one over the other. The first opinion prefers the muttasil because it includes an addition from a trustworthy narrator (ziyada al-thiqa). The second prefers the mursal. The third prefers the narrator with the stronger memory. The fourth gives weight to the greater number of narrators. The fifth suspends judgment, treating them as equal. The author then shares his own conclusion after studying the practice of early hadith scholars: there is no universal rule. Instead, each case must be evaluated based on various preponderating factors (murajjihaat) such as the narrator's memory, the number of narrators, and the length of association with the teacher. He emphasizes that early scholars did not mechanically apply a single rule but judged each hadith individually. He then gives an example: the hadith about doubt in prayer (shukr) narrated by Malik ibn Anas. This hadith was transmitted by several narrators from Malik, and the chain is given. The implication for fiqh is that the ruling on the prayer of the one who doubts (shakk) can differ depending on which narration is considered stronger. For instance, the Hanafi school may have a different ruling compared to others based on the preference of the muttasil or mursal narration. The author does not state the final fiqh ruling here but sets up the discussion of how this hadith dispute affects fiqh differences.

Key Terms
مرسل (mursal): A hadith with a missing link in the chain, typically a Successor narrating directly from the Prophet without mentioning the Companion.
موصول (muttasil): A hadith with a continuous chain of narrators from the Prophet to the compiler.
زيادة الثقة (ziyadat al-thiqah): An addition in a narration from a trustworthy narrator that is not present in the narrations of other trustworthy narrators.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what should be the basis for preferring a mursal or muttasil narration?
A) Always prefer the muttasil because it has an additional trustworthy narrator.
B) Always prefer the mursal because it is more widespread.
C) There is no universal rule; preference depends on various preponderating factors.
D) Prefer the narration with the older chain.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the preference between mursal and muttasil narrations is not governed by a single rule but by the totality of preponderating factors as practiced by early scholars.

Tarjih Between Mursal and Muttasil: The Doubt-in-Prayer Hadith
Usul dispute over mursal vs muttasil of the doubt-in-prayer hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi tarjih principle to resolve conflicts between mursal and muttasil narrations, and explain why corroboration outweighs mere numerical majority.

Core Idea
Corroboration (shawahid) can outweigh numerical majority in tarjih of hadith.

This passage presents a classic usul al-fiqh problem: when a hadith is transmitted both as mursal and muttasil, which version is stronger? The muhaqqiqun apply the principle of tarjih, weighing not only quantity but also quality of corroboration. Here, the Hanafi approach demonstrates that tarjih by shawahid (supporting narrations) can override the mere numerical advantage of the mursal version.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two variant chains
Distinguish the mursal chain (Malik → Zayd → 'Ata, without Companion) from the muttasil chain (Malik → Zayd → 'Ata → Abu Sa'id, with Companion).
2
Note the number of narrators for each
The mursal version has eight narrators from Malik; the muttasil version has two narrators directly from Malik, but five other narrators corroborate from the same chain.
Total narrators supporting muttasil (including corroborators): at least seven.
3
Observe the tarjih factor
The five corroborating narrators (Fulayh, 'Abd al-'Aziz, etc.) are reliable and transmit from the same teacher (Zayd ibn Aslam) as Malik, strengthening the muttasil version.
These are shawahid that reinforce the muttasil chain.
4
Apply the Hanafi tarjih principle
In Hanafi usul, tarjih by shawahid (corroboration) outweighs mere numerical majority of a single chain, especially when the corroborators are trustworthy.
The principle is: 'al-tarjih bi al-shawahid muqaddam 'ala al-tarjih bi al-'adad.'
5
Derive the fiqh implication
The preferred muttasil version makes the ruling to add a rak'ah and two sujud for doubt a stronger proof, supporting the Hanafi fiqh position.

مثال ذلك رواية مالك بن أنس، عن زيد بن أسلم، عن عطاء بن يسار؛ أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «إذا شك أحدكم في صلاته فلم يدر كم صلى أثلاثاً أم أربعاً؟ فليصل ركعة، وليسجد سجدتين وهو جالس قبل التسليم، فإن كانت الركعة التي صلى خامسة شفعها بهاتين السجدتين، وإن كانت رابعة فالسجدتين ترغيم للشيطان». هذا الحديث رواه هكذا عن مالك جماعة الرواة منهم: ١. سويد بن سعيد. ٢. عبد الرزاق بن همام. ٣. عبد الله بن مسلمة القعنبي. ٤. عبد الله بن وهب. ٥. عثمان بن عمر. ٦. محمد بن الحسن الشيباني. ٧. أبو مصعب الزهري. ٨. يحيى بن يحيى الليثي. فَهؤلاء ثمانيتهم رووه عن مالك، عن زيد بن أسلم، عن عطاء بن يسار، به مرسلاً. والحديث رواه الوليد بن مسلم، ويحيى بن راشد المازني عن مالك، عن زيد بن أسلم، عن عطاء بن يسار، عن أبي سعيد به - متصلاً -. هكذا اختلف على الإمام مالك بن أنس في وصل هذا الحديث وإرساله والراجح فيه الوصل، وإن كان رواة الإرسال أكثر وهو الصحيح من رواية مالك، لما يأتي: وهو أن الإمام مالكاً توبع على وصل هذا الحديث: فقد رواه فليح بن سليمان، وعبد العزيز بن عبد الله بن أبي سلمة، وسليمان بن بلال، ومحمد بن مطرف، ومحمد بن عجلان - خمسهم - رووه عن زيد بن أسلم، عن عطاء بن يسار، عن أبي سعيد الخدري، به متصلاً. وقد ذكر ابن عبد البر في التمهيد غيرهم هشام بن سعد وداود بن قيس، ولم أقف على رواياتهم.
An example of that is the narration of Malik ibn Anas, from Zayd ibn Aslam, from 'Ata' ibn Yasar, that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'If one of you doubts in his prayer and does not know whether he prayed three or four rak'ahs, let him pray one rak'ah and prostrate two prostrations while sitting before the taslim. If the rak'ah he prayed was the fifth, he makes it even with these two prostrations; if it was the fourth, the two prostrations are a humiliation for Satan.' This hadith was narrated from Malik by a group of narrators, among them: 1. Suwayd ibn Sa'id, 2. 'Abd al-Razzaq ibn Hammam, 3. 'Abd Allah ibn Maslamah al-Qa'nabi, 4. 'Abd Allah ibn Wahb, 5. 'Uthman ibn 'Umar, 6. Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, 7. Abu Mus'ab al-Zuhri, 8. Yahya ibn Yahya al-Laythi. These eight narrated it from Malik, from Zayd ibn Aslam, from 'Ata' ibn Yasar, as mursal. And the hadith was narrated by al-Walid ibn Muslim and Yahya ibn Rashid al-Mazini from Malik, from Zayd ibn Aslam, from 'Ata' ibn Yasar, from Abu Sa'id - as muttasil. Thus there is disagreement over Imam Malik ibn Anas regarding the connection and disconnection of this hadith, and the preferred (opinion) is connection, even though the narrators of the mursal are more numerous, and it is the correct one from Malik's narration, for what follows: that Imam Malik was followed in connecting this hadith: Fulaib ibn Sulaiman, 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn 'Abd Allah ibn Abi Salamah, Sulaiman ibn Bilal, Muhammad ibn Mutarrif, and Muhammad ibn 'Ajlan - all five of them - narrated it from Zayd ibn Aslam, from 'Ata' ibn Yasar, from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, as muttasil. And Ibn 'Abd al-Barr mentioned in al-Tamhid others: Hisham ibn Sa'd and Dawud ibn Qays, but I did not come across their narrations.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is an example of how disagreement in the chain of transmission (sanad) - specifically whether a hadith is mursal (missing the Companion) or muttasil (complete chain to the Prophet) - leads to differences among jurists. The author presents a hadith about doubt in prayer narrated from Malik via two groups. The first group (eight narrators) reports it as mursal (from Malik to 'Ata' without Abu Sa'id). The second group (two narrators) reports it as muttasil (including Abu Sa'id). Despite the mursal narrators being more numerous, the author prefers the muttasil version because five additional trustworthy narrators (Fulayh, 'Abd al-'Aziz, Sulayman, Muhammad ibn Mutarrif, and Muhammad ibn 'Ajlan) corroborated the connection from Malik's chain. The tarjih (preference) here is based on the strength of the supporting narrations rather than sheer number. The Hadith relates to fiqh: for doubt in prayer, one adds a rak'ah and prostrates before salam. The preferred muttasil version is considered stronger evidence for this ruling.

Key Terms
المرسل (al-mursal): A hadith where the Companion is omitted from the chain; here narrated from Malik to 'Ata' without mentioning Abu Sa'id
المتصل (al-muttasil): A hadith with a continuous chain to the Prophet; here includes Abu Sa'id as the Companion
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The process of preferring one narration over another based on criteria such as number of narrators, reliability, and corroboration

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hadith dispute presented, which version is considered 'al-rajih' (the preferred) and why?
A) The mursal version, because it has eight narrators.
B) The muttasil version, because it is corroborated by five other trustworthy narrators from the same chain.
C) The mursal version, because it is from Malik directly.
D) Both are equal, so no preference.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, tarjih of hadith considers corroboration (shawahid) as a weightier factor than mere numerical majority.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Dispute on Timing of Sujud al-Sahw
Analysis of juristic disagreement on timing of sujud al-sahw based on hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi evidence for sujud al-sahw after taslim and evaluate the strength of hadith evidence in a juristic dispute.

Core Idea
All sujud al-sahw is after taslim according to the Hanafi school, supported by authenticated hadith.

The timing of sujud al-sahw (prostration for forgetfulness) is a classical point of disagreement among jurists. Some argued that prostration due to a deficiency should be performed before the taslim, while others, including the Hanafi school, maintained that all sujud al-sahw is performed after the taslim. This lesson examines the hadith evidence presented for the Hanafi position and analyzes the strength of each narration, demonstrating how ahadith are weighed in usul al-fiqh disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Positions
Clearly state the opposing views: some jurists hold that sujud for deficiency is before taslim (based on a hadith), while the Hanafi school holds that all sujud is after taslim. Note that the author presents the Hanafi position as the one supported by multiple strong proofs.
This is a dispute that has practical consequences in prayer.
2
Analyze the First Hadith (Mughirah ibn Shu'bah)
Read the hadith carefully. The Prophet stood up after two rak'ahs (a deficiency), then completed the prayer, said taslim, and then prostrated. This action explicitly places sujud after taslim for a deficiency. Note that al-Tirmidhi authenticated this hadith and considered it a basis for practice.
This hadith directly refutes the opposing view that deficiency prostration is before taslim.
3
Analyze the Second Hadith (Abu Hurayrah / Dhul-Yadayn)
This hadith involves the Prophet adding two extra rak'ahs (increase). After completing, he said taslim, then prostrated. It proves that even for increase, sujud is after taslim. Since the Prophet spoke and moved, this is an increase in the prayer, yet he prostrated after taslim.
Some argue that this only covers increase, but the Hanafi response uses analogy: both deficiency and increase require sujud after taslim.
4
Evaluate the Third Hadith (Thawban)
This hadith explicitly states 'two prostrations after the taslim for every forgetfulness.' However, it is weak due to a narrator (Zuhayr ibn Salim) who is unknown and did not hear from Thawban. Even though some tried to defend it, the weakness is accepted. Thus, the Hanafi position relies more on the authentic hadith.
Understanding hadith criticism is key to evaluating arguments.
5
Conclude the Tarjih (Preference)
The Hanafi position is supported by two authentic hadith (Mughirah and Abu Hurayrah) and the weak hadith of Thawban is not needed. The opposing view relies on a single narration that is less authentic or less specific. Hence, the author leans toward the Hanafi view.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is that Hanafis always prostrate after taslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
فسجد سجدتين، وَهُوَ جالس قَبْلَ التسليم ثُمَّ سلم. وهذا صريح في أنَّ السجود من النقص يَكُون قَبْلَ السلام... وخالف في ذَلِكَ بَعْض الفُقَهَاء، فذهبوا إلى أن سجود السهو كله بَعْدَ السلام، روي هَذَا عن بَعْض السلف، وإليه ذهب أَبُو حَنِيفَة. والحجة لَهُمْ
١. ما صح عن زياد بن علاقة، قَالَ: «صلى بنا المغيرة بن شُعْبَة؛ فنهض في الرَّكْعَتَيْنِ؛ فسبح به من خلفه؛ فأشار إليهم: قوموا فلما فرغ من صلاته، وسلم، ثُمَّ سجد سجدتين للسهو؛ فلما انصرف قَالَ رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصنع كَمَا صنعت». وهذا الحَدِيث صححه الإمام التِّرْمِذِي وَقَالَ: «و العَمَل عَلَى هَذَا عِنْدَ أهل العِلْم ثُمَّ قَالَ: ((ومن رأى قبل التسليم فحديثه أصح
٢. مَا صَحَّ عن أَبِي هُرَيْرَة: «أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم انصرف من اثنتين فَقَالَ ذو اليدين): أقصرت الصَّلاة، أم نسيت يا رَسُول الله؟ فَقَالَ رَسُول الله : أصدق ذو اليدين؟ فَقَالَ الناس: نعم، فقام رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فصلى اثنتين أخريين، ثُمَّ سلم، ثُمَّ كبر فسجد... الحديث). وهذا دليل عَلَى أن السجود من الزيادة يَكُون بَعْدَ السلام؛ لأن النبي تكلم. وَفِي رِوَايَة مُسْلِم: «أَلَهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلاة والسلام قام فدخل المنزل»، والمشي والكلام زيادة.
٣. ما روي عن ثوبان، عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لكل سهو سجدتان بَعْدَ السلام». وهذا الحَدِيث ضعفه البَيْهَقِي). وأجيب بأن إسماعيل إذا حدث عن أهل بلده فروايته عَنْهُمْ صَحِيحَة، وهذا مِنْها) . إلا أن علة الحَدِيث زُهَيْر بن سالم العنسي) قَالَ عَنْهُ الدَّارَقُطْنِي: حمصي منكر لَمْ يَسْمَع من ثوبان».
Chapter Three / Disagreement in Chain and Text. He prostrated two prostrations while sitting before the taslim, then said the taslim. This is explicit that the prostration due to deficiency is before the taslim... Some jurists disagreed with that, and they held that all prostration of forgetfulness is after the taslim. This is narrated from some predecessors, and Abu Hanifa went to this view. Their evidence: 1. What is authentic from Ziyad ibn ‘Ilaqah: ‘Al-Mughirah ibn Shu‘bah led us in prayer; he stood up in the second rak‘ah; those behind him glorified, so he gestured to them to stand. When he finished his prayer and said the taslim, he prostrated two prostrations for forgetfulness. When he turned away, he said: I saw the Messenger of Allah do as I did.’ This hadith was authenticated by al-Tirmidhi who said: ‘Practice with this according to the scholars’ then said: ‘Whoever holds [it is] before the taslim, his hadith is more authentic.’ 2. What is authentic from Abu Hurayrah: ‘The Prophet finished after two [rak‘ahs] and Dhul-Yadayn said: Has the prayer been shortened or did you forget, O Messenger of Allah? The Messenger said: Is Dhul-Yadayn truthful? The people said: Yes. So the Messenger stood and prayed two more rak‘ahs, then said the taslim, then said the takbir and prostrated...’ This is evidence that the prostration due to increase is after the taslim because the Prophet spoke. In a narration of Muslim: ‘He stood and entered his house,’ and walking and speaking are increase. 3. What is narrated from Thawban from the Prophet: ‘For every forgetfulness there are two prostrations after the taslim.’ This hadith was declared weak by al-Bayhaqi. And it was responded that if Isma‘il narrated from the people of his town, his narration from them is authentic, and this is from that. But the defect of the hadith is Zuhayr ibn Salim al-‘Ansi; al-Daraqutni said about him: ‘A Himsi, munkar, did not hear from Thawban.’
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a juristic dispute analysis concerning the timing of sujud al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). The author first presents the view of some jurists that prostration due to deficiency (like standing up after two rak'ahs) is before the taslim, supported by a hadith. Then he states that some jurists, including Abu Hanifa, hold that all sujud al-sahw is after the taslim. He presents three pieces of hadith evidence for the Hanafi position. The first is the hadith of al-Mughirah ibn Shu'bah, where the Prophet prostrated after the taslim for standing up in the middle of prayer. This hadith is authenticated by al-Tirmidhi, who notes that while some practice it, the hadith for after taslim is more authentic. The second is the famous hadith of Abu Hurayrah about the person called Dhul-Yadayn, where the Prophet after completing extra rak'ahs said the taslim and then prostrated. This proves that prostration due to increase (like extra rak'ahs) is after taslim. The third is a hadith from Thawban explicitly saying 'for every forgetfulness two prostrations after the taslim,' but this hadith is criticized for a weak narrator, Zuhayr ibn Salim al-‘Ansi. The author shows that despite attempts to defend it, the chain is problematic. Thus, the Hanafi position is supported by strong evidence from the Prophet's actions and explicit statements.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
السلام (al-taslim): The concluding salutation of prayer.
ترجيح (tarjih): The process of preferring one evidence over another due to strength or authenticity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Before the taslim for deficiency and after for increase
B) After the taslim in all cases
C) Before the taslim in all cases
D) It depends on the type of forgetfulness

Key Takeaway
Evidence from authentic hadith shows that the Prophet performed sujud al-sahw after the taslim for both deficiency and increase, which is the basis of the Hanafi position.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Placement of Sujood as-Sahw: A Usul Dispute on the Evidence
Presents three juristic views on sujood as-sahw placement before or after salutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main positions on the placement of sujood as-sahw, cite the key hadith evidence for each, and evaluate the Hanafi position within the ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Sujood as-sahw placement depends on deficiency or increase—except the Hanafi school places it always before salam.

This passage introduces a classic usul dispute among jurists: should sujood as-sahw be performed before or after the closing salutation? The answer hinges on how one interprets two key hadiths — one involving a deficiency (missing tashahhud) and another involving an increase (extra speech). Understanding the reasoning behind each position will sharpen your skill in evaluating textual evidence and madhhab-based tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
What exactly is being disputed? The placement of sujood as-sahw in relation to the salam. Determine the two main categories: due to deficiency (naqs) or due to increase (ziyada).
2
Examine the evidence for the first position
The first group (Malik, one Shafi'i view, one Ahmad narration) distinguishes based on cause: deficiency → before salam (hadith of Ibn Buhayna), increase → after salam (hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn). Identify the wording and logic used.
3
Examine the evidence for the second position
The second group (Abu Khaythama, Sulayman, another Ahmad narration, Zahiris) holds that all sujood are before salam except two cases: when one salam-ed after a deficiency, or when an uncertain imam acts on predominant opinion. Their proof: sujood is compensatory, so logically before salam; exceptions are text-based (hadith of Ibn Mas'ud).
4
Compare with the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school (not explicitly in this passage) holds that all sujood as-sahw are performed before salam, without exception. This is based on the hadith of Ibn Buhayna as a general rule and consideration that the salam itself is not fully valid until the sujood compensates the flaw. Contrast this with the views presented.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Why do the Hanafis prefer their view? They argue that the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn is specific to an extraordinary case (the Prophet was addressed by Dhu al-Yadayn), while the general principle from Ibn Buhayna is more universal. Also, the compensating sujood must complete the prayer before the salam validates it.

Source Text

وذهب بَعْض الفُقَهَاءِ إِلَى: أن السجود إذا كَانَ عن نقص في الصَّلاة فمحله قَبْلَ السلام، وإذا كَان زيادة فمحله بَعْدَ السلام، وَهُوَ مَذْهَب مَالِك ) وأحد قَوْلي الشَّافِعي ()، وإحدى الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ عن الإمام أحمد (۳). والحجة لَهُمْ: حَدِيث عَبْد الله بن بحينة السابق؛ فإنّ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم سجد لتركه التشهد الأول سجدتين قَبْلَ السلام وهذا من نقص في الصَّلاة؛ فحملوا عَلَيْهِ كُلّ نقص، وجعلوا السجود لأجله قَبْلَ السلام. و استدلوا بحديث ذي اليدين؛ فإن النبي له سجد بَعْدَ السلام، لما حصل في الصَّلاة من زيادة الكلام والمشي؛ فحملوا عَلَيْهِ كُلّ زيادة وجعلوا السجود لأجلها بَعْدَ السلام). وذهب بعضهم إلى أن السجود كله قَبْلَ السلام إلا في موضعين، فيكون بَعْدَ السلام وهما: إذا سلم من نقص في صلاته، أو تحرى الإمام فبنى على غالب ظنه. وبذلك قَالَ أبو خيثمة، وسليمان بن دَاوُد، وَهُوَ رِوَايَة عن الإمام أحمد (ه)، واختاره بغض الشافعية (٦) ، وَهُوَ مَذْهَب الظاهرية (). والحجة لَهُمْ: أن السجود إنما شرع لجبر خلل وقع في الصَّلاة؛ فالمعقول أن يَكُون محله قبل السلام، ويستثنى من ذَلِكَ مَا ورد النص بأنه يَكُون بَعْدَ السلام، وَقَدْ ورد ذَلِكَ في النقص، وَهُوَ حَدِيث عبدالله بن بحينة. وفيما إذا تحرى الشاك فبنى عَلَى غالب ظنه ؛ وَذَلِكَ لما صَحَّ عن ابن مَسْعُود لله عن النَّبي : إذا شك أحدكم في صلاته فليتحر الصَّوَاب، وليتم عليه ثُمَّ ليسلم ثُمَّ يسجد سجدتين) (۸). (۱) المدونة الكبرى (١٣٤/١ ، والمنتقى ١٨٣/١. (٢) المجموع ١٥٥/٤. (۳) المغني ٦٧٤/١ ، وشرح الزَّرْكَشِي ٣٦١/١-٣٦٢ وانظر : حلية العُلَمَاء ۱۷۸/۲-۱۷۹، وبداية المجتهد ١٣٩/١. (٤) فقه الإمام سعيد ٢٦٢/١. (٥) المغني ٦٧٤/١. (٦) المهذب ،۹۹/۱ وحاشية الجمل عَلَى شرح المنهج ٤٦٥/١. (٧) المحلى ١٧١/٤. (۸) أخرجه الطَّيَالِسِي (۲۷۱)، وأحمد ٣٧٦/١ و ٣٧٩ و ٤١٩ و ٤٢٤ و ٤٣٨ و ٤٤٣ و ٤٥٥ و ٤٦٥، والدارمي (١٥٠٦)، والبُخَارِيّ (۱۱۰/۱ (٤۰۱) و ١ / ١١١ (٤٠٤) و ١٧٠/٨ (٦٦٧١) و ١٠٨/٩ (٧٢٤٩)، ومسلم ٥٧٢٨٤/٢) (۸۹) و (٩٠) و (٨٥/٢ (٥٧٢) (۹۰) و (٩١)و(٩٤) و ٨٦/٢ (٥٧٢) (٩٥)، وأبو دَاوُد (۱۰۱۹) و (۱۰۲۰) و (۱۰۲۱) و (۱۰۲۲)، وابن ماجه (۱۲۰۳) و (۱۲۰۵) و (۱۲۱۱) و (۱۲۱۲) و (۱۲۱۸)، والتِّرْمِذِي (۳۹۲)، والنَّسَائِي ۲۸/۳ و ۲۹ و ٣١و٣٢ وفي الكبرى
Some jurists held that when sujood (prostration) is due to a deficiency in prayer, its place is before the salutation, and when it is due to an increase, its place is after the salutation. This is the madhhab of Malik, one of the two opinions of al-Shafi'i, and one of the two narrations from Imam Ahmad. Their proof is the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Buhayna mentioned earlier: the Prophet performed two prostrations before the salutation for omitting the first tashahhud, and this is a deficiency in the prayer. So they applied this to every deficiency and made sujood for it before the salutation. They also used the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn as evidence: the Prophet prostrated after the salutation due to the increase of speech and walking in the prayer. So they applied this to every increase and made sujood for it after the salutation. Some others held that all sujood are before the salutation except in two cases where they are after: when one makes salutation from a deficiency in his prayer, or when the imam who is uncertain acts upon his predominant opinion. This was said by Abu Khaythama and Sulayman ibn Dawud, and it is a narration from Imam Ahmad, chosen by some Shafi'is, and it is the madhhab of the Zahiris. Their proof is that sujood was only legislated to compensate for a defect that occurred in the prayer; so it is reasonable that its place be before the salutation. Excepted from this is what textual evidence indicates is after the salutation, and that is in the case of deficiency, namely the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Buhayna, and also when the uncertain person acts upon his predominant opinion due to what is authentically reported from Ibn Mas'ud from the Prophet: 'If one of you is uncertain in his prayer, let him seek what is correct, complete upon it, then make salutation, then prostrate two prostrations.'
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage presents a classic fiqhi ikhtilaf about the placement of sujood as-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). The author first mentions the view of some jurists (including Malik, one view of Shafi'i, and one narration from Ahmad) who distinguish between deficiency (naqs) and increase (ziyada): if the sujood is due to a deficiency, it is performed before the closing salam; if due to an increase, it is performed after. They support their view with two hadith: the hadith of Abdullah ibn Buhayna (the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs, then prostrated before salam for forgetting the first tashahhud) and the hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn (the Prophet prostrated after salam due to adding speech). A second group (Abu Khaythama, Sulayman ibn Dawud, a narration of Ahmad, some Shafi'is, and the Zahiris) holds that all sujood are before salam except two cases: when someone inadvertently completes his prayer after a deficiency, or when an imam acts on his preponderant guess. Their rationale is that sujood compensates for a flaw, so logically it should come before the salutation; the exceptions are based on textual evidence. Note that the Hanafi position (which places all sujood before salam without exception) is not explicitly mentioned in this passage, though it aligns with the second view except for the two exceptions. The discussion illustrates how differences in interpreting hadith lead to divergent fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujood as-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for errors in prayer.
نقص (naqs): Deficiency, an omission in prayer (e.g., missing tashahhud).
زيادة (ziyada): Increase, extra action in prayer (e.g., extra speech or movement).
السلام (al-salam): The closing salutation of the prayer (taslim).
التشهد الأول (al-tashahhud al-awwal): The first tashahhud recited after the second rak'ah in a prayer of three or four rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which hadith is used by the first group to support sujood before salam for a deficiency in prayer?
A) Hadith of Dhu al-Yadayn
B) Hadith of Abdullah ibn Buhayna
C) Hadith of Ibn Mas'ud
D) Hadith of Abu Huraira

Key Takeaway
The placement of sujood as-sahw is a disputed issue rooted in how general and specific hadith evidence are weighed; the Hanafi school adopts a unified position (all before salam) based on the general principle from the hadith of Ibn Buhayna.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Preferring Marfu' over Mawquf: The Hanafi Approach
Defining mawquf and marfu' and analyzing the dispute when a hadith is both

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between marfu' and mawquf narrations and apply the Hanafi principle that the marfu' version is preferred when there is a conflict.

Core Idea
When a hadith is both marfu' and mawquf, the Hanafi school prefers the raised version due to ziyadat al-thiqa.

In this passage, the author addresses a common issue in hadith criticism: a single hadith transmitted both as attributed to the Prophet (marfu') and stopped at a Companion (mawquf). Which should a jurist rely on? The Hanafi school, following the majority of jurists and hadith scholars, gives precedence to the marfu' version, based on the principle of accepting an additional affirmation from a reliable narrator. However, there are other opinions that consider the majority of narrators. This lesson walks you through the definitions, the three views, and the Hanafi justification.

Guided Path
1
Define the two categories
Identify mawquf and marfu' as defined in the text. Mawquf stops at a Companion, marfu' is attributed to the Prophet.
2
Identify the conflict
Understand the scenario: the same hadith is narrated both ways, causing a dispute among scholars.
3
Outline the three opinions
List the three scholarly positions: 1) prefer marfu', 2) prefer mawquf, 3) prefer marfu' unless the majority stops it.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi argument
Analyze how the principles of ziyadat al-thiqa and preferring an affirmer over a denier lead to preferring marfu'.
The Hanafi school adopts the first opinion.
5
Consider the third opinion's nuance
Understand the exception: if a majority of reliable narrators stop it, the mawquf may be preferred.
This nuance is not the Hanafi default but is acknowledged.

الفصل الثالث الاختلاف في السند والمتن النوع الثاني : تعارض الوقف والرفع
الوقف: مَصْدَر للفعل وقف وَهُوَ مَصْدَر بمعنى المفعول، أي مَوْقُوف). والمَوْقُوْف: هُوَ مَا يروى عن الصَّحَابَة له من أقوالهم، أو أفعالهم ونحوها فيوقف عَلَيْهِمْ وَلا يتجاوز بِهِ إِلى رَسُول الله (۲)
والرَّفع : مَصْدَر للفعل رَفَعَ، وَهُوَ مَصْدَر بمعنى المفعول، أي: مرفوع)،
والمَرْفُوع: هُوَ مَا أضيف إلى رَسُول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم خَاصَّة).
والاختلاف في بعض الأحاديث رفعاً ووقفاً أمرٌ طبيعي، وجـد فـي كثيـر مـن الأحاديث، والحَدِيث الواحد الذي يختلف به هكذا محل نظر عِنْدَ المُحَدِّثِينَ، وَهُوَ أَن المُحَدِّثِينَ إذا وجدوا حديثاً روي مرفوعاً إلى النبي ، ثُمَّ نجد الحَدِيث عينه قَدْ روي عن الصَّحَابي نفسه موقوفاً عَلَيْهِ، فهنا يقف النقاد أزاء ذَلِكَ؛ لاحتمال كون المَرْفُوع خطأ من بَعْض الرواة والصَّوَاب الوقف، أو لاحتمال كون الوقف خطأ والصَّوَاب الرفع؛ إذ إن الرفع علة للموقوف والوقف علة للمرفوع. فإذا حصل مِثْل هَذَا فِي حَدِيث ما، فإنه يَكُون محل نظر وخلاف عِنْدَ العُلَمَاء وخلاصة أقوالهم فيما يأتي: إذا كَانَ السَّنَد نظيفاً خالياً من بقية العلل؛ فإنّ للعلماء فيه الأقوال الآتية:
القَوْل الأول: يحكم للحديث بالرفع لأن راويه مثبت وغيره ساکت، وَلَوْ كَانَ نافياً فالمثبت مقدم عَلَى النافي؛ لأَنَّهُ علم ما خفي، وَقَدْ عدوا ذَلِكَ أيضاً من قبيل زيادة الثَّقَة، وَهُوَ قَوْل كَثِير من المُحَدِّثِينَ، وَهُوَ قَوْل أكثر أهل الفقه والأصول (۱) ، قَالَ العراقي: «الصَّحِيحَ الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ الْجُمْهُورِ أَن الرَّاوِي إِذا رَوَى الحَدِيث مرفوعاً وموقوفاً فالحكم للرفع، لأن مَعَهُ في حالة الرفع زيادة، هَذَا هُوَ المرجح عِنْدَ أهل الحَدِيث).
القَوْل الثَّانِي: الحكم للوقف (۳).

والترجيح برواية الأكثر هُوَ الذي عَلَيْهِ العَمَل عِنْدَ المُحَدِّثِينَ؛ لأَن رِوَايَة الجمع إذا كانوا ثقات أتقن وأحسن وأصح وأقرب للصواب؛ لذا قال ابن المبارك: «الحفاظ عن ابن شهاب ثلاثة: مَالِك ومعمر وابن عيينة، فإذا اجتمع اثنان على قول أخذنا وتركنا قول الآخر»).
به
قَالَ العلائي: «إن الجماعة إذا اختلفوا في إسناد حَدِيث كَانَ القَوْل فِيْهِمْ للأكثر عدداً أو للأحفظ والأتقن... ويترجح هَذَا أيضاً من جهة المَعْنَى، بأن مدار قبول خبر
Chapter Three: The difference in chain and text. Type Two: Conflict between stopping and raising. al-Waqf: a verbal noun from the verb waqafa, and it is a verbal noun in the sense of the passive participle, i.e., stopped. And al-Mawquf: it is what is narrated from the Companions, from their statements or their actions and the like, so it stops with them and does not go beyond to the Messenger of Allah (2). And al-Raf': a verbal noun from the verb rafa'a, and it is a verbal noun in the sense of the passive participle, i.e., raised. And al-Marfu': it is what is specifically attributed to the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. And difference in some hadiths as raised and stopped is a natural matter, found in many hadiths. The single hadith that differs in this way is a point of consideration among hadith scholars. That is, when scholars find a hadith narrated as raised to the Prophet, then they find the same hadith narrated from the Companion himself as stopped upon him. Here the critics pause because it is possible that the raised version is a mistake from some narrators and the correct is the stopped, or it is possible that the stopped is a mistake and the correct is the raised. So if such occurs in a hadith, it becomes a point of consideration and disagreement among scholars. The summary of their statements is as follows: If the chain is clean and free from other defects, then scholars have the following opinions: The first opinion: The hadith is judged as raised because its narrator is an affirmer and others are silent, and even if there is a denier, the affirmer is given precedence over the denier because he knows what is hidden. They also consider this as a case of an addition by a reliable narrator, and this is the opinion of many hadith scholars and the opinion of most jurists and usul scholars (1). Al-Iraqi said: 'The correct view upon which the majority is that if a narrator narrates a hadith as raised and as stopped, the ruling is for the raised, because with him in the raised state there is an addition. This is the preponderant view among hadith scholars.' The second opinion: The ruling is for the stopped (3). The third opinion: The detail: that the raised is an addition and the addition from a reliable narrator is accepted, unless the majority stops it and one raises it, due to apparent error (4). And the preponderance according to the narration of the majority is what is acted upon among hadith scholars, because the narration of the group, if they are reliable, is more precise, better, more correct, and closer to the truth. Hence Ibn al-Mubarak said: 'The reliable memorizers of Ibn Shihab are three: Malik, Ma'mar, and Ibn 'Uyaynah. If two agree on a statement, we take it and leave the statement of the other.' Al-'Ala'i said: 'If a group differs in the chain of a hadith, the statement among them is for the majority in number or for the one who is most accurate and most precise... And this is also preponderant from the perspective of meaning, because the basis for accepting a report...'
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a classic usul al-fiqh discussion on how to resolve the conflict between two narrations of the same hadith: one marfu' (attributed to the Prophet) and one mawquf (stopped at a Companion). The author first defines both terms: mawquf is a narration that stops at a Companion, while marfu' is one that goes up to the Prophet. The problem arises when the same hadith is transmitted both ways. The author explains that scholars have three opinions. The first opinion, held by many hadith scholars and most jurists and usul scholars, is that the marfu' version takes precedence because the narrator who reports it as marfu' is adding extra information (ziyadat al-thiqa), and the affirmative witness is preferred over the negative. This is supported by al-Iraqi's statement that this is the majority view. The second opinion is that the mawquf version is preferred, but the author does not elaborate. The third opinion details that the marfu' addition is normally accepted unless the mawquf version is narrated by a majority of reliable narrators, in which case the minority marfu' version is considered erroneous. This 'detail' opinion aligns with the practice of preferring the narration of the majority, as illustrated by Ibn al-Mubarak's statement about preferring two over one. Al-'Ala'i similarly emphasizes that when narrators differ, the statement of the majority or the most accurate is preferred. The passage thus presents a nuanced approach to resolving such conflicts, emphasizing that the number and reliability of narrators are key factors.

Key Terms
الوقف (al-waqf): The act of stopping a narration at a Companion, not attributing it to the Prophet.
الرفع (al-raf'): The act of raising a narration to the Prophet, attributing it directly to him.
زيادة الثقة (ziyadat al-thiqa): An additional piece of information added by a reliable narrator that others do not mention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of hadith scholars and jurists (including the Hanafis), when a hadith is narrated both as marfu' and mawquf with a clean chain, what is the preferred ruling?
A) The hadith is considered mawquf (stopped).
B) The hadith is considered marfu' (raised) because the narrator who raises it is an affirmer with additional knowledge.
C) The ruling depends on the number of narrators for each version.
D) The hadith is considered weak and cannot be used.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when a hadith is reported both as marfu' and mawquf, the marfu' version is preferred based on the principle of ziyadat al-thiqa and preferring an affirmer over a denier, unless there is strong evidence of error.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
