Four Scholarly Opinions on Marfu' vs. Mawquf Conflicts
Four scholarly opinions on conflicting marfu' and mawquf narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four opinions on marfu' vs. mawquf conflicts and explain why the Hanafi school prefers the marfu' version.

Core Idea
The affirmant (muthbit) has knowledge the negator lacks; marfu' is preferred unless counter evidence appears.

When a hadith is narrated both as marfu' (raised to the Prophet) and as mawquf (stopped at a Companion), how do scholars resolve the conflict? This lesson presents four scholarly opinions, focusing on the first opinion—preferring marfu'—which is the dominant view in Hanafi usul. Understanding these positions is critical for evaluating the strength of a hadith and its application in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Problem
Recognize the scenario: a hadith has two versions, one marfu' and one mawquf. Both chains are authentic but contradict each other.
The raising (raf') or stopping (waqf) is considered a defect ('illah) in the other version.
2
Memorize the Four Opinions
List the four opinions: (1) judge for marfu' (majority view), (2) judge for mawquf, (3) differentiate based on majority narration, (4) interpret mawquf as narrator's own opinion.
The first opinion is the most accepted in Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Argument
The Hanafi preference for marfu' rests on two principles: al-muthbit muqaddam 'ala al-nafi (affirmant over negator) and acceptance of ziyadat al-thiqa (addition by a reliable narrator).
The affirmant has knowledge the silent/negator lacks, so his version is more complete.
4
Compare with Opposing Views
The second opinion fears error in raising; the third gives weight to the majority of narrators. Evaluate these against the Hanafi response that a single reliable narrator's addition is accepted unless outweighed.
The author notes that practice is often case-by-case, not rigid.
5
Apply to Fiqh Consequences
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: a hadith like 'sprinkle boy's urine, wash girl's' would be binding sunnah if marfu', or only Companion opinion if mawquf.
This affects rulings on purity (taharah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثَّالِث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
عن الصَّحَابي نفسه موقوفاً عَلَيْهِ، فهنا يقف النقاد أزاء ذَلِكَ؛ لاحتمال كون المَرْفُوع خطأ من بَعْض الرواة والصَّوَاب الوقف، أو لاحتمال كون الوقف خطأ والصَّوَاب الرفع؛ إذ إن الرفع علة للموقوف والوقف علة للمرفوع. فإذا حصل مِثْل هَذَا فِي حَدِيث ما، فإنه يَكُون محل نظر وخلاف عِنْدَ العُلَمَاء وخلاصة أقوالهم فيما يأتي: إذا كَانَ السَّنَد نظيفاً خالياً من بقية العلل؛ فإنّ للعلماء فيه الأقوال الآتية:
القَوْل الأول: يحكم للحديث بالرفع لأن راويه مثبت وغيره ساکت، وَلَوْ كَانَ نافياً فالمثبت مقدم عَلَى النافي؛ لأَنَّهُ علم ما خفي، وَقَدْ عدوا ذَلِكَ أيضاً من قبيل زيادة الثَّقَة، وَهُوَ قَوْل كَثِير من المُحَدِّثِينَ، وَهُوَ قَوْل أكثر أهل الفقه والأصول (۱) ، قَالَ العراقي: «الصَّحِيحَ الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ الْجُمْهُورِ أَن الرَّاوِي إِذا رَوَى الحَدِيث مرفوعاً وموقوفاً فالحكم للرفع، لأن مَعَهُ في حالة الرفع زيادة، هَذَا هُوَ المرجح عِنْدَ أهل الحَدِيث).
القَوْل الثَّانِي: الحكم للوقف (۳).
القَوْل الثَّالث: التفصيل غلطه (٤) فالرفع زيادة والزيادة من الثَّقَة مقبولة، إلا أن يوقفه الأكثر ويرفعه واحد، لظاهر والترجيح برواية الأكثر هُوَ الذي عَلَيْهِ العَمَل عِنْدَ المُحَدِّثِينَ؛ لأَن رِوَايَة الجمع إذا كانوا ثقات أتقن وأحسن وأصح وأقرب للصواب؛ لذا قال ابن المبارك: «الحفاظ عن ابن شهاب ثلاثة: مَالِك ومعمر وابن عيينة، فإذا اجتمع اثنان على قول أخذنا به وتركنا قول الآخر»).
قَالَ العلائي: «إن الجماعة إذا اختلفوا في إسناد حَدِيث كَانَ القَوْل فِيْهِمْ للأكثر عدداً أو للأحفظ والأتقن... ويترجح هَذَا أيضاً من جهة المَعْنَى، بأن مدار قبول خبر الواحد عَلَى غلبة الظن، وعند الاختلاف فِيْمَا هُوَ مقتضى لصحة الحَدِيث أو لتعليله، يرجع إلى قَوْل الأكثر عدداً لبعدهم عن الغلط والسهو، وَذَلِكَ عِنْدَ التساوي في الحفظ والإتقان. فإن تفارقوا واستوى العدد فإلى قَوْل الأحفظ والأكثر إتقاناً، وهذه قاعدة متفق عَلَى العَمَل بِهَا عِنْدَ أهل الحَدِيث).
القَوْل الرابع: يحمل المَوْقُوْفَ عَلَى مَذْهَب الرَّاوِي ، والمُسْنَد عَلَى أَنَّهُ روايته فَلاَ تعارض ) . وَقَدْ رجح الإمام النَّوَوِيّ من هذِهِ الأقوال القَوْل الأول، ومشى عَلَيْهِ فِي تصانيفه، وأكثر من القَوْل بِهِ.
والذي ظهر لي - من صنيع جهابذة المُحَدِّثِينَ ونقادهم -: أنهم لا يحكمون عَلَى الحَدِيث الَّذِي اختلف فِيهِ عَلَى هَذَا النحو أول وهلة، بَلْ يوازنون ويقارنون ثُمَّ يحكمون عَلَى الحَدِيث بما يليق بهِ، فَقَدْ يرجحون الرِّوَايَة المرفوعة، وَقَدْ يرجحون الرّوَايَة الموقوفة، على حسب المرجحات والقرائن المحيطة بالروايات؛ فعلى هَذَا فإن حكم المُحَدِّثِيْنَ فِي مِثْل هَذَا لا يندرج تَحْتَ قاعدة كلية مطردة تقع تحتها جميع الأحاديث؛ لِذلِكَ فإن ما أطلق الإمام النووي ترجيحه يمكن أن يكون مقيداً على النحو الآتي:
الحكم للرفع - لأن راويه مثبت وغیره ساکت وَلَوْ كَانَ نافياً فالمثبت مقدم عَلَى النافي؛ لأَنَّهُ علم ما خفي ، إلا إذا قام لدى الناقد دليل أو ظهرت قرائن يترجح معها الوقف.
وسأسوق أمثلة لأحاديث اختلف في رفعها ووقفها متفرعة على حسب ترجيحات المُحَدِّثِينَ.
فمثال ما اختلف في رفعه ووقفه وكانت كلتا الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ صَحِيْحَة:
حَدِيث علي : ينضح من بول الغلام ويغسل بول الجارية». قال الإمام التِّرْمِذِي: رفع هشام الدستوائي هَذَا الحَدِيث عن قتادة وأوقفه سعيد بن أبي عروبة، عن قتادة، وَلَمْ يرفعه»(4).
وَقَالَ الحافظ ابن حجر: إسناده صحيح إلا أنه اختلف في رفعه ووقفه، وَفِي (۱) شرح التبصرة والتذكرة ,۱۷۷/۱ و ۲۳۳/۱ طبعتنا ومقدمة جامع الأصول ١٧٠/١، وفتح المغيث ١٩٤/١، والمحصول ۲۲۹/۲ - ۲۳۰، والكفاية (٥۸۸ ت - ٤١٧هـ)، شرح ألفية السيوطي ٢٩.
(۲) فتح المغيث ١٦٨/١ ط عَبْد الرحمان مُحَمَّد عُثْمَان، و ١٩٥/١ ط عويضة.
(۳) مقدمة جامع الأصول ۱۷۰/۱، فتح المغيث ,١٩٤/١، شرح ألفية السيوطي: ۲۹. (٤) شرح التبصرة والتذكرة ,۱۷۹/۱، ۲۳۳/۱ طبعتنا وفتح المغيث ,١٩٥/١، وشرح ألفية السيوطي: .۲۹
(٥) نقله عَنْهُ النَّسَائِي في السُّنَن الكبرى ٦٣٢/١ عقيب (۲۰۷۲)، ونقله عَنْهُ العلائي في نظم الفرائد: ٣٦٧ بلفظ: «حفاظ علم الزُّهْرِيّ ثلاثة : مَالِك ومعمر وابن عيينة، فإذا اختلفوا أخذنا بقول رجلين منهم.
Chapter Three: Difference in Chain and Text. From the Companion himself, as a mawquf (stopped) narration. Here the critics pause regarding that; due to the possibility that the marfu' (raised) is a mistake from some narrators and the correct version is mawquf, or the possibility that the mawquf is a mistake and the correct is marfu'; indeed the raising is a defect for the mawquf and the stopping is a defect for the marfu'. So if such occurs in a hadith, it becomes a subject of consideration and disagreement among scholars. The summary of their statements is as follows: If the chain is clean and free of other defects, then scholars have the following opinions: The first opinion: The hadith is judged as marfu' because its narrator is an affirmant (muthbit) and others are silent; even if they are negators, the affirmant takes precedence over the negator because he knows what is hidden. They also considered this as a case of 'addition by a reliable narrator' (ziyadat al-thiqa). This is the view of many muhaddithin and the view of most scholars of Fiqh and Usul. Al-Iraqi said: 'The correct view upon which the majority is that when a narrator narrates the hadith as marfu' and as mawquf, the ruling is for the marfu', because he has an addition in the case of raising; this is the preponderant view according to the people of hadith.' The second opinion: The ruling is for the mawquf. The third opinion: Differentiation: that the raising is an addition and the addition from a reliable narrator is accepted, unless the majority makes it mawquf and only one makes it marfu', due to the apparent. And preponderance by the narration of the majority is what is practiced by the muhaddithin; because the narration of a group, if they are reliable, is more precise, better, more correct, and closer to correctness. Hence Ibn al-Mubarak said: 'The preservers of Ibn Shihab are three: Malik, Ma'mar, and Ibn 'Uyaynah. When two agree on a statement, we take it and leave the statement of the other.' Al-'Ala'i said: 'If a group differs on the chain of a hadith, the statement among them is for the majority in number or for the most memorizer and precise... This is also preponderant from the perspective of meaning, because the basis for accepting a solitary report is preponderance of assumption; and when there is disagreement on what necessitates authenticity or defect, one refers to the statement of the majority in number because they are farther from error and oversight. That is when equality in memory and precision. If they differ and the number is equal, then to the statement of the most memorizer and most precise. This is a rule agreed upon in practice among the people of hadith.' The fourth opinion: The mawquf is interpreted as the narrator's own opinion, and the musnad (i.e., marfu') is considered his narration, so there is no contradiction. Imam al-Nawawi gave preponderance to the first opinion among these, and proceeded upon it in his works, and most of his statements support it. What appears to me from the practice of the leading critics and muhaddithin is that they do not judge on the hadith that differs in this manner at first glance; rather they weigh and compare, then judge on the hadith according to what befits it. Sometimes they may preponderate the marfu' version, sometimes the mawquf version, depending on the preponderators and contextual clues surrounding the narrations. Therefore, the ruling of the muhaddithin in such cases does not fall under a universal encompassing rule covering all hadiths. Hence, what Imam al-Nawawi declared as preponderant can be restricted as follows: The ruling is for the marfu' because its narrator is an affirmant and others are silent even if they are negators; the affirmant takes precedence over the negator because he knows what is hidden, unless there appears to the critic evidence or clues that make the mawquf preponderant. I will present examples of hadiths that differed in being raised or stopped, branching according to the preponderances of the muhaddithin. An example of what differed in its raising and stopping while both versions are authentic: The hadith of 'Ali: 'One sprinkles from the urine of a boy and washes from the urine of a girl.' Imam al-Tirmidhi said: Hisham al-Dastawa'i raised this hadith from Qatadah, and Sa'id ibn Abi 'Arubah stopped it from Qatadah and did not raise it. Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: Its chain is authentic except that there is difference in its raising and stopping. And in the footnotes: (1) Explanation of al-Tabsira wa al-Tadhkira 1/177 and 1/233 our edition, and Muqaddimah Jami' al-Usul 1/170, and Fath al-Mughith 1/194, and al-Mahsul 2/229-230, and al-Kifayah (588 T - 417H), and Sharh Alfiyyat al-Suyuti 29. (2) Fath al-Mughith 1/168 ed. 'Abd al-Rahman Muhammad 'Uthman, and 1/195 ed. 'Uwaydah. (3) Muqaddimah Jami' al-Usul 1/170, Fath al-Mughith 1/194, Sharh Alfiyyat al-Suyuti: 29. (4) Explanation of al-Tabsira wa al-Tadhkira 1/179, 1/233 our edition, and Fath al-Mughith 1/195, and Sharh Alfiyyat al-Suyuti: 29. (5) Transmitted from him by al-Nasa'i in al-Sunan al-Kubra 1/632 after (2072), and transmitted from him by al-'Ala'i in Nazm al-Fara'id: 367 with the wording: 'The preservers of the knowledge of al-Zuhri are three: Malik, Ma'mar, and Ibn 'Uyaynah. When they differ, we take the statement of two of them.'
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a methodological discussion from the third chapter on differences in chain and text. It addresses the scenario where a hadith is narrated both as marfu' (ascribed to the Prophet) and as mawquf (ascribed to a Companion). The author presents four scholarly opinions on how to resolve such a conflict. The first opinion, held by most muhaddithin and fuqaha/usuliyyun, judges the hadith as marfu' because the narrator who raised it provides an addition (ziyadat al-thiqa) and is an affirmant (muthbit), which takes precedence over silence or negation. The second opinion favors mawquf. The third opinion differentiates: accept the marfu' as a reliable addition unless the majority of narrators report it as mawquf, in which case the majority's version is preferred (a principle from Ibn al-Mubarak and al-'Ala'i). The fourth opinion harmonizes by interpreting the mawquf as the narrator's own opinion and the marfu' as his actual narration. Imam al-Nawawi preferred the first opinion. However, the author observes that in practice, leading critics do not apply a universal rule; they weigh evidence case-by-case. They may prefer the marfu' generally but if there are indications supporting the mawquf, they choose that. This is illustrated with the hadith of 'Ali about sprinkling or washing from a child's urine. The hadith has authentic chains but differed in being marfu' or mawquf. Hisham al-Dastawa'i narrated it marfu', while Sa'id ibn Abi 'Arubah narrated it mawquf. The critics do not automatically prefer one; they consider circumstances.

Key Terms
رفع (raf'): Attributing a hadith to the Prophet (marfu'); raising the chain to the Prophet.
وقف (waqf): Stopping the chain at a Companion (mawquf); not attributing to the Prophet.
مثبت (muthbit): The narrator who affirms a fact (here, the raising of the hadith), in contrast to one who is silent or negates.
زيادة الثقة (ziyadat al-thiqa): An addition made by a reliable narrator to the hadith text or chain, which is generally accepted by hadith scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first opinion on a hadith narrated both marfu' and mawquf?
A) Judge for the mawquf because the Companion is a witness.
B) Judge for the marfu' because the narrator is an affirmant and the addition of a reliable narrator is accepted.
C) Suspend judgment until further evidence appears.
D) Accept both as equally valid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prefers the marfu' version in a marfu' vs. mawquf conflict, based on the affirmant having additional knowledge, but final judgment is often case-specific.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Practical Methodology of Muhaddithin: Case-by-Case Resolution with the Hadith of 'Ali
Practical methodology and example of case-by-case resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the case-by-case methodology of muhaddithin to resolve marfu' vs. mawquf conflicts, using the hadith of 'Ali as an example.

Core Idea
Leading critics weigh evidence case-by-case; no universal rule always applies.

While the majority opinion prefers marfu' in theory, the practical methodology of leading muhaddithin is not rigid. They compare narrations, consider preponderators, and may sometimes prefer the mawquf version. This lesson explores that nuanced approach using the famous hadith of 'Ali about urine of children. Understanding this flexibility is crucial for accurate istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the Author's Observation
The author notes that muhaddithin do not automatically apply the first opinion; they balance evidence and contextual clues.
This is an important corrective to a rigid reading of the four opinions.
2
Examine the Hadith Example
Read the hadith of 'Ali: 'Sprinkle from the urine of a boy and wash from the urine of a girl.' Note that it has two authentic chains: one marfu' (via Hisham al-Dastawa'i) and one mawquf (via Sa'id ibn Abi 'Arubah).
Both chains are sahih, so the conflict is in the attribution, not the text.
3
Apply the Case-by-Case Methodology
According to the author, the critic weighs: who is more reliable? what are the contextual clues? Here, even though the majority may have narrated it mawquf (Sa'id is one of many?), the specific circumstances determine the preference.
The passage does not specify which version is ultimately preferred, only that the methodology is flexible.
4
Connect to Usul Principles
Identify how the principles of muthbit, ziyadat al-thiqa, and majority narration are applied in practice. The affirmant principle gives initial preference to marfu', but if evidence suggests the raising is a mistake (e.g., the majority are more precise), the mawquf may prevail.
This shows the interaction between general rules and case-specific factors.
5
Derive the Fiqh Ruling
If the marfu' version is preferred, the ruling is a Prophetic sunnah: sprinkle for boy, wash for girl. If mawquf prevails, it becomes a Companion's opinion, which may be weaker but not necessarily discarded.
The Hanafi school generally follows the marfu' version, leading to different rulings than schools that prefer mawquf.

Source Text

الفصل الثَّالِث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
عن الصَّحَابي نفسه موقوفاً عَلَيْهِ، فهنا يقف النقاد أزاء ذَلِكَ؛ لاحتمال كون المَرْفُوع خطأ من بَعْض الرواة والصَّوَاب الوقف، أو لاحتمال كون الوقف خطأ والصَّوَاب الرفع؛ إذ إن الرفع علة للموقوف والوقف علة للمرفوع. فإذا حصل مِثْل هَذَا فِي حَدِيث ما، فإنه يَكُون محل نظر وخلاف عِنْدَ العُلَمَاء وخلاصة أقوالهم فيما يأتي: إذا كَانَ السَّنَد نظيفاً خالياً من بقية العلل؛ فإنّ للعلماء فيه الأقوال الآتية:
القَوْل الأول: يحكم للحديث بالرفع لأن راويه مثبت وغيره ساکت، وَلَوْ كَانَ نافياً فالمثبت مقدم عَلَى النافي؛ لأَنَّهُ علم ما خفي، وَقَدْ عدوا ذَلِكَ أيضاً من قبيل زيادة الثَّقَة، وَهُوَ قَوْل كَثِير من المُحَدِّثِينَ، وَهُوَ قَوْل أكثر أهل الفقه والأصول (۱) ، قَالَ العراقي: «الصَّحِيحَ الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ الْجُمْهُورِ أَن الرَّاوِي إِذا رَوَى الحَدِيث مرفوعاً وموقوفاً فالحكم للرفع، لأن مَعَهُ في حالة الرفع زيادة، هَذَا هُوَ المرجح عِنْدَ أهل الحَدِيث).
القَوْل الثَّانِي: الحكم للوقف (۳).
القَوْل الثَّالث: التفصيل غلطه (٤) فالرفع زيادة والزيادة من الثَّقَة مقبولة، إلا أن يوقفه الأكثر ويرفعه واحد، لظاهر والترجيح برواية الأكثر هُوَ الذي عَلَيْهِ العَمَل عِنْدَ المُحَدِّثِينَ؛ لأَن رِوَايَة الجمع إذا كانوا ثقات أتقن وأحسن وأصح وأقرب للصواب؛ لذا قال ابن المبارك: «الحفاظ عن ابن شهاب ثلاثة: مَالِك ومعمر وابن عيينة، فإذا اجتمع اثنان على قول أخذنا به وتركنا قول الآخر»).
قَالَ العلائي: «إن الجماعة إذا اختلفوا في إسناد حَدِيث كَانَ القَوْل فِيْهِمْ للأكثر عدداً أو للأحفظ والأتقن... ويترجح هَذَا أيضاً من جهة المَعْنَى، بأن مدار قبول خبر الواحد عَلَى غلبة الظن، وعند الاختلاف فِيْمَا هُوَ مقتضى لصحة الحَدِيث أو لتعليله، يرجع إلى قَوْل الأكثر عدداً لبعدهم عن الغلط والسهو، وَذَلِكَ عِنْدَ التساوي في الحفظ والإتقان. فإن تفارقوا واستوى العدد فإلى قَوْل الأحفظ والأكثر إتقاناً، وهذه قاعدة متفق عَلَى العَمَل بِهَا عِنْدَ أهل الحَدِيث).
القَوْل الرابع: يحمل المَوْقُوْفَ عَلَى مَذْهَب الرَّاوِي ، والمُسْنَد عَلَى أَنَّهُ روايته فَلاَ تعارض ) . وَقَدْ رجح الإمام النَّوَوِيّ من هذِهِ الأقوال القَوْل الأول، ومشى عَلَيْهِ فِي تصانيفه، وأكثر من القَوْل بِهِ.
والذي ظهر لي - من صنيع جهابذة المُحَدِّثِينَ ونقادهم -: أنهم لا يحكمون عَلَى الحَدِيث الَّذِي اختلف فِيهِ عَلَى هَذَا النحو أول وهلة، بَلْ يوازنون ويقارنون ثُمَّ يحكمون عَلَى الحَدِيث بما يليق بهِ، فَقَدْ يرجحون الرِّوَايَة المرفوعة، وَقَدْ يرجحون الرّوَايَة الموقوفة، على حسب المرجحات والقرائن المحيطة بالروايات؛ فعلى هَذَا فإن حكم المُحَدِّثِيْنَ فِي مِثْل هَذَا لا يندرج تَحْتَ قاعدة كلية مطردة تقع تحتها جميع الأحاديث؛ لِذلِكَ فإن ما أطلق الإمام النووي ترجيحه يمكن أن يكون مقيداً على النحو الآتي:
الحكم للرفع - لأن راويه مثبت وغیره ساکت وَلَوْ كَانَ نافياً فالمثبت مقدم عَلَى النافي؛ لأَنَّهُ علم ما خفي ، إلا إذا قام لدى الناقد دليل أو ظهرت قرائن يترجح معها الوقف.
وسأسوق أمثلة لأحاديث اختلف في رفعها ووقفها متفرعة على حسب ترجيحات المُحَدِّثِينَ.
فمثال ما اختلف في رفعه ووقفه وكانت كلتا الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ صَحِيْحَة:
حَدِيث علي : ينضح من بول الغلام ويغسل بول الجارية». قال الإمام التِّرْمِذِي: رفع هشام الدستوائي هَذَا الحَدِيث عن قتادة وأوقفه سعيد بن أبي عروبة، عن قتادة، وَلَمْ يرفعه»(4).
وَقَالَ الحافظ ابن حجر: إسناده صحيح إلا أنه اختلف في رفعه ووقفه، وَفِي (۱) شرح التبصرة والتذكرة ,۱۷۷/۱ و ۲۳۳/۱ طبعتنا ومقدمة جامع الأصول ١٧٠/١، وفتح المغيث ١٩٤/١، والمحصول ۲۲۹/۲ - ۲۳۰، والكفاية (٥۸۸ ت - ٤١٧هـ)، شرح ألفية السيوطي ٢٩.
(۲) فتح المغيث ١٦٨/١ ط عَبْد الرحمان مُحَمَّد عُثْمَان، و ١٩٥/١ ط عويضة.
(۳) مقدمة جامع الأصول ۱۷۰/۱، فتح المغيث ,١٩٤/١، شرح ألفية السيوطي: ۲۹. (٤) شرح التبصرة والتذكرة ,۱۷۹/۱، ۲۳۳/۱ طبعتنا وفتح المغيث ,١٩٥/١، وشرح ألفية السيوطي: .۲۹
(٥) نقله عَنْهُ النَّسَائِي في السُّنَن الكبرى ٦٣٢/١ عقيب (۲۰۷۲)، ونقله عَنْهُ العلائي في نظم الفرائد: ٣٦٧ بلفظ: «حفاظ علم الزُّهْرِيّ ثلاثة : مَالِك ومعمر وابن عيينة، فإذا اختلفوا أخذنا بقول رجلين منهم.
Chapter Three: Difference in Chain and Text. From the Companion himself, as a mawquf (stopped) narration. Here the critics pause regarding that; due to the possibility that the marfu' (raised) is a mistake from some narrators and the correct version is mawquf, or the possibility that the mawquf is a mistake and the correct is marfu'; indeed the raising is a defect for the mawquf and the stopping is a defect for the marfu'. So if such occurs in a hadith, it becomes a subject of consideration and disagreement among scholars. The summary of their statements is as follows: If the chain is clean and free of other defects, then scholars have the following opinions: The first opinion: The hadith is judged as marfu' because its narrator is an affirmant (muthbit) and others are silent; even if they are negators, the affirmant takes precedence over the negator because he knows what is hidden. They also considered this as a case of 'addition by a reliable narrator' (ziyadat al-thiqa). This is the view of many muhaddithin and the view of most scholars of Fiqh and Usul. Al-Iraqi said: 'The correct view upon which the majority is that when a narrator narrates the hadith as marfu' and as mawquf, the ruling is for the marfu', because he has an addition in the case of raising; this is the preponderant view according to the people of hadith.' The second opinion: The ruling is for the mawquf. The third opinion: Differentiation: that the raising is an addition and the addition from a reliable narrator is accepted, unless the majority makes it mawquf and only one makes it marfu', due to the apparent. And preponderance by the narration of the majority is what is practiced by the muhaddithin; because the narration of a group, if they are reliable, is more precise, better, more correct, and closer to correctness. Hence Ibn al-Mubarak said: 'The preservers of Ibn Shihab are three: Malik, Ma'mar, and Ibn 'Uyaynah. When two agree on a statement, we take it and leave the statement of the other.' Al-'Ala'i said: 'If a group differs on the chain of a hadith, the statement among them is for the majority in number or for the most memorizer and precise... This is also preponderant from the perspective of meaning, because the basis for accepting a solitary report is preponderance of assumption; and when there is disagreement on what necessitates authenticity or defect, one refers to the statement of the majority in number because they are farther from error and oversight. That is when equality in memory and precision. If they differ and the number is equal, then to the statement of the most memorizer and most precise. This is a rule agreed upon in practice among the people of hadith.' The fourth opinion: The mawquf is interpreted as the narrator's own opinion, and the musnad (i.e., marfu') is considered his narration, so there is no contradiction. Imam al-Nawawi gave preponderance to the first opinion among these, and proceeded upon it in his works, and most of his statements support it. What appears to me from the practice of the leading critics and muhaddithin is that they do not judge on the hadith that differs in this manner at first glance; rather they weigh and compare, then judge on the hadith according to what befits it. Sometimes they may preponderate the marfu' version, sometimes the mawquf version, depending on the preponderators and contextual clues surrounding the narrations. Therefore, the ruling of the muhaddithin in such cases does not fall under a universal encompassing rule covering all hadiths. Hence, what Imam al-Nawawi declared as preponderant can be restricted as follows: The ruling is for the marfu' because its narrator is an affirmant and others are silent even if they are negators; the affirmant takes precedence over the negator because he knows what is hidden, unless there appears to the critic evidence or clues that make the mawquf preponderant. I will present examples of hadiths that differed in being raised or stopped, branching according to the preponderances of the muhaddithin. An example of what differed in its raising and stopping while both versions are authentic: The hadith of 'Ali: 'One sprinkles from the urine of a boy and washes from the urine of a girl.' Imam al-Tirmidhi said: Hisham al-Dastawa'i raised this hadith from Qatadah, and Sa'id ibn Abi 'Arubah stopped it from Qatadah and did not raise it. Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said: Its chain is authentic except that there is difference in its raising and stopping. And in the footnotes: (1) Explanation of al-Tabsira wa al-Tadhkira 1/177 and 1/233 our edition, and Muqaddimah Jami' al-Usul 1/170, and Fath al-Mughith 1/194, and al-Mahsul 2/229-230, and al-Kifayah (588 T - 417H), and Sharh Alfiyyat al-Suyuti 29. (2) Fath al-Mughith 1/168 ed. 'Abd al-Rahman Muhammad 'Uthman, and 1/195 ed. 'Uwaydah. (3) Muqaddimah Jami' al-Usul 1/170, Fath al-Mughith 1/194, Sharh Alfiyyat al-Suyuti: 29. (4) Explanation of al-Tabsira wa al-Tadhkira 1/179, 1/233 our edition, and Fath al-Mughith 1/195, and Sharh Alfiyyat al-Suyuti: 29. (5) Transmitted from him by al-Nasa'i in al-Sunan al-Kubra 1/632 after (2072), and transmitted from him by al-'Ala'i in Nazm al-Fara'id: 367 with the wording: 'The preservers of the knowledge of al-Zuhri are three: Malik, Ma'mar, and Ibn 'Uyaynah. When they differ, we take the statement of two of them.'
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a methodological discussion from the third chapter on differences in chain and text. It addresses the scenario where a hadith is narrated both as marfu' (ascribed to the Prophet) and as mawquf (ascribed to a Companion). The author presents four scholarly opinions on how to resolve such a conflict. The first opinion, held by most muhaddithin and fuqaha/usuliyyun, judges the hadith as marfu' because the narrator who raised it provides an addition (ziyadat al-thiqa) and is an affirmant (muthbit), which takes precedence over silence or negation. The second opinion favors mawquf. The third opinion differentiates: accept the marfu' as a reliable addition unless the majority of narrators report it as mawquf, in which case the majority's version is preferred (a principle from Ibn al-Mubarak and al-'Ala'i). The fourth opinion harmonizes by interpreting the mawquf as the narrator's own opinion and the marfu' as his actual narration. Imam al-Nawawi preferred the first opinion. However, the author observes that in practice, leading critics do not apply a universal rule; they weigh evidence case-by-case. They may prefer the marfu' generally but if there are indications supporting the mawquf, they choose that. This is illustrated with the hadith of 'Ali about sprinkling or washing from a child's urine. The hadith has authentic chains but differed in being marfu' or mawquf. Hisham al-Dastawa'i narrated it marfu', while Sa'id ibn Abi 'Arubah narrated it mawquf. The critics do not automatically prefer one; they consider circumstances.

Key Terms
رفع (raf'): Attributing a hadith to the Prophet (marfu'); raising the chain to the Prophet.
وقف (waqf): Stopping the chain at a Companion (mawquf); not attributing to the Prophet.
مثبت (muthbit): The narrator who affirms a fact (here, the raising of the hadith), in contrast to one who is silent or negates.
زيادة الثقة (ziyadat al-thiqa): An addition made by a reliable narrator to the hadith text or chain, which is generally accepted by hadith scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the author say about how muhaddithin actually resolve marfu' vs. mawquf conflicts?
A) They always follow Imam al-Nawawi's rule to prefer marfu'.
B) They weigh evidence and sometimes prefer marfu', sometimes mawquf, case-by-case.
C) They always prefer mawquf because it is safer.
D) They reject both versions if there is a conflict.

Key Takeaway
The practical methodology of muhaddithin is case-by-case; the marfu' is a default preference that can be overridden by evidence.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Linguistic Analysis in Usul: The Infant Urine Dispute
Usul dispute analyzing contrasting hadith wordings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that conjunction requires distinction (al-'atf yuqtadi al-mughayara) to evaluate conflicting hadith interpretations and derive the ruling on infant urine purification.

Core Idea
Contradiction in prophetic statements is impossible; identical meanings for distinct terms are rejected.

The purification of infant urine is a classical point of ikhtilaf rooted in hadith wording. This lesson examines three madhhabs, focusing on the linguistic argument that terms like 'sprinkling' (nadh) cannot mean 'washing' (ghusl) when the Prophet explicitly contrasts them. You will learn how Hanafi usul uses the principle of non-contradiction and conjunction to prefer the ruling that requires full washing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three madhhabs
List the three positions: (1) washing required for all infants (Abu Hanifa), (2) urine of non-food-eating infant is pure (dismissed as weak), (3) sprinkling sufficient before solid food, washing after.
The second madhhab is set aside due to weak transmission.
2
Isolate the key hadith evidence
Focus on the hadith of Umm Qays: 'He sprinkled it and did not wash it.' This wording is the core proof for the third madhhab.
Also note the hadith of Ali and Abu al-Samh that conjoin washing and sprinkling.
3
Apply the principle: conjunction requires distinction
If 'sprinkling' meant 'washing', then the phrase 'he sprinkled and did not wash' would be contradictory. Also, in hadiths where both are mentioned together, the conjunction ('and') implies they are different actions.
This is a central rule in Hanafi linguistics: al-'atf yuqtadi al-mughayara.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa's school holds that the hadiths must be interpreted consistently: sprinkling is a separate, insufficient action; washing is required. The third madhhab's interpretation creates an impossible contradiction.
The text argues that attributing washing to 'nadh' would make the Prophet say 'he washed it and did not wash it.'
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: under the Hanafi ruling, all infant urine (regardless of diet) requires full washing (multiple times with wringing). Under the third madhhab, pre-solid-food infants only need sprinkling.
This affects daily practice for Muslim parents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن (٣) أخرجه أبو داؤد)، وابن ماجه (٣) ، وَالنَّسَائِي (٣) ، وابن خزيمة)، والدارقطني والمزي). (ه) ، وقد اختلف الفُقَهَاء في الأحكام المستفادة من هذه الأحاديث على مذاهب أشهرها ما يأتي: المذهب الأول: يرى أن التطهير من بول الرضيع - كالتطهير من بول الكبير – إنما يكون بغسله، وَلا فرق في ذَلِكَ بَيْنَ بول رضيع أكل الطعام أو لم يأكل، كَمَا أَنَّهُ لا فرق فِي ذَلِكَ بَيْنَ الذكر والأنثى. وإلى ذَلِكَ ذهب أبو حَنِيفَة وَهُوَ المشهور عن مَالِك عَلَى خِلاف في كيفية الغسل الذي يجزئ في التطهير من النجاسة، فإن أبا حنيفة يشترط لتطهير النجاسة غير المرئية تعدد مرات غسلها - ثلاثاً أو سبعاً والعصر بَعْدَ كُلّ غسلة ) ، وَلَمْ يشترط مَالِك أكثر من صب الماء عَلَى النجاسة بحيث يغمرها، ويذهب لونها وطعمها ورائحتها ولا يشترط لإزالة النجاسة إمرار اليد والعصر، ونحو ذلك (۸). وَقَدْ حملوا: «إتباع الماء» ونضحه» و «رشه»، هذه الألفاظ كلها حملوها عَلَى مَعْنَى الغسل، وَقَدْ أفاض الطحاوي في إيراد الآثار الدالة عَلَى أن هذِهِ الألفاظ قد تطلق ويراد بها الغسل). لَكِن هَذَا يؤخذ عَلَيْهِ: ان هذِهِ الألفاظ، وإن كَانَتْ تطلق أحياناً على الغسل فإن الحال في مسألتنا هذه لا يحتمل ذَلِكَ؛ لأنَّه يؤدي إلى تناقض تتنزه عَنْهُ نصوص الشريعة؛ فحديث أم المؤمنين عائشة رضي الله عَنْهَا قَدْ جاء بلفظ: «فدعا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بماء فأتبعه وَلَمْ يغسله فإذا جَعَلَ أتبعه بمعنى غسله فإن المَعْنَى حينئذ يَكُون فغسله وَلَمْ يغسله وَكَذَلِكَ حَدِيث أم قيس بنت محصن قَدْ جاء بلفظ: «فنضحه وَلَمْ يغسله» فلو حمل النضح عَلَى مَعْنَى الغسل لكان التقدير : فغسله وَلَمْ يغسله، وهذا تناقض غَيْر معقول. وأيضاً فإن النبي مع الطفل الغسل على النصح في حديث علي ، وعطف الرش عَلَى الغسل في حَدِيث أبي السمح له، والعطف يقتضي المغايرة. فلو أريد بهما مَعْنَى واحدٌ، لكان عبثاً يتنزه عَنْهُ الشارع ) (1) المذهب الثاني: نُسِبَ إلى الشَّافِعِي قَوْلٌ: بأن بول الصبي الَّذِي لَم يأكل الطعام طاهر. ونسبت رِوَايَة إلى الإمام مالك: أنَّهُ لا يغسل بول الجارية ولا الغلام قبل أن يأكلا الطعام. لَكِنْ ذكر الباجي (٢) أن هذِهِ الرِّوَايَة عن مَالِك شاذة (۳). وذكر النَّوَوِيّ أن نقل هَذَا القَوْل عن الشافعي باطل). لذلك لا حاجة للتعليق عَلَى هَذَا المذهب. المذهب الثالث: ينضح بول الطفل الرضيع الَّذِي لَمْ يأكل الطعام، فإذا أكل الطعام كَانَ حكم بوله کحكم بول الكبير يغسل. وَقَدْ فسّر هَذَا المذهب النضح بأنه غمر مَوْضِع البول ومكاثرته بالماء مكاثرة لا يبلغ جريانه وتردده وتقطره. فَهُوَ بمعنى الغسل الذي سبق ذكره عن مالك). وَقَدْ اعتمد هَذَا المذهب حَدِيث أم قيس بنت محصن، فَقَدْ جاء بلفظ: «أَنَّهَا أتت بابن لَهَا صَغِير لَمْ يأكل الطعام... الخ».
Chapter Three / Difference in Sanad and Matn (3) Abu Dawood narrated it, and Ibn Majah (3), and al-Nasa'i (3), and Ibn Khuzaymah, and al-Daraqutni, and al-Mizzi. (H) And the jurists differed in the rulings derived from these hadiths according to schools, the most famous of which are as follows: The First School: It holds that purification from the urine of a nursing infant—like purification from the urine of an adult—is only by washing it, and there is no difference in that between the urine of an infant who has eaten food or not, just as there is no difference between male and female. Abu Hanifa held this, and it is the well-known view from Malik, though there is a difference in the manner of washing that suffices for purification from impurity. For Abu Hanifa requires for purification from non-visible impurity multiple washings—three or seven—and wringing after each washing, while Malik only requires pouring water over the impurity such that it covers it and removes its color, taste, and smell, and he does not require rubbing or wringing for removal of impurity, etc. (8). And they interpreted 'following with water,' 'sprinkling,' and 'spraying'—all these terms they interpreted as meaning washing. Al-Tahawi extensively cited traditions indicating that these terms are sometimes used and meaning washing. But this is objected to: that these terms, even if sometimes used for washing, the situation in our case does not allow that, because it leads to a contradiction from which the texts of the Sharia are free. For the hadith of Umm al-Mu'minin Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, came with the wording: 'The Prophet, peace be upon him, called for water and followed it and did not wash it.' If one makes 'followed it' mean 'washed it,' then the meaning would be 'he washed it and did not wash it.' Likewise, the hadith of Umm Qays bint Mihsan came with the wording: 'He sprinkled it and did not wash it.' If one interprets sprinkling as washing, the estimation would be: he washed it and did not wash it, and this is an unintelligible contradiction. Also, the Prophet contrasted sprinkling with washing in the hadith of Ali, and he conjoined spraying with washing in the hadith of Abu al-Samh, and conjunction requires distinction. If they intended the same meaning, it would be frivolity from which the Lawgiver is free. (1) The Second School: A statement is attributed to al-Shafi'i that the urine of a boy who has not eaten food is pure. And a narration is attributed to Imam Malik that he does not wash the urine of a girl or a boy before they eat food. However, al-Baji mentioned that this narration from Malik is anomalous (3). And al-Nawawi mentioned that transmission of this statement from al-Shafi'i is false. Therefore, there is no need to comment on this school. The Third School: One sprinkles the urine of a nursing infant who has not eaten food; when he eats food, the ruling of his urine is like the urine of an adult—washed. And this school interpreted 'sprinkling' as covering the place of urine and drenching it with water to an extent that does not reach flowing, dripping, or dripping. So it is like the washing mentioned earlier from Malik. And this school relied on the hadith of Umm Qays bint Mihsan, which came with the wording: 'She brought a young son of hers who had not eaten food... etc.'
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the juristic dispute on the purification of infant urine. It presents three madhhabs. The first madhhab, of Abu Hanifa (and the famous view of Malik), requires full washing for infant urine, just like adult urine, with no distinction based on diet or gender. The text then defends this view linguistically: although words like 'following' (ittiba'), 'sprinkling' (nadh), and 'spraying' (rashsh) might sometimes mean washing, in the specific hadiths about infant urine they cannot mean washing because that would create a contradiction (e.g., 'he washed it and did not wash it'). The author argues that the Prophet explicitly contrasted these actions with washing, showing they are distinct. The second madhhab (attributed to Shafi'i and Malik) is dismissed as anomalous or incorrectly transmitted. The third madhhab distinguishes based on diet: before eating food, only sprinkling is needed; after eating, washing is required. This third view interprets sprinkling as a thorough drenching, similar to Malik's minimal washing. The passage demonstrates how careful hadith analysis—particularly the handling of apparent contradictions between texts—leads to different fiqh rulings.

Key Terms
نضح (nadh): In this context, sprinkling water on the impurity without full washing or flowing.
غسل (ghusl): Washing with water that flows and is rubbed, typically repeated and wrung out according to Hanafis.
إتباع (ittiba'): Following with water; sometimes interpreted as washing, but argued here to be distinct.
رش (rashsh): Spraying or sprinkling water; in hadiths, contrasted with washing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first madhhab (Abu Hanifa), what is the ruling on the urine of a male infant who has not eaten solid food?
A) It is pure and does not require washing.
B) It must be washed, just like the urine of an adult.
C) It requires only sprinkling of water.
D) It is purified by wiping only.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the principle that conjunction requires distinction (al-'atf yuqtadi al-mughayara) is used to enforce that different terms in a hadith must have different meanings, preventing contradictions.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Certainty vs Doubt in Hadith: Infant Urine Purification
Analyzing hadith evidence for purification from infant urine

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that certainty (yaqin) is not overridden by doubt (shakk) to evaluate conflicting hadith evidence on a disputed fiqh ruling.

Core Idea
Certainty in general impurity of urine is not abandoned for doubtful specification—only established exceptions are accepted.

This passage explores a classic usul dispute: does sprinkling (nadh) suffice for all infant urine, or only for male infants who have not eaten food? The Hanafi position relies on general hadiths establishing impurity of all urine, with a specific exception proven by the hadith of Umm Qays. The lesson examines how certainty and doubt operate in weighing evidence, and how hadith confirmation can change a ruling over time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue and conflicting views
Pinpoint the dispute: is there a difference between male and female infant urine in purification? List the Hanafi position (sprinkling for male, washing for female) and the opposing view of Ibn Hazm (all urine requires washing).
Also note al-Shafi'i's initial position: sprinkling for both, but with caution.
2
Analyze the types of hadith evidence
Categorize the evidence: general hadiths (e.g., 'Avoid urine, for most punishment of the grave is from it') establish the impurity of all urine (qat'i al-dalala in Hanafi view). The specific hadith of Umm Qays provides a specification (takhsis) for male infant urine. Consider the epistemological weight of each.
Hanafi usul: 'amm is qat'i until proven otherwise.
3
Apply the principle of certainty not overridden by doubt
The general hadiths produce certainty (yaqin) that all urine is najis and must be washed. The specification is a limited exception, established by a specific hadith. For female infant urine, there is no such exception (doubtful), so the general rule remains. Thus, sprinkling is only for the proven exception.
This is a core Hanafi usul maxim: 'Certainty is not removed by doubt.'
4
Examine the role of hadith authentication in the dispute
Note that al-Shafi'i initially did not consider the differentiating hadiths (e.g., hadith of 'Ali and Abu al-Samh) as established (thabita). Once his followers found them authentic, they adopted the distinction. This shows how the strength of riwaya affects the ruling.
Al-Bayhaqi: when the musnad hadiths are combined, they become strong.
5
Assess the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: Hanafis prescribe sprinkling for male infant urine, washing for female; Ibn Hazm requires washing for both; later Shafi'is also differentiate. Understanding this helps appreciate how usul principles produce different rulings.
Also note the precautionary element: al-Shafi'i preferred washing even when he permitted sprinkling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثَّالِث / الاختلاف في السند والمتن
وقد اعترض ابن حزم - القائل: بأن النضح يكفي في التطهير من بول الذكر كبيراً أو صغيراً : بأن تخصيص ذلِكَ بالصبي الَّذِي لَمْ يأكل لَيْسَ من كلام النَّبِيِّ ، لِذلِكَ فالحديث لا دلالة فِيهِ عَلَى هَذَا التحديد.
ويجاب عَلَى ذَلِكَ : بأنه نجاسة الأبوال المستتبعة لوجوب غسلها، كُلّ ذَلِكَ مستيقن بالأحاديث العامة الدالة عَلَى ذَلِكَ، كحديث ابن عَبَّاس في القبرين اللذين أخبر رَسُول الله له أن صاحبيهما يعذبان، وَقَالَ: «أما أحدهما فكان يمشي بالنميمة، وأما الآخر فكان لا يستنزه من البول». أخرجه البُخَارِيّ وَمُسْلِم )
وحديث أبي هُرَيْرَة مرفوعاً: استنزهوا» من البول؛ فإن عامة عذاب القبر منه». رواه أحمد وابن ماجه وابن خزيمة والدارقطني والحاكم وصححه البخاري).
وحديث ابن عباس مرفوعاً: «تَنزهوا من البول، فإن عامة عذاب القبر مِنْهُ». أخرجه البزار والطبراني والدارقطني والحاكم فنجاسة بول الآدمي ووجوب غسله كُلّ ذَلِكَ متيقن بهذه الأحاديث، وتخصيص بول الصبي الَّذِي لَمْ يأكل الطعام بالنضح متيقن بحديث أم قيس بنت محصن، وما عدا ذَلِكَ مشكوك فِيهِ، فَلاَ يترك اليقين للشك.
والاكتفاء بالنضح في التطهير من بول الرضيع خصه أحمد وجمهور بالصبي الَّذِي لَمْ يأكل الطعام، أما بول الصبية فلا يجزئ فيه إلا الغسل.
الشافعية
أما الشَّافِعِي نَفْسه فَقَدْ نَصَّ عَلَى جواز الرش عَلَى بول الصبي مَا لَمْ يأكل الطعام، واستدل عَلَى ذَلِكَ بالحديث ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: «وَلاً يبين لي في بول الصبي والجارية فرق من السُّنَّة الثابتة، وَلَوْ غسل بول الجارية كَانَ أحب إلي احتياطاً، وإن رش عَلَيْهِ مَا لَمْ تأكل الطعام أجزأ، إن شاء الله تَعَالَى».
وَقَدْ ذكر النَّوَوِيِّ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى - أَنَّهُ لَمْ يذكر عن الشَّافِعِي غَيْرِ هَذَا، وَقَالَ البَيْهَقِيّ: والأحاديث المسندة في الفرق بَيْنَ بول الغلام والجارية في هَذَا الباب إذَا ضُمَّ بعضها إلى بَعْض قويت، وكأنها لَمْ تثبت عِنْدَ الشَّافِعِيّ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - حِيْنَ قَالَ: ولا يتبين لي في بول الصبي والجارية فرق من السنة الثابتة). وقول الشَّافِعِيّ هَذَا مروي عن النخعي، وَهُوَ رِوَايَة عن الأوزاعي، ووجه لبعض الشافعية، ووصفه النَّوَوِيّ : بأنه ضَعِيف ) وهنا يأتي دور حَدِيث علي الله ومثله حَدِيث أبي السمح له خادم النبي ، فهي أحاديث ثابتة، وَقَدْ فرقت بَيْنَ بول الصبي وبين بول الصبية. وَقَدْ ثبت هَذَا عِنْدَ أحمد؛ لِذلِكَ أخذ بِهِ وفرق بَيْنَهُمَا في الحكم، أما الشَّافِعِي فَقَدْ صرح بأنه لم يثبت عنده من السُّنَّة ما يفرق بَيْنَهُمَا ؛ لِذلِكَ رأى أن النضح يكفي فِيْهِمَا – وإن كَانَ الأحب إليه غسل بول الصبي احتياطاً ؛ وَلَوْ ثبت عِنْدَ الشَّافِعِي هَذِهِ الأحاديث لأخذ بها، فهذا هُوَ شأنه وشأن الفُقَهَاء كافة لا يتخطون السنة الثابتة عندهم إلى غيرها، مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهَا عندهم معارض؛ ولذلك أطبق أصحاب الشَّافِعِي عَلَى الفرق في الحكم بين بول الصبي والصبية لما ثبتت عندهم هذه الأحاديث).
Chapter Three: Difference in Chain and Text. And Ibn Hazm objected - he who says that sprinkling suffices for purification from the urine of a male, whether adult or child: by specifying that with the boy who has not eaten food is not from the speech of the Prophet, therefore the hadith has no indication of this specification. And the response to that: that it is the impurity of urine that necessitates washing it; all that is established by the general hadiths indicating that, like the hadith of Ibn Abbas about the two graves that the Messenger of Allah informed that their occupants are being punished, and he said: 'As for one, he used to walk with gossip, and as for the other, he did not avoid urine.' Narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. And the hadith of Abu Hurairah marfu': 'Avoid urine, for most of the punishment of the grave is from it.' Narrated by Ahmad, Ibn Majah, Ibn Khuzaymah, al-Daraqutni, and al-Hakim, and al-Bukhari authenticated it. And the hadith of Ibn Abbas marfu': 'Avoid urine, for most of the punishment of the grave is from it.' Narrated by al-Bazzar, al-Tabarani, al-Daraqutni, and al-Hakim. So the impurity of human urine and the obligation of washing it are all established by these hadiths, and the specification of the urine of the boy who has not eaten food by sprinkling is established by the hadith of Umm Qays bint Mihsan, and beyond that is doubtful, so certainty is not left for doubt. And sufficiency of sprinkling in purification from the urine of an infant was specified by Ahmad and the majority to the boy who has not eaten food; as for the female infant's urine, washing alone suffices. The Shafi'is: As for al-Shafi'i himself, he ruled on the permissibility of sprinkling for the urine of a boy who has not eaten food, and he argued for that with the hadith, then he said: 'It is not clear to me from the established sunnah a difference between the urine of a boy and a girl, and if I were to wash the urine of a girl, it would be more beloved to me as a precaution, and if one sprinkles on it while she has not eaten food, it suffices, Allah willing.' And al-Nawawi mentioned that nothing else is reported from al-Shafi'i, and al-Bayhaqi said: The musnad hadiths differentiating between the urine of a male infant and a female infant, when one is added to another, become strong; and it is as if they were not established with al-Shafi'i when he said: 'It is not clear to me from the established sunnah a difference between the urine of a boy and a girl.' And this saying of al-Shafi'i is narrated from al-Nakha'i, and it is a narration from al-Awza'i, and a position of some Shafi'is, and al-Nawawi described it as weak. And here comes the role of the hadith of 'Ali and the hadith of Abu al-Samh, the servant of the Prophet; these are established hadiths, and they differentiated between the urine of a boy and a girl. And this was established with Ahmad; therefore he adopted it and differentiated between them in the ruling. As for al-Shafi'i, he stated that it was not established with him from the sunnah what differentiates between them; therefore he saw that sprinkling suffices for both – although washing the urine of a boy would be more beloved to him as a precaution; and if these hadiths had been established with al-Shafi'i, he would have adopted them. This is his way and the way of all jurists: they do not go beyond the established sunnah with them to other things, as long as there is no conflicting evidence with them. Therefore, the Shafi'i followers agreed on the differentiation in ruling between the urine of a boy and a girl once these hadiths became established with them.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute in the Hanafi context regarding purification from urine, specifically whether sprinkling (nadh) suffices for male infant urine or only washing (ghusl). The author begins by reporting Ibn Hazm's objection: that the specification of the ruling to a boy who has not eaten food is not from the Prophet's own words, so the hadith does not indicate such a specification. The response is that general hadiths establish the impurity of all human urine and the necessity of washing it. The exception for male infant urine is specifically proven by the hadith of Umm Qays, so that exception is certain, while anything beyond that (like female infant urine) is doubtful. Thus, certainty is not abandoned for doubt. Ahmad ibn Hanbal and the majority restrict sprinkling to the male infant who has not eaten food; female infant urine requires washing. Then the passage turns to al-Shafi'i's position: he permitted sprinkling for the male infant based on the hadith, but he saw no established sunnah difference between male and female infants. Thus, he considered sprinkling sufficient for both, though washing was preferable for precaution. Later, when hadiths differentiating between the genders became established among his followers, they adopted the distinction. This illustrates how the strength and confirmation of hadith evidence determine the ruling.

Key Terms
النضح (al-nadh): Sprinkling water on the impurity without flowing, sufficient only for certain impurities
الغسل (al-ghusl): Washing with water flowing over the impurity
اليقين (al-yaqin): Certainty, established by clear evidence
الشك (al-shakk): Doubt, uncertainty about a legal ruling or evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position as presented, what is the ruling for purifying from the urine of a female infant who has not eaten food?
A) Sprinkling suffices just like for a male infant
B) Washing is required
C) Neither sprinkling nor washing is required
D) It is impure only if she has eaten food

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the general rule (impurity of all urine) remains binding unless a specific exception is proven with certainty; doubt does not expand the exception.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
The Principle of Generality and the Junub Reciting Quran
Usul dispute on junub reciting Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that al-'amm is qat'i until takhsis to evaluate the argument that a junub may recite Quran based on the hadith 'he used to remember Allah in all his states'.

Core Idea
The Quran is dhikr, and the Prophet's general practice of dhikr in all states includes recitation — specification requires proof.

This lesson examines a classic usul dispute: does the general permission of dhikr in the Prophet's hadith include Quran recitation for a junub? The second opinion argues yes, citing the principle of generality (al-'umum), while opponents seek to restrict the term 'dhikr' to non-Quranic remembrance. You will analyze the istidlal chains and understand how the Hanafi school applies the maxim 'al-amm yufidu al-wujub' to textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
What is the legal question? Is a person in major impurity (junub) allowed to recite Quran? Note that the passage presents multiple opinions.
The first opinion (not fully detailed) prohibits it based on a weak hadith; the second permits it using a strong hadith.
2
Analyze the second opinion's primary dalil
Locate the hadith: 'كَانَ يذكر الله عَلَى كُلِّ أحيانه'. Recognize its authenticity (Muslim). Note the claim: 'القرآن ذكر'.
The hadith is general (ʿāmm) in wording — 'every state' includes janabah.
3
Apply the usul principle of ʿumūm
According to Hanafi usul, the general term (al-ʿāmm) is decisive (qaṭʿī) until a specific exclusion (takhṣīṣ) is proven. The opponents' claim that 'dhikr' here customarily excludes Quran is challenged as lacking legal evidence (lā dalīl ʿalayhi).
Al-Qurṭubī's comment distinguishes customary (ʿurfī) specification from legal (sharʿī) specification.
4
Examine the counter-response
The first opinion's response is that 'dhikr' when unrestricted is understood as other than Quran. The second opinion refutes this: such a restriction would be a takhṣīṣ without proof, violating the principle of ʿumūm.
This illustrates the tension between linguistic custom (ʿurf) and the default legal rule of generality.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence? If the second opinion is adopted, a junub may recite Quran freely. If the first, he must refrain. Note also the third opinion (limited recitation) and Malik's distinction.
The passage does not settle; it is an exposure of ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث الاختلاف في السند والمتن
وَهُوَ حَدِيث ضَعِيف لضعف إسناده فَهُوَ من رِوَايَة إِسْمَاعِيْل بن عياش، عن موسى بن عُقْبَة، عن نافع عن ابن عُمَر. وإسماعيل بن عياش منكر الحديث عن أهل الحجاز وأهل العراق، وحديثه هَذَا عن أهل الحجاز؛ لأن موسى بن عقبة مدني
القول الثاني: يجوز للجنب قراءة القُرْآن وهذا القَوْل مروي عن ابن عَبَّاس، وسعيد بن المسيب، وعكرمة، وربيعة الرأي، وسعيد بن جبير، وَهُوَ قَوْل ابن حزم الظاهري ونقله عن دَاوُد وعامة أصحابهم واختاره ابن المنذر. والحجة لهذا المذهب:
مَا صَحَّ أَنَّهُ عليه الصَّلاة والسلام: «كَانَ يذكر الله عَلَى كُلِّ أحيانه». أخرجه مسلم، وغيره.
قالوا: والقُرْآن ذكر.
قَالَ أبو بَكْر بن المنذر: «فَقَالَ بعضهم: الذكر قَدْ يَكُون بقراءةِ القُرْآن وغيره، فكلُّ ما وقع عَلَيْهِ اسم ذكر الله فغير جائز أن يمنع مِنْهُ أحد، إذا كَانَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يمتنع من ذكر الله عَلَى أحيانه».
وَأجاب أصحاب المذهب الأول عن هَذَا: بأن المراد من الذكر غَيْر القُرْآن فَهُوَ المفهوم عند الإطلاق.
ويجاب عن هَذَا: بأن التخصيص لا دليل عَلَيْهِ، فالأصل العموم حَتَّى يأتي دليل يخصصه. ولذا قال القرطبي: أصل الذكر التنبه بالقلب للمذكور والتيقظ لَهُ، الذكر باللسان ذكراً لأَنَّهُ دلالة عَلَى الذكر القلبي؛ غَيْر أَنَّهُ لما كثر إطلاق الذكر عَلَى القَوْل اللساني صار هُوَ السابق للفهم. فالتخصيص عرفي لا شرعي.
وقالوا أيضاً: لَمْ يصح دليل في منع المحدث حدثاً أكبر من قراءة القُرْآن، والأصل عدم التحريم. وَقَد خالف هذين المذهبين جَمَاعَة من الفُقَهَاء ففرقوا بَيْنَ القليل والكثير، وقالوا: تجوز قراءة الآية والآيتين. روي ذَلِكَ عن عَبْد الله بن مغفل، ومحمد الباقر، ورواية عن عكرمة، وسعيد بن جبير وَقَدْ شدد ابن حزم النكير عَلَى هَذَا القَوْل وعدَّها أقوالاً فاسدة لا يعضدها دليل من قرآن أو سنة صَحِيحَة ولا سقيمة، ولا من إجماع، وَلاً من قَوْل صاحب، وَلاً من قياس، وَلاً من رأي سديد؛ لأن بغض الآية والآية قرآن بلا شك، ولا فرق بَيْنَ أن يباح لَهُ آية أو أن يباح لَهُ أخرى أو بَيْنَ أن يمنع من آية أو يمنع من أخرى. ومما تنبغي الإشارة إليهِ مَذْهَب الإمام مَالِكَ، وَهُوَ أَنَّهُ أَجاز قِرَاءة القُرْآن للحائض والنفساء دُونَ الجنب.
والحجة للإمام مالك في تفريقه بَيْنَ الجنب، وبين الحائض والنفساء: أن الحيض
Chapter Three: Disagreement in Sanad and Matn. And it is a weak hadith due to the weakness of its chain, for it is from the narration of Isma'il ibn 'Ayyash, from Musa ibn 'Uqbah, from Nafi', from Ibn 'Umar. Isma'il ibn 'Ayyash is a denier of hadith from the people of Hijaz and Iraq, and his hadith here is from the people of Hijaz because Musa ibn 'Uqbah is from Madinah. The second opinion: it is permissible for a person in major impurity (junub) to recite the Quran, and this opinion is narrated from Ibn 'Abbas, Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, 'Ikrimah, Rabi'ah al-Ra'y, Sa'id ibn Jubayr, and it is the opinion of Ibn Hazm al-Zahiri, and he transmitted it from Dawud and his general followers, and Ibn al-Mundhir chose it. The evidence for this school: What is authentically reported that he, peace be upon him, 'used to remember Allah in all his states' – reported by Muslim and others. They said: The Quran is remembrance. Abu Bakr ibn al-Mundhir said: Some said: Remembrance may be by recitation of the Quran and other than it, so everything to which the name of remembrance of Allah applies is not permissible to prevent anyone from it, since the Prophet, peace be upon him, did not refrain from the remembrance of Allah in his states. The proponents of the first opinion responded to this: that the intended meaning of remembrance is other than the Quran, as that is the understood meaning when the term is unrestricted. And it is responded to this: that specification has no evidence, and the principle is generality until evidence comes to specify it. Hence al-Qurtubi said: The origin of remembrance is attention of the heart to the remembered and alertness to it; remembrance by the tongue is remembrance because it indicates the heart's remembrance, but due to the frequent use of the term 'remembrance' for verbal speech, it became the first to come to mind. So the specification is customary, not legal. They also said: No evidence has been established to prevent a person with major impurity from reciting the Quran, and the origin is non-prohibition. And a group of jurists differed from these two opinions, distinguishing between a little and a lot, and they said: It is permissible to recite one or two verses. That is narrated from 'Abdullah ibn Mughaffal, Muhammad al-Baqir, and a narration from 'Ikrimah and Sa'id ibn Jubayr. And Ibn Hazm severely criticized this opinion and considered it corrupt opinions that are not supported by any evidence from the Quran or authentic or weak Sunnah, nor from consensus, nor from a Companion's statement, nor from analogy, nor from sound opinion, because a part of a verse and a verse are undoubtedly Quran, and there is no difference between permitting one verse and another, or between prohibiting one verse and another. And among what should be pointed out is the school of Imam Malik, which is that he permitted recitation of the Quran for the menstruating woman (ha'id) and the postpartum woman (nufasa') but not for the junub. The evidence for Imam Malik's distinction between the junub and the menstruating/postpartum woman is that menstruation [the text cuts off]
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage presents the second opinion in a dispute over whether a person in a state of major impurity (janabah) may recite the Quran. The author first notes a weak hadith that prohibits it, then introduces the second opinion that permits it, attributed to several early authorities and to Ibn Hazm. The evidence is the hadith that the Prophet used to remember Allah in all his states, which they argue includes reciting the Quran since it is remembrance. A counter-argument from the first opinion claims that 'remembrance' here does not include Quranic recitation, but the second opinion responds that such a specification is not supported by evidence; the general principle of al-'umum (generality) applies. Al-Qurtubi's analysis explains that the customary use of 'remembrance' for verbal speech does not legally restrict it. Additionally, the text mentions a third opinion that distinguishes between reciting a little or a lot, which Ibn Hazm rejects as illogical. Finally, it notes Imam Malik's view that distinguishes between the junub and the menstruating woman, but the passage cuts off before completing the evidence.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring a full bath (ghusl), typically due to sexual intercourse or seminal emission.
ذكر (dhikr): Remembrance of Allah, which by custom may mean verbal invocation but the text argues the legal meaning includes all forms, including Quran.
عموم (umum): Generality; the principle that a general term applies to all individuals until a specific exception is proven.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the fundamental usul principle used by the second opinion to argue that a junub may recite Quran?
A) Al-ḥarām yuqaddamu ʿalā al-ḥalāl
B) Al-ʿāmm yufidu al-ʿumūm ḥattā yarida al-takhṣīṣ
C) Al-amr yufidu al-wujūb
D) Al-muṭlaq yuḥmalu ʿalā al-muqayyad

Key Takeaway
A general text (ʿāmm) in the Sunnah holds independent legal authority; any attempted restriction (takhṣīṣ) must be supported by explicit evidence, not mere customary usage.
